Miracles

Miracles as Divine Testimony
Baqillani explains how miracles establish truthfulness and transmit proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles function as divine testimony for a prophet's truthfulness and how that testimony extends to the prophet's reports about others.

Core Idea
Miracles are God's testimony confirming a prophet's truthfulness.

Baqillani explains that a miracle is not just a wonder but a divine endorsement. When a miracle appears at the hand of someone claiming prophethood, it serves as God's witness to that claim. Moreover, this testimony extends to the prophet's reports about others, forming a chain of credibility. This passage lays the foundation for understanding how prophetic knowledge is transmitted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation to grasp the logical flow. Notice the key terms: المعجزة (miracle), الصدق (truthfulness), الشهادة (testimony).
2
Identify the two inferences
Baqillani makes two related points: (1) the miracle itself proves the prophet's truthfulness, (2) that truthfulness then validates the prophet's reports about others' honesty. Trace how the first inference leads to the second.
3
Reflect on the concept of testimony
Think about how a testimony works in a court: it vouches for someone. Here, the miracle is God's testimony. How does that affect the reliability of the prophet's statements?
The miracle is not just a sign; it carries legal-like weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يُسْتَدَلُ بالمعجزة على صدق من ظهرت على يده لأنها تجرى مجرى الشهادة له، ويُستدل على صدق المُخبر الذي أخبر عنه النبي صلى الله عليه أنه لا يكذب وكذلك يستدل بخبر من صاحب المعجزة على صدق من أخبر عنه أنه لا يكذب
And one may infer by the miracle the truthfulness of the one on whose hand it appears, because it runs the course of testimony for him. And one infers the truthfulness of the informant whom the Prophet, peace be upon him, informed about that he does not lie. Likewise, one infers by the report of the miracle-performing person the truthfulness of the one about whom he reported that he does not lie.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents the miracle as a proof of prophetic truthfulness. A miracle functions as a testimony from God confirming the prophet's claim. Furthermore, if the prophet reports that someone else (like a companion) does not lie, that report is also validated by the miracle. Similarly, if the miracle-performing person (the prophet) reports about another person's truthfulness, that report is accepted. Thus, the chain of credibility extends through the miracle.

Key Terms
المعجزة
الصدق
الشهادة
المخبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles only prove the prophet's power or knowledge, not necessarily his truthfulness.
Correction: Baqillani explicitly says the miracle runs the course of testimony (شهادة) for the prophet, meaning it is a direct proof of his truthfulness (صدق), not merely a display of power.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani describe the function of a miracle in relation to a prophet?
A) It is a direct proof of God's existence
B) It serves as testimony for his truthfulness
C) It proves his knowledge of the unseen
D) It establishes his superiority over other humans

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divine testimony for a prophet, and that testimony extends to validate the prophet's reports about others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The miracle of the Quran is before you every day. If you truly accepted it as divine testimony, would your certainty in every report of the Prophet—about the grave, the scales, the bridge—be as firm as your certainty in his own truthfulness? Where is the gap between your intellectual acceptance and your lived conviction? What one habit can you start today to close that gap?
?
When you hear the Prophet's report about a matter that benefits you personally—like a reward for a good deed—you want to believe it. But what about his reports that demand something difficult from you? Do you treat those reports with the same trust, as if you heard them from God Himself? If not, what does that say about your heart's true testimony?

God Can Break Custom: The Miracle of Multiplication
Baqillani responds to the custom-based objection and clarifies the meaning of making little much.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the objection that miracles are impossible by appealing to God's power to break custom, and what the true meaning of multiplying food is.

Core Idea
Miracles are not impossible; God can break custom for wise purposes.

In this passage, Baqillani continues his defense of miracles. He addresses the claim that miracles are impossible in custom, and then clarifies a specific miracle: the multiplication of food. He explains that it is not a change in the food's substance but God's creation of additional food.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Baqillani structures his response to the objection.
The Arabic ends mid-sentence due to the page break; the translation covers what is present.
2
Understand the objection and refutation
Identify the objection: that miracles are impossible in custom. Baqillani refutes it by asking why God cannot break custom for a wise purpose, just as He uses human reason as proof.
The refutation is logical: if God can argue through intellects, He can also break customs.
3
Clarify the miracle of multiplication
Baqillani explains that making little much does not mean literal transformation. Instead, God creates additional food at the prophet's supplication and touch.
This clarifies the mechanism: creation ex nihilo, not alteration.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this argument supports the possibility of miracles and prophethood. Why is it important to distinguish between custom and impossibility?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالوا : عنينا أن هذه الأمور مستحيلة في العادة، قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن ينقض الله سبحانه العادات ويُظهر المعجزات على أيدي رسله لما أراده من حسن النظر لهم ولمن عَلم أنه يؤمن بهم ويعمل من العبادات ما يكون وصلة وذريعة إلى إجزال ثوابهم كما جاز وحسن منه أن يحتج عليهم بعقولهم؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك من حيث اعتلوا متعلقاً . صحيح فأما ما قالوه من استحالة كون الكثير قليلاً والقليل كثيراً فإنّه على ما ادعوه وإنما معنى قول المسلمين وكلّ ذي ملة إن الرسول عليه السلام يجعل القليل من الطعام والشراب كثيراً هو أن الله سبحانه يخلق عند دعاء النبي صلى الله عليه ووضعه يده في الطعام والشراب أمثال
And if they say: We meant that these matters are impossible in custom, it is said to them: Then why do you deny that God may break customs and manifest miracles at the hands of His messengers for the sake of what He desired of fair consideration for them and for those whom He knows will believe in them and perform acts of worship that are a means and a path to multiplying their reward, just as it is permissible and good for Him to argue against them through their intellects? So they have no way to refute that from the basis of their argument. Correct. As for what they said about the impossibility of the much becoming little and the little becoming much, it is as they claimed. Rather, the meaning of the Muslims and every religious community that the prophet makes the little food and drink much is that God creates similar amounts at the prophet's supplication and his placing his hand in the food and drink.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage continues the response to the deniers. If they insist that miracles are impossible only in custom, Baqillani argues that God can break customs for wise purposes, just as He uses human reason as proof. The deniers' objection is thereby refuted. Then he clarifies a specific claim about making little much: it is not a literal transformation but God creating additional food ex nihilo at the prophet's hand.

Key Terms
خرق العادة
معجزات
قليل
كثير
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People might think that the miracle of multiplying food involves the food itself expanding or changing in volume.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that it is God's creation of additional food at the prophet's hand, not a transformation of the existing food.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the meaning of the prophet making little food into much?
A) The food itself expands in volume
B) God creates additional food at the prophet's hand
C) It is a metaphorical saying
D) It is impossible

Key Takeaway
Miracles are not limited by custom; Allah can create extra food at the prophet's hand, which is the true meaning of multiplication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if God is bound by the 'customs' of your life—your routines, your expectations, your perceived limitations? Where have you ruled out the possibility of divine intervention because it seems 'impossible' in your experience? Will you actively ask God to break those patterns for His wise purposes, even if it makes you uncomfortable?
?
The prophet’s role was to be a conduit for God’s creation of food. Are you willing to be a vessel through which God provides for others, even if you feel you have little to offer? What 'little' thing in your life—time, money, skill—can you place in God's hands today, trusting Him to create abundance through your act of giving?
?
Baqillani teaches that miracles are not impossible, but they are not natural transformations either. Have you been dismissing the extraordinary acts of God in your life as mere coincidences or natural processes? Commit to recording one moment this week where you recognized God's direct intervention, outside of your usual explanations.

Refuting the 'Never Seen' Argument
Baqillani refutes the objection using an analogy with ordinary causation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses an analogy from ordinary causation to refute the claim that miracles are impossible because they have never been witnessed.

Core Idea
Unprecedented does not mean impossible — ordinary things are also unprecedented when first created.

The objectors claim that miracles are impossible because no one has ever seen them happen. Baqillani responds by drawing attention to the fact that many ordinary things, like the creation of a human from a drop, are never witnessed in their creation either, yet they exist. He uses this analogy to expose the flaw in their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objectors say: we never saw a miracle, so it cannot be. Read the first part of the passage carefully to see how Baqillani presents this objection.
2
Understand Baqillani's analogy
He points out that the creation of bodies, eggs from chickens, etc., are also never witnessed. Notice how he lists examples of ordinary causation that are never observed in their initial act of creation.
The analogy shows that lack of precedent does not prove impossibility.
3
Follow the logical consequence
If they accept their own reasoning, they must deny ordinary creation, which leads to materialism. If they refuse, they contradict themselves. Reflect on the dilemma Baqillani presents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصانع ألحدوا وتركوا دينهم، وقيل لهم: ما الدليل على إحالة ذلك؟ وإن قالوا لأننا لم نجد أحداً فعله ولا يقدر عليه ولا رأينا ذلك قط ولا جرى مثل ما تدعون، قيل لهم: فيجب أن تحيلوا أيضاً أن يخلق الله تعالى الأجسام ولا يوجد آدم إلا من ذكر وأنثى ولا يخلق دجاجة إلا من بيضة أو بيضة إلا من دجاجة أو نطفة إلا من إنسان أو إنساناً إلا من نطفة لأن ذلك أجمع لم يوجد قط ولم يشاهد فإن مروا على ذلك لحقوا بأهل الدهر وإن أبوه نقضوا اعتلالهم. وإن قالوا: عنينا أن هذه الأمور مستحيلة في العادة، قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم أن ينقض الله سبحانه العادات ويُظهر المعجزات على أيدي رسله لما أراده من حسن النظر لهم ولمن علم أنه يؤمن بهم ويعمل من العبادات ما يكون وصلة وذريعة إلى إجزال ثوابهم كما جاز وحسن منه أن يحتج عليهم بعقولهم؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك من حيث اعتلوا متعلقاً. صحيح
The Creator they deviated and left their religion, and it was said to them: What is the evidence for the impossibility of that? And if they say: Because we have not found anyone doing it and he is not capable of it, and we have never seen that and nothing like what you claim has occurred, it is said to them: Then you must also deem impossible that Allah Almighty creates bodies and that Adam exists only from male and female, and that a chicken is created only from an egg or an egg only from a chicken, or a drop only from a human or a human only from a drop, because all of that has never existed nor been witnessed. For if they pass over that, they join the materialists; and if they refuse, they refute their own reasoning. And if they say: We meant that these matters are impossible by custom, it is said to them: Then what prevents you from Allah Almighty breaking the customs and manifesting miracles at the hands of His messengers, for the good consideration He desired for them and for those He knew would believe in them and perform acts of worship that would be a means and a cause for increasing their reward, just as it is permissible and good for Him to argue with them through their intellects? Then they will find no way to repel that from the standpoint of their argument. Correct.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection against miracles. Baqillani presents an objection and then answers it in two stages. First, the objectors say miracles are impossible because they have never seen them happen. Baqillani retorts by analogy: if that were valid, they would also have to deny ordinary causation—like humans being born only from parents, or chickens from eggs—since these are never observed in a different manner. If they accept that, they become materialists denying creation; if they reject it, they contradict themselves. Second, the objectors clarify that they mean customary impossibility. Baqillani then argues that God can break customs and perform miracles for His prophets as a sign, and this is as reasonable as God using people's intellects to guide them. The passage ends with 'Correct', affirming the refutation.

Key Terms
معجزة
عادة
نقض العادة
استحالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What analogy does Baqillani use to refute the claim that miracles are impossible because never seen?
A) Miracles are like natural disasters.
B) Ordinary creations like humans from parents are also never seen in their origination.
C) The objectors themselves perform miracles.
D) Prophets have seen miracles before.

Key Takeaway
Lack of precedent does not prove impossibility, as many existing things are never witnessed in their creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a possibility in your life simply because you never saw it happen before? Where might you be limiting God's power by your own lack of experience? Will you actively fight that mindset this week?
?
The materialist trusts only what is observed. In what area of your faith have you allowed the 'never seen' argument to weaken your certainty—prayer, miracles, the unseen? Which belief will you now hold with more conviction because of this lesson?
?
Baqillani forces a dilemma: either accept materialism or affirm the possibility of miracles. Are there moments in your daily life where you live as though God cannot intervene because you haven't seen it? What would change if you lived as though miracles are always possible?

The Possibility of Custom-Breaking
Baqillani refutes the claim that customary impossibility prevents miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why customary impossibility does not rule out miracles, and how Baqillani argues that God can break customs for prophetic signs.

Core Idea
Customs are not laws; God can break them for a wise purpose.

The objectors refine their position, saying that miracles are impossible by custom, not by reason. Baqillani seizes this distinction: if it is only custom, then God, who established custom, can also break it. He explains that breaking custom serves a good purpose—to confirm prophets and reward believers—just as God uses intellect to guide people.

Guided Path
1
Understand the refined objection
The objectors clarify they mean 'customarily impossible', not absolutely impossible. Read the passage to see how Baqillani quotes them.
2
Grasp the concept of 'nagd al-'ada'
Baqillani argues that God can break customs (nagd al-'ada) and manifest miracles. Understand that custom is not a binding law but a usual pattern.
3
See the purpose behind miracles
The breaking of custom is for good purposes: to guide people and increase reward for believers. Notice how Baqillani links miracles to divine wisdom.
4
Recognize the analogy with intellect
God uses both intellect and miracles to argue with people. Just as it is good for God to reason with people through their minds, it is also good to show miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصانع ألحدوا وتركوا دينهم، وقيل لهم: ما الدليل على إحالة ذلك؟ وإن قالوا لأننا لم نجد أحداً فعله ولا يقدر عليه ولا رأينا ذلك قط ولا جرى مثل ما تدعون، قيل لهم: فيجب أن تحيلوا أيضاً أن يخلق الله تعالى الأجسام ولا يوجد آدم إلا من ذكر وأنثى ولا يخلق دجاجة إلا من بيضة أو بيضة إلا من دجاجة أو نطفة إلا من إنسان أو إنساناً إلا من نطفة لأن ذلك أجمع لم يوجد قط ولم يشاهد فإن مروا على ذلك لحقوا بأهل الدهر وإن أبوه نقضوا اعتلالهم. وإن قالوا: عنينا أن هذه الأمور مستحيلة في العادة، قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم أن ينقض الله سبحانه العادات ويُظهر المعجزات على أيدي رسله لما أراده من حسن النظر لهم ولمن علم أنه يؤمن بهم ويعمل من العبادات ما يكون وصلة وذريعة إلى إجزال ثوابهم كما جاز وحسن منه أن يحتج عليهم بعقولهم؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك من حيث اعتلوا متعلقاً. صحيح
The Creator they deviated and left their religion, and it was said to them: What is the evidence for the impossibility of that? And if they say: Because we have not found anyone doing it and he is not capable of it, and we have never seen that and nothing like what you claim has occurred, it is said to them: Then you must also deem impossible that Allah Almighty creates bodies and that Adam exists only from male and female, and that a chicken is created only from an egg or an egg only from a chicken, or a drop only from a human or a human only from a drop, because all of that has never existed nor been witnessed. For if they pass over that, they join the materialists; and if they refuse, they refute their own reasoning. And if they say: We meant that these matters are impossible by custom, it is said to them: Then what prevents you from Allah Almighty breaking the customs and manifesting miracles at the hands of His messengers, for the good consideration He desired for them and for those He knew would believe in them and perform acts of worship that would be a means and a cause for increasing their reward, just as it is permissible and good for Him to argue with them through their intellects? Then they will find no way to repel that from the standpoint of their argument. Correct.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection against miracles. Baqillani presents an objection and then answers it in two stages. First, the objectors say miracles are impossible because they have never seen them happen. Baqillani retorts by analogy: if that were valid, they would also have to deny ordinary causation—like humans being born only from parents, or chickens from eggs—since these are never observed in a different manner. If they accept that, they become materialists denying creation; if they reject it, they contradict themselves. Second, the objectors clarify that they mean customary impossibility. The passage ends with 'Correct', affirming the refutation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that customary impossibility makes something absolutely impossible.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that custom is not a law; God can overrule custom for a wise purpose.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why can God break customs?
A) Because God is arbitrary.
B) For the good of people and to increase reward for believers.
C) Because miracles are not truly impossible.
D) Because custom is not real.

Key Takeaway
Customary impossibility does not prevent God from performing miracles, as custom is not an absolute law and God can break it for wise purposes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation that seems impossible by custom, do you truly believe that God can break that custom for you? What would change in your prayer if you remembered that custom is not law?
?
The passage says God breaks customs for 'good consideration' and to increase reward. Have you ever seen a 'miracle' in your life that you attributed to coincidence rather than to God's direct intervention? How might acknowledging His custom-breaking change your gratitude?
?
If you believe God can break customs, why do you still often rely on natural means alone without turning to Him first? What would it take for you to truly depend on His power beyond the habitual?

Baqillani on the Miracle of Multiplying Food
Baqillani explains the true meaning of the miracle of multiplying food.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's explanation of how the miracle of multiplying food occurs—not through physical expansion but through God's creation of additional food.

Core Idea
The miracle is creation, not transformation.

Baqillani addresses a common objection against miracles: how can little become much? He clarifies that the true understanding is not that each part expands, but that God creates additional food at the Prophet's supplication. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and shows why the objection collapses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Notice the logical structure: an objection followed by a clarification.
The passage is concise; read carefully to follow the argument.
2
Identify the objection
The objectors claim it is impossible for much to become little or little to become much. Recognize that Baqillani agrees with their premise of impossibility, but reinterprets the miracle.
Baqillani is not denying the logical principle; he is redefining the miracle's mechanism.
3
Understand Baqillani's explanation
The miracle is that God creates new food at the Prophet's supplication, not that the existing food expands. Pay attention to the phrase 'خلق أمثال ذلك الطعام والشراب' (creates the likes of that food and drink).
This preserves the logical principle while affirming the miracle.
4
Reflect on the misconception
The common misunderstanding is that the miracle involves physical expansion. Baqillani's explanation shows it is about creation, not transformation. Consider why this distinction matters.
5
Confirm the key takeaway
The key takeaway is that the miracle of multiplying food is an act of creation, not a change in the nature of the original food. This removes the apparent impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما ما قالوه من استحالة كون الكثير قليلاً والقليل كثيراً فإنّه على ما ادعوه وإنما معنى قول المسلمين وكل ذي ملة إن الرسول عليه السلام يجعل القليل من الطعام والشراب كثيراً هو أن الله سبحانه يخلق عند دعاء النبي صلى الله عليه ووضعه يده في الطعام والشراب أمثال ذلك الطعام والشراب ويخترع أضعافه لا أن كل جزء فيه أو أكثر من ذلك لأن الكثير لا يتوجد كما أن الواحد لا يتكثر وكذلك عند دعائه عليه السلام بعض الموجودات ويبقى بعضها وإن كان التأويل فى ذلك على ما وصفنا سقط ما توهموه.
As for what they said about the impossibility of much becoming little and little becoming much—it is as they claimed. But the meaning of the Muslims' statement, and every adherent of a religion, that the Messenger (peace be upon him) makes a little food and drink much, is that Allah Almighty creates, at the Prophet's supplication (peace be upon him) and his placing his hand in the food and drink, the likes of that food and drink, and He invents multiples of it—not that every part of it becomes larger or more than that, because much does not become less just as the one does not become many. Similarly, at his supplication (peace be upon him), some existents are annihilated and others remain. And if the interpretation is as we have described, what they imagined falls away.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of a specific objection regarding the miracle of multiplying food. The objectors argued that it is impossible for a little food to become much, as that would mean much becoming little and vice versa. Baqillani explains that the correct understanding is not that each part expands, but that God creates additional food at the Prophet's prayer. For example, when the Prophet placed his hand in a small amount of food, God created more food alongside it, multiplying it. He also notes that the same principle applies when some existing things are annihilated and others remain. When understood this way, the objection collapses.

Key Terms
استحالة
تأويل
خلق
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the miracle involves a part of food physically expanding or changing in quantity.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that God creates additional food at the Prophet's supplication, not that the existing food becomes more.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani explain the miracle of little food becoming much?
A) The food expands in size.
B) Each part of the food becomes larger.
C) God creates additional food alongside the original.
D) The food loses its density.

Key Takeaway
The miracle of multiplying food is not a physical expansion but God's creation of additional food at the Prophet's supplication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a miracle, do you secretly think it must contradict logic? This lesson says otherwise. Do you trust that God's power works within His own created order, not against it? How does that change the way you approach the miracles mentioned in the Quran or hadith?
?
Baqillani teaches that the miracle is a direct creation of God through the Prophet's supplication. Do you truly believe that your own supplications can be the means for God to create new realities in your life? What is one situation where you have not turned to du'a because you thought it was 'impossible'?
?
The objection in this lesson comes from a logical mind seeking consistency. Are there areas of your faith where you have been tripped up by 'logical' objections, causing doubt? Will you now re-examine them, asking whether the miracle is actually a creation rather than a violation? What is one specific doubt you will take before God today?

Miracles
intermediate
8 min
The Quran's Miracle Known by Necessity
Baqillani proves the Quran's miraculous nature through necessary knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani argues that knowledge of the Quran's miraculous nature is necessary (ḍarūrī) for anyone who hears of its widespread transmission, and why denial would be obstinacy.

Core Idea
The Quran's miracle is known by necessity through unanimous, widespread testimony.

Baqillani begins by listing several miracles of the Prophet, including the Quran, to establish that such acts are beyond human power. Then he anticipates an objection: how can we be sure these miracles actually occurred? His answer introduces two ways of knowing, but the primary focus is on necessary knowledge, which he applies to the Quran. This passage is foundational for understanding how Kalam uses tawatur to ground belief in foundational events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and list the miracles
Read the Arabic passage once. Identify the various miracles mentioned by Baqillani, including the Quran and other signs. Notice that he states they are beyond human capability.
The list serves to establish the category of miracles before focusing on the Quran.
2
Understand the two paths to knowledge
Find where Baqillani presents the two epistemological paths: necessary knowledge (al-iḍṭirār) and theoretical inference (al-naẓar wa al-istidlāl). Note that he will elaborate only on the first for the Quran.
3
Analyze the argument for necessity
Focus on how Baqillani argues that knowledge of the Quran's origin from the Prophet is necessary. He cites universal agreement among all groups, including non-Muslims, and compares it to well-known poetry and sermons.
This is the core of the proof: tawatur leads to necessary knowledge.
4
Apply the principle of obstinacy
Reflect on the analogy: denying the Quran's origin is like denying Imru' al-Qays's poetry—it shows willful ignorance. If denial of less widespread reports is obstinate, denial of the Quran is even more so.
This reinforces that the knowledge is necessary and cannot be rationally denied.

Source Text

كثيرة؛ منها القرآن المرسوم في مصاحفنا الذي أتى به وتحدى العرب بالإتيان بمثله ومنها حنين الجذع وكلام الذئب وجعل قليل الطعام كثيراً وانشقاق القمر وتسبيح الحصى في يده وكلام الذراع له في غير هذه الآيات مما يجري مجراها وقد علم أن مجيء مثلها من الخلق ممتنع متعذر وأنه من مقدورات الخالق سبحانه. فإن قالوا: وما الطريق إلى العلم بصحة هذه الآيات وظهورها على يديه؟ قيل لهم: السبيل إلى ذلك من طريقين: أحدهما الاضطرار والآخر النظر والاستدلال. فأما العلم بظهور القرآن على يده ومجيئه من جهته وأنه تحدى العرب أن يأتوا بمثله فواقع لنا ولكل من خالفنا باضطرار من حيث لا يمكن جحده ولا الارتياب به كما أن العلم بظهور النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بمكة والمدينة ودعوته إلى نفسه واقع من جهة الاضطرار لأن المسلمين واليهود والنصارى والمجوس والصابئة والثنوية والزنادقة وكل منحرف عن الملة يقرون بأن القرآن المتلو في محاريبنا المرسوم في مصاحفنا من قبل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نجم ومن جهته ظهر من غير اختلاف بينهم في ذلك. فلو حمل حامل نفسه على ذلك لجحد الضرورة وسقطت مكالمته كما لو ادعى مدع أن التوراة والإنجيل ليسا من جملة من قبل موسى وعيسى عليهما السلام لكان معانداً وجاحداً للضرورة. بل لو جحد جاحد ما هو دون هذا فزعم أن قفا نبك ليست من شعر امرئ القيس، وأن ودع هريرة إن الركب مرتحل ليس من شعر الأعشى، ونزل إلى جحد خطب الحجاج وزياد من نظم ورسائل ابن المقفع، وإنكار كون الكتاب لسيبويه لوجب عناده وسقط كلامه. وقد علم أن ظهور الخبر بمجيء القرآن من جهة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أعظم وحاله أشهر فوجب أن يكون ما تواتر الخبر عنه هذه السبيل والعلم به اضطراراً لا يمكن جحده ولا الشك فيه.
Many [miracles]; among them the Qur'an inscribed in our copies which he brought and challenged the Arabs to produce something like it, and among them the moaning of the palm-stump, the speech of the wolf, the making of little food plentiful, the splitting of the moon, the glorification of the pebbles in his hand, and the speech of the foreleg to him, besides other signs of this sort. And it is known that the coming of the like of them from creation is impossible and unattainable, and that they are from the capabilities of the Creator, exalted is He. If they say: What is the way to know the authenticity of these signs and their appearance at his hands? It is said to them: The path to that is from two ways: one of them is necessary [knowledge] and the other is reflection and inference. As for the knowledge of the appearance of the Qur'an at his hands and its coming from him, and that he challenged the Arabs to produce its like, it is realized for us and for every opponent of ours by necessity, in a way that cannot be denied nor doubted, just as the knowledge of the appearance of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Mecca and Medina and his call to himself is realized by necessity, because Muslims, Jews, Christians, Magians, Sabians, Dualists, Zindiqs, and every deviant from the religion affirm that the Qur'an recited in our prayer niches, inscribed in our copies, emerged from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and appeared from him without any disagreement among them about that. So if someone were to force himself to that, he would deny necessity and his argument would collapse, just as if someone claimed that the Torah and the Gospel are not from those [books] that came before Moses and Jesus (peace be upon them), he would be obstinate and a denier of necessity. Rather, if someone denied something less than this, claiming that 'Stop, let us weep' is not from the poetry of Imru' al-Qays, and that 'Leave Umm Hurayra, indeed the caravan is departing' is not from the poetry of al-A'sha, and descended to denying the sermons of al-Hajjaj and Ziyad from the compositions and epistles of Ibn al-Muqaffa', and denying that the book belongs to Sibawayh, his obstinacy would be established and his speech would collapse. And it is known that the appearance of the report of the coming of the Qur'an from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is greater and its condition is more famous, so it must be that what has been transmitted by multiple chains about him in this way, and the knowledge of it, is by necessity, which cannot be denied nor doubted.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the authenticity of the Prophet's miracles, specifically the Qur'an, arguing that knowledge of it is necessary (ḍarūrī). Baqillani begins by listing several miracles of the Prophet, including the Qur'an, the moaning of the palm stump, etc., establishing that such acts are beyond human capability and are from God alone. He then anticipates an objection: 'What is the way to know that these miracles actually occurred at his hands?' He answers by stating there are two paths: necessary knowledge (al-iḍṭirār) and theoretical inference (al-naẓar wa al-istidlāl). He then focuses on the Qur'an as the primary example, arguing that knowledge of its divine origin is necessary. This is because everyone—Muslims, Jews, Christians, Magians, etc.—agrees that the Qur'an came from Muhammad (peace be upon him), with no disagreement. Denial of such widespread, unanimous testimony would be like denying the well-known poetry of Imru' al-Qays or the sermons of al-Ḥajjāj—it would be willful obstinacy. The argument uses the principle of tawātur (mass transmission) to establish necessary knowledge. The conclusion is that since the report of the Qur'an's coming from the Prophet is even more widespread and famous than such literary works, knowledge of it is necessary and cannot be denied.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that knowledge of miracles requires theoretical proof for everyone, but Baqillani argues it is necessary for those who have witnessed the widespread transmission.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that for events like the Quran's revelation, the sheer volume and unanimity of transmission confer necessary knowledge, not requiring further inference.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why is knowledge of the Qur'an's divine origin considered necessary (ḍarūrī)?
A) Because the Qur'an is linguistically inimitable.
B) Because all religious groups agree it came from Muhammad, making denial obstinate.
C) Because the Prophet performed it in public repeatedly.
D) Because it is mentioned in previous scriptures.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani establishes that the Quran's miraculous nature is known by necessary knowledge due to its massive widespread transmission, making denial an act of obstinacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You profess belief in the Quran's divine origin, but do you treat it as a necessity—something so undeniable that you live by it without hesitation—or do you secretly harbor doubts? What would change in your life if you truly accepted it as necessary knowledge?
?
When you read the Quran, do you engage with it as a challenge to produce something like it? Have you ever felt the weight of its inimitability to the point where it humbles you? If not, why do you think that is?
?
The passage argues that even non-Muslims agree the Quran came from Muhammad. If your faith is confirmed by the testimony of those who reject it, what does that say about the strength of that testimony? How should this affect your confidence when speaking about Islam to others?

Reasoning Establishes the Prophet's Miracles
Objection and answer on the epistemology of miracles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Baqillani's argument that the Prophet's miracles are known through reasoning and inference, and how the public nature of their transmission yields certainty despite being reported by solitary narrators.

Core Idea
Miracles are known by reasoning, not necessity; public transmission makes them certain.

Imam Baqillani addresses a key epistemological question: How can we be certain of miracles reported by only a few narrators? He distinguishes between necessary knowledge of the Quran and inferential knowledge of miracles, then provides a proof based on the public context of each report. This passage lays out the objection and the author's detailed answer.

Guided Path
1
Understand the knowledge distinction
Read the first sentence: the author states that knowledge of miracles is based on reasoning (nazar wa istidlal), not necessity (idtirar). Why is this distinction important?
Necessary knowledge is immediate and undeniable, like knowing fire burns. Reasoning requires evidence.
2
Identify the objector's challenge
Find the objection: if you admit you are not necessitated, how can you be certain? What is the objector trying to undermine?
3
Follow the author's reply
The author claims we know necessarily that these reports have been continuously transmitted from the earliest times. What does 'we know necessarily' mean here?
This is a meta-claim about the transmission history.
4
Analyze the nature of the reports
Notice that the reports are ahad (solitary) but each one is tied to a specific public event: a witnessed scene, known battle, or gathering. How does this compensate for the lack of tawatur?
The key is the cumulative contextual specificity.
5
Reflect on the example
The author gives an example: 'In such-and-such battle... the arm spoke in the mosque on a known day.' Why does this example clarify the argument?
It shows how a solitary report can be anchored in shared memory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما سبيل العلم بكلام الذراع وتسبيح الحصى وحنين الجذع وجعل قليل الطعام كثيراً وأشباه ذلك من أعلامه عليه السلام فهو نظر واستدلال لا اضطرار. فإن قال قائل : وما الدليل على صحة ظهور هذه الأمور على يده علمكم بخلاف من يخالف فيها وإقراركم بأنكم غير مضطرين إلى العلم بصحتها؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك أنا نعلم ضرورة وجميع أهل الآثار ونقلة الأخبار ومعرفة السير أن هذه الأعلام قد نقلت للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في جميع أعصار المسلمين وأن الأمة لم تَخْلُ قط في زمن الأزمان من ناقلة لهذه الأعلام وما جرى مجراها وأنها قد أذيعت في الصدر الأول ورُويَت من حيث رواتها يسمع من شاهد النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم وعاصره وأن الناقلين لها وإن قَصُرَ عددهم عن عدد أهل التواتر وكانوا آحاداً فإن كل واحد منهم أضاف ما نقله للنبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من هذه الأعلام إلى مشهد مشهود وموقف معروف وغَزاةٍ قد حضَرَ أهلها وبقعةٍ أكثرُ السامعين لخبره قد شهدها ومجتمع قد عرفوه وحضروه فقال : كان في الغزاة الفلانية كذا وكذا وكلم الذراعُ رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم في مسجده يوم مجتمع أصحابه وجعل قليل
As for the way of knowing the speaking of the arm, the praising of pebbles, the moaning of the trunk, the making of little food plentiful, and similar signs of his (peace be upon him), it is [based on] reasoning and inference, not necessity. If someone says: 'What is the evidence for the authenticity of the appearance of these things at his hand, given your knowledge contrary to those who disagree with it, and your admission that you are not necessitated to know their authenticity?' It is said to him: The evidence for that is that we know necessarily, along with all the people of reports, transmitters of news, and those knowledgeable of biographies, that these signs were transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in all eras of Muslims, that the community never ceased at any time to have transmitters of these signs and what is similar, that they were publicized in the early generation and narrated from their narrators who heard from those who witnessed and lived with the Prophet (peace be upon him). And although the number of transmitters of them falls short of the number of those of tawatur and they were individuals, yet each one of them attributed what he transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) of these signs to a witnessed scene, a known location, a battle whose people attended, a place that most hearers of his report witnessed, and a gathering they knew and attended. He said: 'In such-and-such battle, such-and-such happened; the arm spoke to the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) in his mosque on the day of his companions' gathering; and he made little [food] plentiful...'
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer concerning the epistemological status of the Prophet's miracles. The author first distinguishes between two types of knowledge: necessary knowledge (اضطرار) of the Quran, and inferential knowledge (نظر واستدلال) of the miracles. The miracles in question include the speaking of the arm, the praising of pebbles, the moaning of the trunk (the palm tree trunk that wept when the Prophet left it), and the multiplication of food. These are known through reasoning, not immediately. An objector then questions: if you admit you are not necessitated to know these miracles, how can you be certain they occurred, especially when others deny them? The author answers with a detailed proof. He claims we know necessarily—along with all traditionists and historians—that these reports have been continuously transmitted in every generation of Muslims from the earliest times. The reports were publicized from the beginning and narrated by those who directly witnessed the events. The key point is that although the individual chains of transmission are solitary (آحاد) and do not reach the level of tawatur in number, each reporter explicitly links the event to a specific public occasion: a witnessed scene (مشهد مشهود), a known location (موقف معروف), a specific battle (غزاة), a place that most hearers of the report had themselves witnessed, and a gathering (مجتمع) they knew and attended. The author gives an example: 'In such-and-such battle, such-and-such happened; the arm spoke to the Messenger of God in his mosque on the day of his companions' gathering.' This contextual specificity provides cumulative certainty, even though each report is ahad. The argument is that the public nature and multiple independent attestations to the same events make denial unreasonable. The passage is cut off at the end, but the argument is essentially complete: the miracles are established through reasoning from the nature of their transmission.

نظر
استدلال
اضطرار
تواتر
آحاد
أعلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles must be transmitted by tawatur to be accepted as certain.
Correction: The author argues that even ahad reports can yield certainty when they are tied to specific public events witnessed by many, providing cumulative evidence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes the reports of miracles certain despite being transmitted by solitary narrators?
A) The narrators were all trustworthy.
B) The reports are tied to specific public events and places witnessed by many.
C) The Quran confirms them.
D) The reports were written down immediately.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are known through reasoning, and the public nature of their transmission makes solitary reports certain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about the Prophet's miracles like the speaking arm or the multiplication of food, do you truly feel their reality as certain events, or do you treat them as distant stories? The author says they are known through reasoning and public testimony. Have you ever reasoned through the evidence yourself, or have you just accepted them out of habit? What will you do today to strengthen your conviction in these miracles?
?
The objector doubted because the reports are not 'necessary' knowledge. Is there any aspect of the Prophet's miracles that you secretly wonder about? Are you willing to investigate the historical evidence for yourself, or do you prefer to remain in comfortable doubt? What is one step you can take this week to verify the truth of these reports?
?
If these miracles are certain, then every claim the Prophet made is backed by divine testimony. Does your daily life reflect that you are convinced of this? Or do you live as if the Prophet were just a good man with some interesting stories? How will you let that certainty transform your relationship with the Sunnah starting tomorrow?

Miracles

Proof of Miracles Through Tawatur and Customary Impossibility
Baqillani proves miracles via tawatur and impossibility of mass silence on falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the principle of customary impossibility and widespread transmission to prove the authenticity of the Prophet's miracles, even when individual reports do not meet strict tawatur.

Core Idea
Mass silence on a lie proves its falsehood; thus, widespread acceptance without denial confirms truth.

This passage from Baqillani's Tamhid addresses a key objection: how can we be certain about miracles reported by individuals (āḥād)? He argues that the lack of denial by the community, combined with the transmitters' attribution to specific witnessed events, provides a compelling proof. You will see how he builds a case that these miracles are established through a combination of rational deduction and customary knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial claim
Baqillani states that knowledge of certain miracles comes through reflection and deduction, not necessity. This sets up the need for a rational proof.
2
Follow the objection and response
An objector asks for the proof. Baqillani's response introduces the key argument: we know necessarily that these reports have been transmitted across generations without denial.
3
Analyze the transmission details
Note that the transmitters are individuals (āḥād) but each report is tied to a specific witnessed event. The hearers, who were present at those events, did not deny the reports.
4
Grasp the principle of impossibility of silence
Baqillani invokes established custom: it is impossible for a large number of morally upright people to remain silent about a lie attributed to them. This is the core proof.
5
Consider the analogy
He gives an example of someone claiming false miracles today — we would immediately deny it. This illustrates how natural it is to refute lies, so the lack of denial in the past confirms truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما سبيل العلم بكلام الذراع وتسبيح الحصى وحنين الجذع وجعل قليل الطعام كثيراً وأشباه ذلك من أعلامه عليه السلام فهو نظر واستدلال لا اضطرار. مع فإن قال قائل: وما الدليل على صحة ظهور هذه الأمور على يده علمكم بخلاف من يخالف فيها وإقراركم بأنكم غير مضطرين إلى العلم بصحتها؟ قيل له: الدليل على ذلك أنا نعلم ضرورة وجميع أهل الآثار ونقلة الأخبار ومعرفة السير أن هذه الأعلام قد نقلت للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في جميع أعصار المسلمين وأن الأمة لم تخل قط في زمن الأزمان من ناقلة لهذه الأعلام وما جرى مجراها وأنها قد أذيعت في الصدر الأول ورويت من حيث رواتها يسمع من شاهد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعاصره وأن الناقلين لها وإن قصر عددهم عن عدد أهل التواتر وكانوا آحاداً فإن كل واحد منهم أضاف ما نقله للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من هذه الأعلام إلى مشهد مشهود وموقف معروف وغزاة قد حضر أهلها وبقعة أكثر السامعين لخبره قد شهدها ومجتمع قد عرفوه وحضروه فقال: كان في الغزاة الفلانية كذا وكذا وكلم الذراع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في مسجده يوم مجتمع أصحابه وجعل قليل الطعام كثيراً يوم أولم في قصة كذا وكذا وفي بقعة كذا وكذا وعزا كل شيء من ذلك إلى مشهد قد حضره السامعون لنقلهم ومشهد قد شهدوه فلم ينكروا ذلك ولا أحد منهم عليه ولا ردوا نقلهم ولا ظهر منهم تهمة للنقلة ولا شك في أمرهم لا عند سماعهم وطرقه لأسماعهم ولا بعد ذلك. وقد علم بمستقر العادة امتناع إمساك العدد الكثير والجم الغفير عن إنكار كذب يدعى عليهم ويضاف إلى سماعهم ومشاهدتهم وعلمهم نزاهة الأنفس وكبر الهمم وعظم الخطر وجلالة القدر والتدين بتحريم الكذب والنفور عنه والذم له والتبجح بالصدق وشدة تمسكهم به فلو كانوا عالمين بكذب ما ادعاه النقلة عليهم لسارع جميعهم أو الجمهور منهم وقت سماع الكذب عليهم وإضافة ما لا أصل له إليهم وبعد ذلك الوقت إلى إنكاره وتبكيت ناقليه وتكذيبه وذمه وإعلام الناس كذبه كما أنه لو ادعى في وقتنا هذا مدع أن من أعلام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم قلب العصا حية وفلق البحر وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وغير ذلك ليست له لم يلبث أن نسارع إلى تكذيبه ورد قوله وإعلام الناس بطلان ما أتى به ولقلنا له أو أكثرنا: لسنا محتاجين في إثبات نبوة نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى وضع هذا الكذب الذي لا أصل له. وكذلك لو ادعى مدع بحضرة كافة أهل بغداد أو الجانب الشرقي منها من الآيات التي
As for the way of knowing the speech of the arm, the glorification of the pebbles, the moaning of the trunk, making little food plentiful, and similar miracles of his (peace be upon him), it is reflection and deduction, not necessity. Moreover, if someone says: 'What is the proof of the correctness of the appearance of these things at his hand, given your knowledge contrary to those who oppose them and your acknowledgment that you are not compelled to know their correctness?' It is said to him: 'The proof of that is that we know necessarily, along with all people of traditions, transmitters of reports, and knowers of biographies, that these miracles have been transmitted to the Prophet (peace be upon him) in all eras of Muslims, and that the community has never been devoid at any time of transmitters of these miracles and what runs in their course, and that they were widespread in the early period and narrated from those who heard from those who witnessed the Prophet (peace be upon him) and were his contemporaries. And that the transmitters of them, even if their number falls short of the number of people of tawātur and were individuals, yet each one of them attributed what he transmitted of these miracles to a witnessed scene, a known situation, a battle whose people attended, a place that most hearers of his report had witnessed, and a gathering they knew and attended, saying: 'During such-and-such battle there was such-and-such; the arm spoke to the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) in his mosque on the day of his companions' gathering; and he made little food plentiful on the day of his wedding in such-and-such story and in such-and-such place.' And he attributed everything of that to a scene that the hearers of their transmission had attended and a scene they had witnessed; they did not deny that, nor did anyone object to it, nor did they reject their transmission, nor did any suspicion of the transmitters appear from them, nor any doubt about their matter, neither at the time of hearing and its reaching their ears nor after that. And it is known by established custom the impossibility of a large number and a great multitude refraining from denying a lie attributed to them and associated with their hearing and witnessing, given the purity of souls, greatness of aspirations, magnitude of consequence, majesty of status, and religious commitment to prohibiting lying, aversion to it, blame for it, and boasting of truthfulness and strong adherence to it. For if they knew the falsehood of what the transmitters claimed against them, all of them or the majority of them would have hastened, at the time of hearing the lie attributed to them and the addition of what has no basis to them, and after that time, to deny it, rebuke its transmitters, declare it false, blame it, and inform people of its falsehood. Just as if someone in our time claimed that among the miracles of Muhammad (peace be upon him) are the turning of the staff into a snake, splitting the sea, healing the blind and leprous, and other things that are not for him, it would not delay that we would hasten to deny him, reject his statement, inform people of the falsehood of what he brought, and we would say to him or most of us: 'We are not in need, in establishing the prophethood of our Prophet (peace be upon him), of fabricating this lie that has no basis.' And similarly, if someone claimed in the presence of all the people of Baghdad or the eastern side of it, from the verses that...
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the authenticity of the Prophet's miracles. It begins by stating that knowledge of these miracles is acquired through reflection (naẓar) and deduction (istidlāl), not through immediate necessity (ḍarūra). This sets up the problem: if the knowledge is not necessary, how is it certain? An objection is then raised: what is the proof that these miracles indeed occurred, given that you acknowledge you are not compelled to know them? The answer unfolds in several steps. First, the author asserts that we know necessarily (bi-ḍarūra) — along with all traditionists — that these miracles have been transmitted in all Muslim eras, that the community never lacked transmitters of these events, and that they were widespread in the early period, narrated by eyewitnesses (those who saw the Prophet and were his contemporaries). The transmitters, although they may be individuals (āḥād) and not reaching the level of tawātur in number, each one attributed his report to a specific witnessed event (a battle, a location, a gathering) that many of the hearers had themselves witnessed. The hearers did not deny these reports, nor did they object, nor did they show suspicion. Then the argument moves to a general principle: it is known by established custom (mustaqarr al-ʿāda) that a large number of people, given their moral excellence and religious commitment to truth, could not remain silent about a lie falsely attributed to them. If they knew the report was false, they would have hastened to deny it, rebuke the transmitters, and expose the lie. This is illustrated by an analogy: if someone today claimed fabricated miracles for the Prophet (like turning a staff into a snake, splitting the sea, etc.) — which are not from him — we would immediately deny it and say we don't need such lies to prove his prophethood. Similarly, if someone made a false claim in front of all the people of Baghdad (the text ends incompletely), it would be refuted. This is a classic argument from tawātur via the impossibility of mass collusion on falsehood (imtinaʿ al-imsāk ʿan inkār al-kadhib).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Reports transmitted by individuals (āḥād) are inherently weak and cannot establish certainty.
Correction: Baqillani argues that even though the transmitters are individuals, their reports are tied to specific witnessed events that many hearers attended. The lack of denial by those hearers, due to their moral integrity, establishes the truth.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the proof that the miracles of the Prophet (peace be upon him) are authentic despite not being known by necessity?
A) They are known by necessity without any need for evidence.
B) The transmitters were all companions of the Prophet and thus trustworthy.
C) The transmission is linked to specific witnessed events that many hearers attended, and the lack of denial by those hearers proves the truth.
D) The miracles are recorded in the Qur'an so they are automatically accepted.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani proves the authenticity of the Prophet's miracles through the impossibility of mass silence on falsehood, using transmission tied to witnessed events that were never denied.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in the miracles of the Prophet, but have you ever genuinely examined the evidence for them as Baqillani presents it, or do you just take them for granted? What would it mean for your faith if you never truly reflected on their proof?
?
Imagine a lie was told about you in front of a large group who knew the truth. Would you remain silent? If not, how can you explain the silence of the companions who witnessed the Prophet's miracles? Does your own conscience convict you of their truth?
?
Today, when someone in your presence denies or disparages a miracle of the Prophet, do you speak up? Or do you stay silent? What does your silence say about your conviction? Will you resolve to defend the truth even when it is uncomfortable?

The Companions' Silence as Proof of Miracles' Tawatur
Baqillani argues from customary experience that silence implies truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the principle of customary impossibility to argue that the Companions' silence about miracles confirms their tawatur.

Core Idea
If a multitude knows a claim is false, they cannot remain silent – their silence is proof of truth.

Baqillani grounds his argument in human nature: no large group of truthful people would tolerate a false accusation. He applies this to the Companions, arguing that their silence about the miracle reports is itself a powerful testimony. This lesson walks through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read through the Arabic and translation to grasp the overall argument.
2
Identify the key principle
Notice how Baqillani establishes that it is impossible for a large group to remain silent about a known falsehood.
This is based on customary experience (al-ada al-mustaqirra).
3
Apply to the Companions
See how Baqillani concludes that the Companions' silence equals verbal confirmation of the miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطعام كثيراً يوم أولم في قصة كذا وكذا وفي بقعة كذا وكذا وعزوا كل شيء من ذلك إلى مشهد قد حضره السامعون لنقلهم ومشهد قد شهدوه فلم ينكروا ذلك ولا أحد منهم عليه ولا ردوا نقلهم ولا ظهر منهم تهمة للنقلة ولا شك في أمرهم لا عند سماع خبرهم ولا بعد ذلك. وقد علم بمستقر العادة امتناع إمساك العدد الكثير والجم الغفير عن إنكار كذب يدعى عليهم ويضاف إلى سماعهم ومشاهدتهم وعلمهم نزاهة الأنفس وكبر الهمم وعظم الخطر وجلالة القدر والتدين بتحريم الكذب والنفور عنه والذم له والتبجح بالصدق وشدة تمسكهم به فلو كانوا عالمين بكذب ما ادعاه النقلة عليهم لسارع جميعهم أو الجمهور منهم وقت سماع الكذب عليهم وإضافة ما لا أصل له إليهم وبعد ذلك الوقت إلى إنكاره وتبكيت ناقليه وتكذيبه وذمه وإعلام الناس كذبه كما أنه لو ادعى في وقتنا هذا مدع أن من أعلام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم قلب العصا حية وفلق البحر وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وغير ذلك ليست له لم يلبث أن نسارع إلى تكذيبه ورد قوله وإعلام الناس بطلان ما أتى به ولقلنا له أو أكثرنا: لسنا محتاجين في إثبات نبوة نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى وضع هذا الكذب الذي لا أصل له. وكذلك لو ادعى مدع بحضرة كافة أهل بغداد أو الجانب الشرقي منها أو الغربي أو في محلة من محالها أنهم رأوا ما لم يروا وسمعوا ما لم يسمعوا وشهدوا ما لم يعاينوه لم يلبثوا أن يردوا قوله ويشهدوا بكذبه ويعلموا الناس بطلان ما ادعاه عليهم هذا ثابت في مستقر العادة كما أنه ثابت فيه أن اجتماع مثل عدد من ذكرنا على نقل كذب وكتمان ما شوهد ممتنع مع استمرار السلامة في النقل والكتمان من غير ذكر سبب دعاهم إلى ذلك وجمعهم عليه وظهور الحديث به وانطلاق الألسن بذكره ولهج النفوس بحفظه وكما يستحيل في موضوع العادة على نقلة السير والوقائع والبلدان الكذب فيما نقلوه وإذا كان ذلك كذلك دل إمساك الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم عن تكذيب ما نقل من هذه الأعلام وادعي فيه مشاهدتهم وحضورهم وسماعهم على صدق ما أضيف إليهم وادعي عليهم وقام إمساكهم عن إنكار ذلك مقام نقلهم لمثل ما نقله الآحاد وشهادتهم من جهة النطق به وقولهم: قد صدقوا فيما نقلوه وقد شاهدنا منه مثل الذي شاهدوه وهذه دلالة ظاهرة وحجة قاهرة على صحة نقل هذه الأعلام وصدق روايتها وإن قصروا عن التواتر.
The food was abundant on the day of the wedding feast in such and such a story, and in such and such a place, and they attributed each thing from that to a witnessed event that the hearers had attended for their transmission and a scene they had witnessed, and they did not deny that, nor did anyone among them deny it, nor did they reject their transmission, nor did there appear from them any suspicion of the transmitters, nor any doubt in their affair, neither at the hearing of their report nor after that. And it is known by settled custom that it is impossible for a large number and a great multitude to refrain from denying a falsehood claimed against them and attributed to their hearing, their witnessing, and their knowledge, given the purity of souls, greatness of ambitions, magnitude of risk, majesty of status, and religiosity in prohibiting lying, aversion to it, condemnation of it, pride in truthfulness, and their strong adherence to it. For if they had known the falsehood of what the transmitters claimed against them, all of them or the majority of them would have hastened at the time of hearing the falsehood attributed to them and the addition of what has no basis to them, and after that time, to denying it, rebuking its transmitters, declaring it false, condemning it, and informing the people of its falsehood. Just as if someone in our time claimed that among the signs of Muhammad, peace be upon him, are the turning of the staff into a snake, the splitting of the sea, the healing of the blind and leprous, and other things that are not his, he would not delay before we hasten to declare him a liar, reject his statement, inform the people of the invalidity of what he brought, and we would say to him or most of us: 'We are not in need, in establishing the prophethood of our Prophet, peace be upon him, of inventing this falsehood that has no basis.' And likewise, if a claimant claimed in the presence of all the people of Baghdad, or the eastern side thereof, or the western side, or in one of its districts, that they saw what they did not see, heard what they did not hear, witnessed what they did not witness, they would not delay before rejecting his statement, testifying to his falsehood, and informing the people of the invalidity of what he claimed against them. This is established in settled custom, just as it is established therein that the gathering of a number like those we mentioned upon transmitting falsehood and concealing what was witnessed is impossible with the continuation of safety in transmission and concealment without mentioning a reason that called them to that and gathered them upon it, and the appearance of the report thereby, and the tongues being let loose with its mention, and souls being accustomed to its preservation. And just as it is impossible, in the realm of custom, for transmitters of biographies, events, and countries to lie in what they transmit. And if that is so, then the silence of the Companions, may God be pleased with them, regarding the denial of what was transmitted of these signs, in which their witnessing, presence, and hearing was claimed, indicates the truth of what was attributed to them and claimed against them. And their silence regarding the denial of that stands in the place of their transmission of the like of what the single transmitters transmitted and their testimony from the aspect of verbal expression and their saying: 'They have spoken truthfully in what they transmitted, and we have witnessed from it the like of what they witnessed.' And this is a clear indication and a compelling proof of the soundness of the transmission of these signs and the truthfulness of their narrators, even if they fall short of tawatur.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalil) for the tawatur (mass transmission) of the miracles of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), based on the silence of the Companions. Baqillani begins by establishing a general principle from customary experience: if a large group of people is falsely accused of witnessing something they did not see, they would immediately deny it if they knew it was false, due to their natural inclination towards truth and aversion to falsehood. He illustrates this with two hypothetical examples. First, if someone claimed that the food was abundant at a wedding feast and attributed it to witnesses, the witnesses would deny it if false. Second, if a claimant in our time claimed miracles for Muhammad that are not actually his, Muslims would hasten to reject it. Third, if someone claimed in front of all Baghdad that the people saw what they did not see, they would instantly deny it. Baqillani then states that it is impossible, by settled custom, for such a large group to conspire on a lie while staying silent about the truth, especially without any motive. Applying this to the Companions: they remained silent about the transmission of miracles (like the splitting of the moon, etc.) that were attributed to their presence. Their silence, given their known truthfulness and the impossibility of collusion on falsehood, serves as implicit testimony to the truth of those miracles. Baqillani argues that this silence is equivalent to verbal confirmation: 'They have spoken truthfully.' Thus, even if the chains of transmission for these miracles do not reach the level of tawatur in the strict sense, the Companions' silence provides a powerful corroboration.

Key Terms
تواتر
إمساك
صحابة
عادة
معجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Companions' silence might be due to fear or disinterest.
Correction: Baqillani argues that their known character and the impossibility of a multitude remaining silent about a known falsehood rule out such explanations.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why does the Companions' silence about the transmitted miracles indicate their truth?
A) Because the Companions were known to be silent about everything.
B) Because customary experience shows that a large group cannot remain silent about a false claim when they know it is false.
C) Because the Companions were forced to remain silent.
D) Because the miracles are self-evident.

Key Takeaway
The Companions' silence, given their truthfulness, serves as implicit testimony to the authenticity of miracle reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you remained silent about a false claim being made in your presence? What does Baqillani's argument say about your own testimony in that moment, and how will you respond next time?
?
If the Companions' silence was enough to confirm the truth of miracles, what does your silence—or your speech—reveal about what you truly believe? Are there times you've remained silent about truth out of convenience rather than conviction?
?
Baqillani says silence in the face of falsehood is impossible for those who love truth. Examine your own heart: where have you stayed quiet about a falsehood because speaking up was costly? Will you commit today to be one for whom silence is impossible when truth is at stake?

Refuting the Claim that Deniers Accept Events but Deny Miracles
Baqillani refutes the claim that deniers admit events but deny miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that non-Muslim deniers of prophethood do not merely reinterpret miracles as magic but fundamentally deny that the events occurred at all.

Core Idea
Deniers of prophethood do not accept that miracles even occurred.

The objectors try to sidestep the evidence by claiming that non-Muslims do not deny the events but only deny their miraculous nature. Baqillani firmly rejects this, asserting that most of them actually deny the very occurrence. This lesson unpacks that critical response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first refutation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objectors phrase their claim and how Baqillani counters.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ليس الأمر على ما ظننتم' — it signals the refutation.
2
Identify the objectors' claim
The objectors say that non-Muslims admit the events (like the miracles of Moses and Jesus) but deny they were miracles, calling them tricks or magic.
3
Understand Baqillani's counter
Baqillani responds that most (indeed all) of those groups actually deny the events entirely. Even if some concede for argument, they immediately attack as magic.
This is a decisive refutation of the objection.
4
Reflect on the dialectical move
Consider why Baqillani calls their denial 'meaningless'. He shows that the objectors' premise is false, so their conclusion cannot stand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا ليس ينكر أحد من ذكرتم ظهور هذه الأمور على يدي موسى وعيسى وإنما ينكرون كونها معجزاً ويدعون أنها حيل وتخييل ومخاريق فبطل ما قَلَبْتُم به الاعتراض علينا قيل لهم : ليس الأمر على ما ظننتم لأن أكثر من ذكرناه بل الكل منهم يجحد هذه الأمور أصلاً وإن تعاطى المتحذلق منهم أحياناً تسليمه جدلاً والطعن فيه بادعائه أنه من ضروب السحر والحيل وغير ذلك فلا معنى لإنكارهم لذلك . وشيء آخر يبطل ما سألتم عنه وهو أنا لا ننكر تكذب الواحد والاثنين وجحد ما شاهدوه وطيَّه وكتمانه من المسلمين وغيرهم من سائر الملل وإذا كان ذلك كذلك وكنا نعلم أنه لم يحضر مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في هذه المشاهد والغزوات من اليهود والنصارى والمجوس عدد ينقطع بهم العُذر ولا يجوز عليهم الكذب وطي ما شوهد بل لا نعلم أيضاً أنه حضر في أكثرها أحد منهم لما كان من إبعاده إياهم وإخراجهم عن تلك الديار وتحيزهم إلى حيث يمكنهم قتال ونصب راية حرب معه من الحصون
If they say: 'Not one of those you mentioned denies the appearance of these things at the hands of Moses and Jesus; they only deny that they were miracles, and claim that they are tricks, illusions, and sorceries. So your objection against us is invalid.' It is said to them: The matter is not as you think, because most of those we mentioned—rather, all of them—deny these things fundamentally. And even if the clever one among them sometimes concedes it for the sake of argument and then attacks it by claiming that it is a kind of magic, tricks, etc., their denial of it has no meaning. And another thing invalidates what you have asked about: we do not deny that one or two individuals may lie and deny what they witnessed, and conceal it, from Muslims and others of all religions. And if that is so, and we know that there were not present with the Prophet (peace be upon him) in these scenes and battles a number of Jews, Christians, and Magians sufficient to preclude excuse and for whom lying and concealing what was witnessed would be impermissible; rather, we also do not know that any of them were present in most of them, because of his distancing them and expelling them from those lands, and their withdrawal to places where they could fight and raise the banner of war against him from the fortresses.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage contains the second objection and its refutation, followed by an additional argument. The objectors claim that the groups mentioned (Jews, Christians, etc.) do not deny the occurrence of the events at the hands of Moses and Jesus; rather, they deny that these were miracles, alleging them to be tricks or sorcery. Therefore, they argue, the previous refutation fails. Baqillani responds that this is incorrect: most, indeed all, of those groups fundamentally deny the occurrence of these events. Even if some sophisticated individuals occasionally concede them for dialectical purposes and then attack them, their denial is meaningless. Then he adds a further argument: He does not deny that an individual or two may lie and conceal what they witnessed—this happens even among Muslims. But crucially, in the case of the Prophet Muhammad, there were not enough non-Muslims present at the battles and events to form a group whose testimony would be irrefutable (tawātur). In fact, most of these events were not witnessed by any non-Muslims at all, because the Prophet had expelled them from the region, and they were confined to fortresses where they could only engage in war. Thus, their absence invalidates the objection.

Key Terms
المعجز (muʿjiz)
الحيل (ḥiyal)
التخييل (takhīl)
المخاريق (makhārīq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Non-Muslims accept that the events (miracles) occurred but interpret them as magic.
Correction: Baqillani argues they actually deny the events altogether; even if some concede for debate, they attack the miraculous nature.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the real position of most non-Muslims regarding the events of Moses and Jesus?
A) They deny the events entirely.
B) They accept the events but deny miracles.
C) They accept both the events and miracles.
D) They have no opinion.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the objection by asserting that non-Muslims fundamentally deny the occurrence of the events, not just their miraculous nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a truth in Islam that demands change from you, do you ever reduce it to something less—like a mere historical event or a cultural practice—rather than accepting its full miraculous and authoritative nature? What would it cost you to truly embrace it?
?
The clever opponent concedes events but denies their meaning. Is there any area of your life where you 'concede' Islamic teachings outwardly but explain them away inwardly? What would it take for your outward and inward to align in full submission?
?
If someone argues that miracles are just tricks, they deny God's power. But do you, by attributing blessings to your own effort instead of Allah's direct action, deny His signs in your own life? How would your gratitude change if you saw everything as a miracle?

The Argument from Absence of Non-Muslim Witnesses
Baqillani argues that lack of non-Muslim witnesses defeats the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's second response: the lack of reliable non-Muslim witnesses at the Prophet's battles undermines the objectors' argument.

Core Idea
No reliable non-Muslim witnesses were present to contradict the Muslim reports.

Baqillani adds a further point: even if individuals could lie, the crucial fact is that there were not enough non-Muslims present at the Prophet's battles to form a trustworthy group (tawātur). In fact, most events had no non-Muslim witnesses at all. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note how Baqillani concedes that individuals can lie but introduces the concept of tawātur.
Key phrase: 'عدد ينقطع بهم العُذر' — a number that precludes excuse (i.e., tawātur).
2
Understand the role of tawātur
For testimony to be irrefutable, it must come from a group too large to conspire on a lie. Baqillani argues no such group of non-Muslims existed.
Tawātur is a central concept in Islamic epistemology.
3
See why non-Muslims were absent
The Prophet had expelled non-Muslims from the region; they were confined to fortresses and could not witness most events.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Since no reliable non-Muslim witnesses were present, their denial cannot be used to challenge the Muslim reports of miracles.

This passage contains the second objection and its refutation, followed by an additional argument. The objectors claim that the groups mentioned (Jews, Christians, etc.) do not deny the occurrence of the events at the hands of Moses and Jesus; rather, they deny that these were miracles, alleging them to be tricks or sorcery. Therefore, they argue, the previous refutation fails. Baqillani responds that this is incorrect: most, indeed all, of those groups fundamentally deny the occurrence of these events. Even if some sophisticated individuals occasionally concede them for dialectical purposes and then attack them, their denial is meaningless. Then he adds a further argument: He does not deny that an individual or two may lie and conceal what they witnessed—this happens even among Muslims. But crucially, in the case of the Prophet Muhammad, there were not enough non-Muslims present at the battles and events to form a group whose testimony would be irrefutable (tawātur). In fact, most of these events were not witnessed by any non-Muslims at all, because the Prophet had expelled them from the region, and they were confined to fortresses where they could only engage in war. Thus, their absence invalidates the objection.

Key Terms
التواتر (tawātur)
الطعن (ṭaʿn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That any non-Muslim denial disproves the miracle reports.
Correction: Baqillani shows that only a large reliable group (tawātur) could challenge the reports; such a group was absent.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani say the lack of non-Muslim witnesses invalidates the objection?
A) Because non-Muslims are naturally trustworthy.
B) Because a large reliable group is needed to contradict tawātur, and none existed.
C) Because Muslims never lie.
D) Because all non-Muslims were killed in battle.

Key Takeaway
The absence of a reliable non-Muslim witness group at the Prophet's events means their denial cannot counter the Muslim testimony.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on the testimony of the Prophet's companions for your faith. But have you ever considered that the denials of non-Muslims are irrelevant because they were not present? How does this affect your confidence in the prophetic narratives?
?
Baqillani argues that the absence of non-Muslim witnesses invalidates their objection. Ask yourself: Are you ever influenced by the opinions of those who were not present at the events of revelation? How can you shield your faith from such baseless doubts?
?
This lesson shows that the lack of a reliable contradictory witness group strengthens the case for miracles. In your own life, when you face criticism of your beliefs, do you check whether the critics have the proper authority and presence? How can you apply Baqillani's method of evaluating evidence?
