The Twin Proofs: Quranic Inimitability and the Prophet's Unletteredness
Baqillani argues that the Quran's inimitability and the Prophet's lack of learning prove his prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the Arabs' inability to produce a rival to the Quran and the Prophet's known illiteracy as two complementary proofs of prophethood.

Core Idea
The Quran's inimitability and the Prophet's unletteredness are twin proofs of his prophethood.

Baqillani constructs a powerful argument from the historical experience of the Quraysh. Knowing that the Arabs were masters of language and would have done anything to discredit the Prophet, he shows that their silence in the face of the Quran's challenge, combined with the Prophet's known lack of instruction, leaves no explanation except divine origin. This passage unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Let the flow of Baqillani's argument come through.
Notice how the passage moves from context to challenges to conclusion.
2
Identify the two proofs
Find where Baqillani presents the two challenges given by the Prophet and where he brings up the Prophet's unletteredness. These are the two pillars.
3
Understand the Arab context
Baqillani describes the Arabs' pride, zeal, and willingness to suffer war and exile to oppose the Prophet. This sets up why their failure to produce a rival is so significant.
4
Examine the unletteredness argument
The passage notes the Quranic verse about the Prophet not reading or writing, and emphasizes that the Arabs knew his background. If he had studied with scholars, they would have dismissed him.
This eliminates the possibility of human learning.
5
Reflect on the combined proof
Ask yourself why the combination of these two facts is presented as a 'great sign' and 'custom-breaking matter.' How does it strengthen the overall proof?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه من عزة الأنفس أن اللسان الذي نزل به لسانهم ومع العلم بما هم وعظم الأنفة وشدة الحمية والحرص على تكذيبه وتشتيت جمعه وتفريق الناس من حوله والتوفر على إكذابه وما عره وغض منه وخروجهم إلى ما خرجوا إليه معه من الحرب والمسايفة وحمل الأنفس على إراقة الدماء والخروج عن الديار ومفارقة الأوطان. فلو كانوا مع ذلك قادرين على معارضته أو معارضة سورة منه لسارعوا إلى ذلك، ولكان أهون عليهم وأخف من نصب الحرب معه والجلاء عن الأوطان وتحمل الأهوال والصبر على القتل وألم الجراح واحتمال الذل والعار؛ لأنه قد كان عليه السلام مكنهم من تكذيبه من وجهين: أحدهما قوله: "لن تأتوا بمثله"، والآخر قوله: "إن أتيتم فلجتم وكنت مبطلاً وكنتم المحقين"، هذا مع تلاوته عليهم في نص التنزيل قوله: "وما كنت تتلو من قبله من كتاب ولا تخطه بيمينك إذاً لارتاب المبطلون". ولو عرفوه بذلك أو بصحبة أهل الكتب ونقلة السير ومداخلة أهل الأخبار ومجالسة أهل هذا الشأن لم يلبثوا أن يقولوا له: هذا كذب، لأنك ما زلت معروفاً بصحبة أهل الكتب ومجالستهم وقصدهم إلى مواضعهم ومواطنهم ومجاراتهم والأخذ عنهم والاستفادة منهم. وفي صدفهم عن هذا أجمع وعن تكلف معارضة سورة منه أو إيراد ما قل وكثر من ذلك مع علمهم بخروج نظم القرآن عن سائر أوزان كلامهم ونظومهم أعظم دليل على صدقه صلّى الله عليه وأن ظهور القرآن وهو نشأ معهم وبين أظهرهم ولم يعرفوه بقصد أهل الكتاب ومجالسة غير من لقوه وعرفوه والاقتباس منه ولا انفرد بمداخلة فصيح منهم ومتقدم في البراعة واللسن عليهم آية عظيمة وأمر خارق للعادة لأن مثل ذلك لا يكتسب بتعلم وتدقيق ذكاء وفطنة ولطيف حس وحيلة.
From the pride of souls: that the tongue with which it was sent down was their tongue, and with knowledge of what they were, and the greatness of chivalry and intensity of zeal and eagerness to deny him, and to scatter his gathering and disperse the people around him, and to devote themselves to falsifying him, and what shamed and belittled him, and their going out to what they went out to with him of war and sword-fighting, and putting themselves to the spilling of blood, and leaving homes, and forsaking homelands. If they were despite that able to oppose it or oppose a sura from it, they would have hastened to that, and it would have been easier for them and lighter than waging war with him, exile from homelands, enduring terrors, patience with killing, the pain of wounds, and bearing humiliation and disgrace; because he, peace be upon him, gave them the opportunity to deny him in two ways: one of them is his saying: "You will not bring its like," and the other is his saying: "If you bring it, you succeed and I am false and you are truthful." This with him reciting to them in the text of the Revelation His saying: "And you did not recite before it any book nor did you write it with your right hand; then the falsifiers would have doubted." And if they had known him by that or by companionship with the People of the Book and transmitters of biographies and intercourse with the people of reports and sitting with the people of this concern, they would not have delayed to say to him: This is a lie, because you have been known as one who keeps company with the People of the Book, sits with them, visits their places and locales, and imitates them and takes from them and benefits from them. And their turning away from all this and from taking the trouble to oppose a sura from it or to produce anything small or large of that, with their knowledge that the composition of the Quran departs from all the meters of their speech and their compositions, is the greatest proof of his truthfulness, may God bless him, and that the emergence of the Quran while he grew up among them and in their midst and they did not know him to seek the People of the Book and to sit with those other than whom they met and knew, nor to take from them, nor did he alone have access to an eloquent speaker among them, one advanced in eloquence and tongue over them, is a great sign and a custom-breaking matter, because such a thing cannot be acquired by learning and precision of intelligence, cleverness, subtlety of sense, and trickery.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood from two angles: the inimitability of the Quran and the Prophet's unletteredness. It begins by describing the intense pride and zeal of the Arabs, their eagerness to refute the Prophet, and their willingness to endure war, exile, and suffering. Despite this, they could not produce a rival to the Quran, even when challenged directly (the two challenges are the Quranic verse 'Say: If men and jinn gathered...' and the implicit challenge in the demand to bring a sura like it). Moreover, the Prophet himself was not known to have studied with scholars or scribes; the Quran itself points out that he was illiterate ('nor did you write it with your right hand'), which the Arabs could verify. If he had been known to associate with the People of the Book, they would have dismissed his claims. Their failure to produce a rival, combined with the fact that they knew his background, is the greatest proof of his truthfulness. The passage then adds that the Quran's very appearance among them while he was with them and they never saw him learning from any eloquent person is a miracle, as such eloquence cannot be acquired through mere intelligence or trickery.

Key Terms
معارضة
إعجاز
تحدي
أمية الرسول
خرق العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Arabs' failure to produce a rival was due to lack of effort or disinterest.
Correction: Baqillani shows they had the strongest motives—pride, zeal, and willingness to endure war—yet still could not, proving the Quran's divine origin.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what two things combined prove the Prophet's truthfulness in this passage?
A) The Arabs' poverty and the Prophet's wealth
B) The Arabs' inability to produce a rival to the Quran and the Prophet's known illiteracy
C) The Prophet's military victories and his knowledge of languages
D) The Quran's length and the Prophet's age

Key Takeaway
The Arabs' inability to match the Quran, combined with the Prophet's confirmed illiteracy, forms an overwhelming proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Arabs knew the truth of the Quran but their pride prevented them from accepting it. Is there an area in your life where your pride or attachment to a worldview stops you from submitting to a clear truth from Allah? What would it cost you to surrender it today?
?
This lesson shows that the Prophet's unletteredness was a key proof. Do you truly appreciate the miracle of the Quran in your daily life, or have you become so familiar with it that you no longer feel its weight? Re-read the verse about his illiteracy (Q 29:48) again and ask yourself: could this really be from a human being?
?
If you were among the Arabs, knowing their linguistic excellence, would you have been among those who rejected out of arrogance or among those who recognized the miracle? Examine your heart: when you encounter undeniable signs of Allah in your life, do you obey immediately or seek excuses to delay?

The Miracle of Sudden Eloquence and Language Knowledge
Baqillani argues that the Prophet's sudden mastery of languages and eloquence without learning is a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the Prophet's sudden mastery of languages and eloquence as a proof of prophethood, demonstrating a breach of natural custom.

Core Idea
The Prophet's overnight mastery of any language is a miracle that breaks all natural laws.

This passage presents a striking proof of prophethood: the Prophet's ability to go from complete ignorance of a foreign language to being its most eloquent speaker overnight, with no teacher. Baqillani argues that this sudden acquisition of knowledge is a clear breach of custom (khariq al-ada), which serves as a divine sign. The same logic applies to the Quran's eloquence, which is also beyond normal human capacity. Let's examine how this argument works.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage and Translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms like khariq al-ada (breach of custom) and lutf (subtle means).
The passage uses dense theological reasoning; reading it twice helps.
2
Identify the Two Miraculous Events
Find where Baqillani describes two things: (1) the Prophet's overnight mastery of foreign languages, and (2) the revelation of the Quran. Both are presented as breaches of normal custom.
The first example uses Zanj and Turk as languages; the second refers to the Quran's composition and eloquence.
3
Understand the Argument Structure
Baqillani argues that the impossibility of normal learning in such a short time proves divine intervention. He concludes that God only shows such signs to confirm the truth of His messengers.
This is a classic kalam proof: if something is beyond natural human capacity, it must be from God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيًن أن يبيت عليه السلام وهو غير عالم بلغة ذلك ولا فرق بين الزنج والترك وغيرهما من اللغات ثم يصبح أفصح الناس بكل لغة منها وأجرأهم فيها مع العلم بأنه لم يأخذ ذلك عن أهلها لأن خلق العلم فيه بذلك وإقداره عليه في يسير الوقت خرق للعادة وخارج عما عليه بناء الطبيعة وكذلك تعلم هذه اللغات واكتساب معرفتها والتمكن من علمها وتحصيلها في يسير الوقت الذي لا يكتسب في مثله العلم بعظيم ما جاء به آية عظيمة وخرق للعادة. فإنزال هذا الكلام عليه واضطراره إلى إجراء لسانه أو خلق لطبيعة يتمكن بها من إدراك هذا النظم ورصفه وبيانه من أظهر الآيات وأبين الدلالات لأن التمكن من تعلم ذلك بكل لطيفة في يسير الوقت مما لم تجر العادة بمثله نقض لها والله سبحانه لا يظهر الآيات إلا لما ذكرنا من القصد إلى الدلالة على صدق الرسل عليهم السلام.
And it is shown that he, peace be upon him, spent the night while not knowing the language of that, with no distinction between Zanj, Turk, and other languages, then in the morning he became the most eloquent of people in every language among them and the most bold in it, with the knowledge that he did not take that from its people, because the creation of knowledge in him of that and enabling him to do it in a short time is a breach of custom and outside what the constitution of nature is upon. And likewise learning these languages, acquiring knowledge of them, mastering their science, and attaining them in a short time, in the like of which the knowledge of the great thing he brought is not acquired, is a great sign and a breach of custom. For the sending down of this speech upon him and his being compelled to run his tongue, or the creation of a nature by which he becomes able to perceive this composition, arrange it, and clarify it, is among the clearest signs and most evident proofs, because the ability to learn that by every subtle means in a short time, which custom has not run to its like, is a break of it. And God Almighty does not show signs except for what we mentioned of the intent to indicate the truthfulness of the messengers, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is another proof of prophethood, focusing on the miracle of sudden knowledge and eloquence. It states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) could go from being completely ignorant of a foreign language (like Zanj or Turk) to being the most eloquent speaker in that language, with no known teacher. This acquisition of knowledge in an impossibly short time is a clear breach of the normal custom (khariq al-ada), i.e., a miracle. The same holds for the Quran: its revelation and the Prophet's ability to produce such eloquent speech is among the clearest signs. The passage concludes that God only performs such miracles to prove the truthfulness of His messengers.

Key Terms
خرق العادة
لطيفة
خلق العلم
إجراء اللسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Prophet studied languages in secret or had a natural gift that allowed rapid learning.
Correction: Baqillani stresses that the time was too short for normal learning, and the Prophet was not known to have access to teachers, making the acquisition a direct divine intervention—a miracle.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what makes the Prophet's mastery of foreign languages a miracle?
A) He learned them over many years from experts.
B) He became the most eloquent in a language overnight without any known teacher.
C) He only knew Arabic but pretended to know others.
D) He was born knowing all languages.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sudden eloquence and knowledge of languages, as well as the Quran's revelation, are miracles that break natural laws and prove his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Prophet's miracle of eloquence and language was not for him to boast, but to prove his truthfulness to others. In your own life, do you use the gifts Allah has given you as evidence of His generosity, or do you claim them as your own accomplishments? What would it look like to humbly attribute your talents to Allah's direct creation?

This lesson shows that Allah sometimes breaks His own natural laws to confirm His messengers. Refuting the Claim That the Qur'an Is Merely Superior Eloquence
Baqillani states the objection and refutes it by defining the limit of human skill.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the claim that the Quran's inimitability is merely a matter of superior eloquence by defining the normal limits of human skill.

Core Idea
Miracles break the pattern of normal human achievement, and the Quran does so.

Baqillani presents a challenge from Jews and Christians who argue that the Quran might just be exceptionally eloquent human speech. He refutes this by drawing a boundary between ordinary skill and miraculous transcendence. This lesson examines his argument that the Quran exceeds the known limits of human capability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Identify the objection that the Quran is merely superior eloquence from the same kind as human speech.
Notice that the objection concedes the Quran's excellence but denies its miraculous nature.
2
Understand Baqillani's key concept: the known limit of skill
Focus on Baqillani's response where he introduces the idea that every craft has a known limit that can be attained by skilled practitioners. Beyond that limit, it breaks the normal course of events.
This is the foundation of his refutation.
3
Examine the evidence: the Arabs' inability to match the Quran
Observe how Baqillani points out that the Arabs, despite their strong desire and collective effort, were unable to produce anything like the Quran. This proves it goes beyond normal skill.
Consider why this inability is significant: they had every motivation to match it.
4
Conclude why this qualifies as a miracle
Synthesize the argument: because the Quran surpasses the attainable limit and the best efforts of the most skilled, it is a miracle (khāriq li-l-‘āda) and not merely superior eloquence.
This is the central thesis of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في الرد على منكري إعجاز القرآن
فإن قالت اليهود والنصارى ما أنكرتم أن يكون ما أتى به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من جنس كلامهم، غير أنه كان أفصح وأوجز وأحسن نظماً وأن يكون ذلك إنما تأتى له بتقدمه في البلاغة عليهم وحسن فصاحته ولَسَنهِ وبَرَعَهم بذلك وزاد فيه على جميعهم؟ قيل لهم : إن قدر ما يقتضيه التقدم والحذق في الصناعة قدر معروف لا يخرق العادةَ مِثلُه ولا يعجز أهل الصناعة والمتقدمون فيها عنه مع التحدي والتقريع بالعجز والقصور لأن العادة جارية بجمع الدواعي والهمم على بلوغ منزلة الحاذق المتقدم في الصناعة وما أتى به النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من القرآن قد خرج عن حد ما يُكتسب بالحذق وعجز القوم عن معارضته ومقابلته مع إيثارهم لذلك واجتماع هممهم له وتوفر دواعيهم عليه وعلمهم بجعله حجة له ودلالة على صدقه فخرج بذلك عن نمط ما سألتم عنه .
A question concerning the refutation of those who deny the inimitability of the Quran. So if the Jews and Christians say: Why do you deny that what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought might be from the same kind as their speech, except that it was more eloquent, more concise, and better in composition, and that this came to him only by his being ahead of them in eloquence and the excellence of his fluency and tongue, and that he excelled them in that and surpassed all of them? It is said to them: Indeed, the extent required by precedence and skill in a craft is a known extent; nothing like it breaks the normal course of events, nor are the people of the craft and those advanced in it incapable of it when challenged and rebuked for incapacity and deficiency, because the normal course runs by bringing together motivations and determinations to reach the station of the skilled and advanced one in the craft. And what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought of the Quran has gone beyond the limit of what is acquired by skill; and the people were incapable of opposing it and matching it despite their preference for that, the gathering of their determinations for it, the abundance of their motivations for it, and their knowledge that he made it a proof for himself and an indication of his truthfulness. So it thus went out of the category of what you asked about.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. Baqillani begins by stating the objection from Jews and Christians: they claim that the Quran could simply be a product of superior eloquence, like one poet excelling another. The objection suggests that the Prophet's speech is from the same genre as their own, just better in fluency, conciseness, and composition. Baqillani then provides the refutation. He argues that every craft has a known limit of skill that can be attained through practice and precedence; exceeding that limit would break the normal course of events (kharaq al-‘āda). The ordinary course of nature is such that people collectively strive to reach the level of the most skilled in any craft. However, the Quran surpassed that attainable limit. The Arabs, despite their strong desire to refute it, their combined efforts, and their knowledge that the Prophet used it as a proof of his truthfulness, were utterly unable to produce anything like it. Therefore, the Quran does not fall within the category of normal human achievement; it is a miracle.

Key Terms
إعجاز القرآن
خرق العادة
الحذق
التحدي
التقريع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's superiority is merely quantitative—being more eloquent than other speech.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that the Quran's inimitability is a qualitative leap beyond the normal human capacity for eloquence, as it exceeds the known limit of skill and cannot be matched despite all efforts.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what distinguishes the Quran from ordinary human speech that is merely more eloquent?
A) It is in a different language.
B) It exceeds the known limit of human skill and cannot be matched despite efforts.
C) It was revealed by an angel.
D) It contains prophecies.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability lies in its surpassing the natural limits of human skill, as proven by the Arabs' inability to match it despite their best efforts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly feel that it is beyond any human speech, or do you take it for granted? What would it mean for your relationship with Allah if you really believed every word is a miracle that no one can imitate?
?
The Arabs had all the motivation in the world to disprove the Prophet, yet they failed. You have the Quran in your hands—do you live as if it is the ultimate authority, or do you sometimes think your own opinions can compete with it?
?
Baqillani argues that the Quran exceeds the limit of human skill. If you are honest with yourself, have you ever tried to 'improve' upon the Quran's guidance by following your own desires? How will you submit to its miracle today?

The Qur'an's Unique Meter and Quraish's Bewilderment
Baqillani argues the Qur'an's literary form differs from all known Arabic genres, proven by Quraish's confused reactions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the Quraish's inability to classify the Qur'an into known Arabic literary forms as evidence for its miraculous nature.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's meter is unlike any Arabic meter; even the experts were baffled.

Baqillani presents a second argument for the Qur'an's miraculous nature by focusing on its unique literary form. He points out that the Qur'an's meter does not fit any known Arabic poetic or prose form. The fact that the most eloquent Arabs—the Quraish—were completely bewildered and gave contradictory explanations proves that the Qur'an is beyond human capacity. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice Baqillani's logical progression: he states the premise, then gives evidence from Quraish's reactions, and concludes.
Pay attention to the list of contradictory claims by Quraish.
2
Understand the uniqueness claim
Baqillani says the Qur'an's meter (وزن) differs from all known Arabic meters (poetry, oratory, rajaz, long verse, double verse). Why is this significant?
The claim is that the Qur'an does not belong to any recognized genre.
3
Examine Quraish's bewilderment
List the various things Quraish said about the Qur'an (magic, taught by madman, ancient fables, etc.). They could not agree because they could not classify it.
Their confusion is evidence that it is not a product of their craft.
4
Connect to the Quranic verse
Baqillani quotes Quran 16:103 to refute the claim that it was taught by a foreigner. How does this support his argument?
The verse emphasizes the clear Arabic nature of the Qur'an.
5
Draw the conclusion
The inability to classify the Qur'an, despite being experts, proves it is a miracle, not just exceptional skill.
This is the central proof for the Qur'an's inimitability (i'jāz).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى أن الآية في القرآن أنه منزل بلسان العرب وكلامهم ومنظوم على وزن يفارق سائر أوزان كلامهم ولو كان من بعض النظوم التي يعرفونها لعلموا أنه شعر أو خطابة أو رَجَزٌ أو طويل أو مزدوج غير أن ناظمه قد برع وتقدم فيه وليس يُخرج الحذقُ في الصنعة إلى أن يؤتي بغير جنسها وما ليس منها في شيء وما لا يعرفه أهلها وإذا كان ذلك كذلك وكنا نعلم أن قريشاً أفصح العرب وأعرفها باللسان وأقدرها على سائر أوزان الكلام وأنها قد دهِشَت وطاشت عقولها فيما أتى به فقالت مرة إنه سحر، وقالت تارةً إنه معلم مجنون، وقالت أخرى أساطير الأولين اكتتبها، وقالت تارة أخرى شعر، وقالت تارة سلمان يلقنه ويلقي إليه حتى قال تعالى لسان الذي يلحدون إليه أعجمي وهذا لسان عربي مبين، عُلم بذلك أن ما أتى به ليس من جنس الحذق والتقدم في الصناعة في شيء.
And further, the sign of the Quran is that it is revealed in the tongue of the Arabs and their speech, and composed on a meter that differs from all their meters. If it were from some of the meters they know, they would know it is poetry or oration or rajaz or long verse or double verse; but its composer excelled and advanced in it. Skill in a craft does not bring forth something outside its genre and not of it at all, which its people do not recognize. And since that is so, and we know that Quraysh were the most eloquent of the Arabs, the most knowledgeable of the tongue, the most capable of all meters of speech, and that they were bewildered and their minds confounded by what he brought— they said once it is magic, and another time he is taught by a madman, and another time stories of the ancients which he has written down, and another time poetry, and another time Salman teaches him and dictates to him— until the Most High said: 'The tongue of the one they hint at is foreign, while this is a clear Arabic tongue'— it is known thereby that what he brought has nothing to do with the kind of skill and precedence in the craft.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a second proof (marked by 'wa 'alā' — 'and further') that the Quran's miraculous nature is evident from its unique literary form. Baqillani states that the Quran is revealed in Arabic and is composed on a meter (wazn) that differs from all the known meters of Arabic speech. If it belonged to any known category, the Arabs would have recognized it as poetry, oratory, rajaz (a meter), or other forms. But they could not classify it. Moreover, skill in a craft does not produce something entirely outside that craft that even the experts cannot recognize. Since Quraysh were the most eloquent and knowledgeable, their utter confusion—calling it magic, saying a madman taught him, calling it ancient fables, poetry, or claiming Salman taught him— proves it is beyond normal human skill. Even the Quranic verse (16:103) refutes the claim that it was taught by a foreigner, affirming its clear Arabic nature. This shows that the Quran is not merely a result of advanced skill but is a miracle.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran is just highly skilled poetry or oratory.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Quran does not fit any known Arabic genre; even the experts could not classify it, proving it is beyond human capacity.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani argue that the Quran cannot be a product of advanced Arabic literary skill?
A) Because it contains foreign words.
B) Because the Quraish, though experts, were bewildered and could not classify it into any known literary form.
C) Because the Prophet was illiterate.
D) Because it is a book of law.

Key Takeaway
The uniqueness of the Quran's literary form is proven by the bewilderment of the most eloquent Arabs, who could not place it in any known genre.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you ever pause to sense its otherness—that it cannot be reduced to any human category? Or do you treat it as just another book? What would it take for you to approach it with the bewilderment of the Quraish, not as confusion but as awe?
?
The Quraish were the experts of Arabic, yet they were lost. Are you willing to admit that your own knowledge or categories might be insufficient to grasp the Quran's truth? In what area of your life might you be trying to fit the Quran into a comfortable box—science, tradition, or your own desires?
?
Baqillani argues that skill cannot produce something outside its genre. If the Quran is truly unparalleled, does your response to it reflect that reality? Have you let the Quran challenge you, or have you domesticated it? Commit to reading one verse today as if for the first time, asking Allah to show you its miracle.

The Divine Role in Guaranteeing the Miracle
Baqillani presents a conditional proof that divine prevention of imitation is a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the concept of divine prevention to argue that the Quran is a miraculous sign.

Core Idea
Allah's deliberate prevention of imitation proves the Quran's divine origin.

Baqillani presents a subtle theological argument: if the Prophet were a liar, Allah would have enabled others to match the Quran to expose him. Since He did not, the lack of imitation is itself a miracle. This lesson unpacks that logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get its rhythm. Notice the conditional structure starting with 'wa 'alā anna'.
The passage is a single extended argument, so pay attention to the if-then logic.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage presents two scenarios: if the Prophet is truthful, Allah prevents imitation; if he were false, Allah would enable it. Identify these branches.
Look for the pivot around 'wa law ʿalima' (if He knew he was lying).
3
Understand the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that the prevention itself is a miracle (kharaq al-ʿāda) because it is a divine intervention that confirms truth. Ask yourself why this argument works.
This relies on the principle that Allah does not break customs except to indicate truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى أن الله سبحانه إذا أباح له هذا التقدم والحذق وجمع له أسبابه ووفر دواعيه وهمته على تحصيله وعلم مع ذلك أنه سَيَدَّعيه آية له وحجة على صدقه : همم من تحداه على فعل مثله ولا أتاحه لهم ولا مكنهم منه ، صار ذلك آية فعله وخرقاً للعادة وجرى مجرى سائر الآيات ولو علم الله سبحانه أنه كاذب فيما يدعيه لوفّر الدواعي والهمم وجمعها على معارضته وخلق اللطائف التي يُتوصل بها إلى بلوغ منزلته لكي يُبطل حجته ويزيل شبهته ومتى لم يفعل ذلك كان ناقضاً للعادة بصرف الهمم عن فعل ذلك وجمع الدواعي عليه ومنع اللطائف والأسباب الممكنة منه والله تعالى لا ينقض العادات إلا للدلالة على الصدق.
And further, that Allah Almighty, when He granted him this precedence and skill, gathered for him its causes, made abundant his motivations and determination for its acquisition, and knew with that that he would claim it as a sign for himself and a proof of his truthfulness— He set the determinations of those who challenged him to produce its like, but He did not grant it to them nor enable them to do it. Thus that became a sign of His action and a breaking of the normal course, running the course of other signs. And if Allah Almighty knew that he was lying in what he claimed, He would have made abundant the motivations and determinations and gathered them to oppose him, and He would have created the subtleties by which one could reach his station in order to invalidate his proof and remove his doubt. And when He did not do that, He would be a breaker of the normal course by diverting the determinations from doing that, gathering the motivations upon him, preventing the subtleties and possible means from him. And Allah Almighty does not break customs except as an indication of truthfulness.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a third proof (also beginning with 'wa 'alā') that the Quran is a miracle. Baqillani presents a theological argument: If Allah granted the Prophet this extraordinary level of eloquence and knowledge, and the Prophet intended to use it as a proof of his prophethood, then Allah's not enabling anyone else to produce something similar is a deliberate act of breaking the normal course (kharaq al-‘āda). This breaking of the norm serves as a sign of truth. Conversely, if the Prophet were a liar, Allah would have enabled others to match him to expose his falsehood. Since Allah did not do so, and in fact prevented any matching, it indicates the truthfulness of the Prophet's claim. The argument assumes that Allah is just and would not allow a false prophet's claim to stand unchallenged. Thus, the Qur'an is a miracle.

Key Terms
إباحة
آية
خرق العادة
الدواعي
الهمم
اللطائف
الصدق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the inability of others to match the Quran is due to lack of effort or natural incapacity.
Correction: Baqillani argues it is a divine prevention, a deliberate break of the norm to confirm prophethood, not a natural failure.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why does Allah not break the normal course (kharaq al-‘āda) except for truthfulness?
A) Because He is merciful.
B) Because if He allowed a false claim, He would be enabling a lie.
C) Because the Prophet asked for it.
D) Because the Arabs were not capable.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's argument shows that the inability of others to match the Quran is not a natural fact but a divine act of prevention that confirms the Prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have been given skills and opportunities in life. Do you see them as signs from Allah, or do you attribute them solely to your own effort? How does Baqillani's argument challenge you to recognize Allah's hand in your successes?
?
If you were to claim something significant for the sake of Allah, would you trust that Allah would prevent others from disproving you? How does this passage test your reliance on Allah's justice and protection?
?
Reflect on a time when you felt challenged or opposed. Did you trust that Allah would prevent your opponents from succeeding if you were in the right? How can this truth change how you face future opposition?

Miracles

The Quran as a Miracle through Prevention of Opposition
Baqillani argues that the Quran is a miracle because Allah prevented others from matching it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the Quran's miraculous nature is established not merely by its eloquence but by Allah's active prevention of anyone producing a similar text despite the challenge.

Core Idea
The Quran’s miracle lies in Allah's prevention of opposition, not just its eloquence.

Baqillani presents a sophisticated kalam proof that the Quran is a true miracle. He begins by addressing the disbelievers' accusations that the Quran was invented or taught by a human, then quotes the Quranic response. From this, he builds a conditional argument: if Allah granted the Prophet skill and allowed him to claim it as a sign, then the fact that no one could match it despite the public challenge is itself a miraculous intervention. This lesson will guide you through his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice the structure: accusations, Quranic reply, conditional argument, counterfactual, conclusion.
The Arabic is dense; focus on the logical connectors like 'if... then'.
2
Identify the accusations
Baqillani lists the disbelievers' claims: that the Prophet wrote it himself, that it is poetry, or that Salman taught him. Notice how the Quranic rebuttal is quoted.
The verse quoted shows the Quran is in clear Arabic, not foreign.
3
Understand the conditional proof
The key conditional: if Allah permitted the Prophet to have skill and knew he would claim it as a sign, then Allah's prevention of others from matching it is the miracle. This is the core of the argument.
The prevention itself is a 'breaking of custom' (kharq al-ada).
4
Consider the counterfactual
Baqillani strengthens his argument with a counterfactual: if the Prophet were lying, Allah would have enabled opposition to expose him. Since He did not, the Prophet is truthful.
This shows that the miracle is not just a static event but an act of divine protection.
5
Conclude the miracle
The prevention of opposition, given the public challenge, is a true miracle that confirms prophethood. This goes beyond linguistic inimitability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اكتتبها، وقالت تارة أخرى شعر، وقالت تارة: سلمان يلقنه ويلقي إليه، حتى قال تعالى: لسان الذي يلحدون إليه أعجمي وهذا لسان عربي مبين. عُلم بذلك أن ما أتى به ليس من جنس الحذق والتقدم في الصناعة في شيء، وعلى أن الله سبحانه إذا أباح له هذا التقدم والحذق وجمع له أسبابه ووفر دواعيه وهمته على تحصيله، وعلم مع ذلك أنه سيدّعيه آية له وحجة على صدقه، همم من تحداه على فعل مثله ولا أتاحه لهم ولا مكنهم منه، صار ذلك آية فعله وخرقاً للعادة وجرى مجرى سائر الآيات. ولو علم الله سبحانه أنه كاذب فيما يدعيه لوفّر الدواعي والهمم وجمعها على معارضته وخلق اللطائف التي يتوصل بها إلى بلوغ منزلته لكي يبطل حجته ويزيل شبهته، ومتى لم يفعل ذلك كان ناقضاً للعادة بصرف الهمم عن فعل ذلك وجمع الدواعي عليه ومنع اللطائف والأسباب الممكنة منه، والله تعالى لا ينقض العادات إلا للدلالة على الصدق.
He wrote it down; and another time they said: poetry; and another time they said: Salman teaches him and dictates to him, until Allah said: 'The tongue of the one they refer to is foreign, while this is a clear Arabic tongue.' So it was known by that that what he brought is not of the kind of skill and advancement in craftsmanship at all; and that Allah, exalted, when He permitted him this advancement and skill, and gathered for him its causes, and provided his motives and his determination to attain it, and He knew with that that he would claim it as a sign for him and a proof of his truthfulness, He prevented the ambitions of those who challenged him from doing the like, and did not grant it to them nor enable them to do it; so that became a sign (aya) from Him and a breaking of custom (kharq al-‘ada) and it ran the course of the other signs. And if Allah, exalted, had known that he was lying in what he claimed, He would have provided the motives and ambitions and gathered them to oppose him, and created the subtle means by which they could attain his station, in order to invalidate his proof and remove his ambiguity. And if He did not do that, He would be breaking custom by diverting ambitions from doing that and gathering motives against it and preventing the subtle means and possible causes from it. But Allah, exalted, does not break customs except to indicate truthfulness.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage presents a complex kalam proof that the Quran is a miracle not merely because of its eloquence, but because Allah actively prevented anyone from opposing it despite the public challenge. Baqillani begins by citing the disbelievers' accusations that the Quran was invented, poetry, or taught by Salman, and then quotes the Quranic reply that those sources are foreign while the Quran is clear Arabic. From this, he argues that the Quran is not the product of ordinary human skill. The core of the argument is a conditional: if Allah granted the Prophet skill and knowledge, and knew that he would claim it as a sign, and yet did not enable others to match it, then the prevention itself is the miracle. The proof is strengthened by a counterfactual: if Allah had known the Prophet was lying, He would have enabled opposition to expose him, but He did not, which shows the Prophet is truthful. Thus, the Quran is a true miracle (khariq li'l-ada) that serves to confirm prophethood.

تحدي (tahaddi) - challenge
إعجاز (i'jaz) - inimitability
خرق العادة (kharq al-‘ada) - breaking of custom (miracle)
آية (aya) - sign/miracle

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's miracle is only its linguistic beauty.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the prevention of opposition is the core miraculous element, not just eloquence.

A) Its eloquence alone
B) The fact that Allah prevented others from producing something like it despite the challenge

Key Takeaway
The Quran's miraculous nature is proven by Allah's active prevention of anyone producing a similar text, which serves as a sign of the Prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Will you today, before you close your eyes, decide to treat your next recitation as a meeting with the very sign of Allah's truth, not just words on a page?
?
Baqillani argues that if the Prophet were a liar, Allah would have exposed him by enabling a rival. You claim to believe the Quran is from Allah — but do you live as though you are accountable to a message that is uniquely protected from imitation? How would your speech, your choices, and your priorities change right now if you truly believed that this Book stands as the only unanswerable challenge from your Creator? What is one habit you will repent of today because it contradicts the claim that you follow the Prophet whose truth was vindicated by divine prevention?

Refuting the Objection of Other Unchallenged Works
Baqillani refutes the objection that Euclid's book and the Almagest would also be miracles if unanswered.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the objection that other unchallenged works would also be miracles, by distinguishing divine support from mere lack of opposition.

Core Idea
An unanswered challenge is only a miracle if God intends it as a sign.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a clever objection: if lack of opposition makes a miracle, then Euclid's geometry book and Imru' al-Qais' poem would also be miracles. Baqillani concedes the principle but adds a crucial condition: God only withholds opposition when He knows the claimant is truthful. This preserves the Quran's unique miraculous status without falling into relativism.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the opponent's hypothetical: if someone challenged with a book like Euclid's, and no one opposed it, would it be a miracle?
2
Analyze Baqillani's response
Note how he first concedes ('ajal) but then introduces a distinction based on divine knowledge of the claimant's truthfulness.
3
Reflect on the implication
This answer explains why the Quran's challenge remains unique: God enabled opposition in other cases but prevented it for the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من مسألة في التحدي: فإن قال قائل: وكذلك يقولون: إن صاحب كتاب إقليدس والمَجْسِطِي والقائل «قفا نبك» لو تحدوا بمثل ما أتوا به وجعلوه دلالة على صدقهم وأنهم رسل الله سبحانه فلم يعارضوا وجب أن يكون ذلك آية لهم. قيل له: أجل، إلا أن الله سبحانه إذا علم أن المدعي ذلك كاذب، فلا بد أن يجمع الهمم ويوفر الدواعي على معارضة ما تحدى القوم به، فلا يلبثون عند احتجاجهم به أن يأتيهم الناس بأمثاله وما هو أبلغ منه في معناه، لكي ينقض كون ما ادعوه معجزاً.
From the issue of the challenge: So if someone says: And likewise they say: The author of Euclid's book and the Almagest and the one who said 'Stop, let us weep' - if they had challenged with something like what they brought and made it a sign of their truthfulness and that they are messengers of Allah, and no one opposed them, it would be necessary that that be a sign for them. It is said to him: Yes, except that Allah, exalted, when He knows that the claimant is lying, necessarily gathers the ambitions and provides the motives to oppose what the people challenged with, so that when they present their argument, people would bring them its like and what is more eloquent in its meaning, in order to invalidate the status of what they claimed as a miracle.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer within the kalam methodology. The opponent raises a counterexample: Euclid, the Almagest (Ptolemy's work), and the famous poet of the Mu'allaqa (Imru' al-Qais) all produced works that were challenged but not opposed. If that makes a miracle, then their works would also be miracles. Baqillani's answer is that the principle is conceded ('ajal) but with a crucial condition: Allah only prevents opposition when He knows the claimant is truthful. If the claimant were false, Allah would ensure that opposition arises to expose him. Thus, the case of the Quran is unique because Allah's knowledge of the Prophet's truthfulness led to the prevention of opposition, whereas in the other cases, either the claimant was not a prophet or Allah did not intend to support them. The answer preserves the miraculous nature of the Quran by linking the lack of opposition to divine will.

Key Terms
تحَدٍّ (tahaddin) - challenge
معارضة (mu‘arada) - opposition
آية (aya) - sign/miracle

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any work that remains unchallenged after a public challenge is a miracle.
Correction: A work is only a miracle if God purposely prevents opposition as a sign of the claimant's truthfulness; otherwise, God would cause opposition.

Checkpoint

B) He says that if the claimant were false, God would have enabled opposition
C) He argues that Euclid was a prophet
D) He says the Quran is more eloquent

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that a miracle is not just any unanswered challenge, but one where God deliberately prevents opposition as a sign of truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Allah ensures that false claims are exposed by providing opposition. Do you truly believe that no one can successfully challenge the Quran? If so, why does your heart sometimes waver when you hear doubts?
?
The fact that Allah knows every claimant's heart and acts accordingly—does this make you more certain of His justice? How does this certainty affect the way you live today, especially when you are tempted to claim something false about yourself?

Refuting the Objection that Fear Prevented Opposition
Baqillani argues that if fear had prevented open opposition, it would still have been transmitted secretly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the principle of customary transmission (istiqrar al-'ada) to refute the claim that fear of reprisal prevented the Arabs from opposing the Quran.

Core Idea
If opposition had occurred, it would have been transmitted — even in secret.

Baqillani now addresses a psychological objection: maybe the Arabs privately opposed the Quran but were too afraid to show it. He refutes this by appealing to the settled custom of how humans behave when afraid of a ruler — they still talk among trusted circles. This passage shows how he turns an absence of evidence into evidence of absence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first line of the Arabic. The objectors claim that fear of the sword prevented the Arabs from showing their opposition to the Quran.
This is a common attempt to explain away the miracle.
2
Analyze Baqillani's response
Notice how he responds with a conditional: 'If the matter were as you claim...' He then argues that even if fear prevented public opposition, private discussion would have occurred and been transmitted.
He uses the word 'settled custom' (mustaqir al-'ada) as a basis for his argument.
3
Reflect on the analogy
Compare Baqillani's argument with the example of people discussing the faults of their rulers in private. This shows that fear does not completely suppress talk about challenges.
The analogy strengthens the point that absence of transmission proves absence of opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في المعارضة: فإن قالوا: ما أنكرتم أن تكون العرب قد عارضته، وأن يكون خوف سيفكم يمنع من إظهار معارضته؟ قيل لهم: لو كان الأمر على ما ادعيتموه لجاز نقله وذكره وذكر المعارض والمتولي له، ولوجب بمستقر العادة أن يغلب إظهاره على طيّه وكتمانه، حتى يكون العلم به كالعلم بالقرآن الذي هو عروضه، وإن منع الخوف من النص عليه والتبيين من كل واحد لذكره، لأنه كان لا بد من تحدثهم بينهم إذا خلوا وجالسوا من يأمنون سيفه على وجه يجب أن يضطر إليه، كما يجب أن تعلم الأسباب الحاملة على الكتمان والكذب الواقعين من السلطان لغرض في الحمل على ذلك مع الخوف منه، وكما يجب في مستقر العادة تحدث الناس بعيوب سلطانهم وجبابرتهم ومذموم الخصال التي فيهم، وإن لم ينقل.
Issue of opposition: So if they say: What do you deny that the Arabs might have opposed it, and that fear of your sword prevented them from showing their opposition? It is said to them: If the matter were as you claim, then its transmission and mention and mention of the opponent and the one who undertook it would be possible, and it would be necessary by settled custom that its disclosure would overcome its concealment and suppression, until knowledge of it would be like knowledge of the Quran which is its counterpart. And even if fear prevented each one from declaring and explaining it, because they would inevitably discuss among themselves when they were alone and with those they feel safe from his sword in a way that would be compelled to know, just as one must know the causes leading to concealment and lies occurring from the sultan for a purpose in that, along with fear of him, and just as it is necessary by settled custom that people discuss the faults of their sultans and tyrants and the blameworthy traits in them, even if that is not transmitted.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents another objection regarding the possibility that fear of the Prophet's military power prevented the Arabs from openly showing their opposition. Baqillani refutes this by appealing to the nature of oral transmission and human psychology. He argues that if any opposition had occurred, it would have been transmitted in some form, even if secretly. Custom dictates that when people fear a ruler, they still discuss his faults in private, especially when among trusted companions. Therefore, the complete absence of any report of opposition—whether hidden or public—proves that no real opposition ever took place. Baqillani uses an analogy: just as we know that people talk about the flaws of their rulers despite fear, we would expect similar reports of any attempted opposition to the Quran. The lack of such reports indicates that the Quran's challenge was truly unanswered, reinforcing its miraculous status.

Key Terms
معارضة (mu‘arada) - opposition
خوف (khawf) - fear
كتمان (kitman) - concealment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Fear could completely suppress all evidence of opposition, so the absence of transmission does not prove opposition didn't occur.
Correction: Baqillani argues that human nature and settled custom guarantee some transmission, even secretly. People always discuss rulers' flaws in private; thus, if opposition had happened, it would have been transmitted.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani counter the claim that fear of the sword prevented the Arabs from showing their opposition?
A) He denies that the Arabs had any fear
B) He argues that any opposition would have been transmitted secretly, just as people discuss rulers' faults
C) He says the Quran's eloquence was so great that no one could oppose it
D) He claims that the Arabs openly admitted they could not oppose it

Key Takeaway
The complete absence of any transmission of opposition, even in secret circles, proves that no one could genuinely oppose the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What truth about your own faith might you be hiding from others due to fear of criticism, and how does Baqillani's argument that secrecy cannot last challenge you to speak out?
?
If you were in a situation where openly affirming the Quran could cost you your reputation or safety, would you still find ways to uphold it in private? What does that reveal about your conviction?
?
The Arabs could not suppress opposition even under threat of death—are there any doubts or objections you have about the Quran that you have not honestly confronted? How might this argument help you face them?

Why Fear Did Not Prevent a Quranic Rival
Baqillani answers the objection that fear of the sword prevented the Arabs from producing a rival to the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's rational argument that fear of the sword could not have prevented the Arabs from producing and transmitting a rival to the Quran, based on the principle of settled custom (mustaqir al-ʿāda).

Core Idea
If a Quranic rival existed, it would have been transmitted through settled custom, just like people talk about rulers' faults despite fear.

Baqillani addresses a common objection: perhaps the Arabs did produce a rival to the Quran but were too afraid of the Prophet's sword to reveal it. He shows this is impossible by appealing to how people naturally transmit information, even dangerous information, among themselves. In this passage, he builds a logical case that such a rival would have become known if it existed.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Baqillani's response
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Baqillani first states the objection clearly, then gives a two-part answer.
The objection claims fear prevented publicizing a rival.
2
Understand the key analogy
Focus on the analogy: people speak about their rulers' faults despite fear. Baqillani argues that if a Quranic rival existed, it would have been transmitted through private conversations, just as rulers' faults are.
This shows settled custom overcomes fear.
3
See the extension to other prophets
Notice how Baqillani turns the argument back on the objectors: if fear explains the lack of a Quranic rival, it could also explain away the miracles of Moses and Jesus, which is absurd.
This strengthens the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في المعارضة
فإن قالوا: ما أنكرتم أن تكون العرب قد عارضته وأن يكون خوف سيفكم يمنع من إظهار معارضته؟ قيل لهم: لو كان الأمر على ما ادعيتموه لجاز نقله وذكره وذكر المعارض والمتولي له ولوجب بمستقر العادة أن يغلب إظهاره على طيه وكتمانه حتى يكون العلم به كالعلم بالقرآن الذي هو عروضه، وإن منع الخوف من النص عليه والتبيين من كل واحد لذكره لأنه كان لا بد من تحدثهم بينهم إذا خلوا وجالسوا من يأمنون سيفه على وجه يجب أن يضطر إليه كما يجب أن تعلم الأسباب الحاملة على الكتمان والكذب الواقعين من السلطان لغرض في الحمل على ذلك مع الخوف منه، وكما يجب في مستقر العادة تحدث الناس بعيوب سلطانهم وجبابرتهم ومذموم الخصال التي فيهم وإن لم ينقل ذلك نقلاً ظاهراً، ويقع تفصيله والنص عليه والبيان له من كل رجل بعينه. وإذا كنا لا نعلم وجود المعارضة للقرآن كعلمنا لظهوره من جهة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وجب سقوط ما قالوا. وأيضاً فلو كان الخوف من من نقلهم المعارضة لمنع ذلك أيضاً من دعوى المعارضة، فإذا لم يمنع الخوف من قولكم: قد عورض، وإن كان تصريحاً بالقدح في القرآن والتكذيب له مع عروه من حجة أو شبهة، فكيف يمنعكم الخوف من إظهار ما ادعيتم؟ ويقال لمن سأل عن هذا من اليهود والنصارى: لو كان ما قلتموه صحيحاً لجاز لمدع أن يدعي أن موسى وعيسى عليهما السلام قد عورضا في قلب العصا حية وفلق البحر وإحياء الميت وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص، وأن الخوف من أسيافكم يمنع من قتل ذلك، وأن الخوف من سيوف المسلمين اليوم يمنع من نقله الآن، لأن مكذب موسى وعيسى عند المسلمين بمنزلة مكذب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم. فإن لم يجب هذا لم يجب ما قلتم.
Issue concerning the counterfeiting. If they say: What prevents you [from admitting] that the Arabs did counter it and that the fear of your sword prevents the manifestation of its counterfeiting? Say to them: If the matter were as you claim, then its transmission, mention, and the mention of the one who counterfeited and undertook it would be possible, and by settled custom its manifestation would prevail over its suppression and concealment, so that knowledge of it would be like knowledge of the Quran which is its counterpart. Even if fear prevented explicit declaration and clarification from every single person, it would still be necessary for them to talk among themselves when alone and with those they trust from the sword, in a manner that would compel knowledge, just as one must know the causes leading to concealment and lying by the ruler for a purpose in compelling that despite fear, and just as by settled custom people speak of the faults of their rulers and tyrants and the blameworthy traits they possess, even if that is not transmitted overtly, and its details, explicit mention, and clarification occur from every individual man. Since we do not know of the existence of a counterfeiting of the Quran as we know of its emergence from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, their claim necessarily falls. Moreover, if fear of the one transmitting the counterfeiting would also prevent the claim of counterfeiting itself, then since fear does not prevent you from saying 'it has been countered' – even though that is an explicit attack on the Quran and denial of it without proof or doubt – how would fear prevent you from manifesting what you claim? And it is said to whoever asks about this from Jews and Christians: If what you said were true, then a claimant could claim that Moses and Jesus, peace be upon them, were countered in the turning of the staff into a serpent, the splitting of the sea, the reviving of the dead, and the curing of the blind and leprous, and that fear of your swords prevents that [counterfeiting], and that fear of the swords of Muslims today prevents its transmission now, because the denier of Moses and Jesus among the Muslims is like the denier of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. If this is not necessary, then what you said is not necessary.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (مسألة في المعارضة) where Baqillani refutes the claim that the Arabs did produce a rival to the Quran but were prevented from publicizing it by fear of the Muslim sword. The argument unfolds in stages: First, Baqillani states that if such a counterfeiting had occurred, it would have been transmitted and mentioned, because by settled custom (مستقر العادة) people tend to spread even hidden matters, especially when they are in private. He draws an analogy: people speak about the faults of their rulers despite fear, so why would a counterfeiting of the Quran be any different? Second, he argues that if fear prevented the transmission of the counterfeiting, it would also prevent the very claim of counterfeiting—yet the objectors freely claim that a counterfeiting occurred, so fear cannot be the excuse. Finally, he extends the argument to Jews and Christians: if fear can explain away the failure to produce a rival for the Quran, then it could also explain away failures for the miracles of Moses and Jesus, which is absurd. Therefore, the objection fails.

Key Terms
معارضة (muʿāraḍa)
خوف (khawf)
مستقر العادة (mustaqir al-ʿāda)
إعجاز (iʿjāz)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Arabs might have produced a rival to the Quran but were too afraid to show it.
Correction: Baqillani demonstrates that settled custom would have transmitted any such rival, and the fear objection is self-contradictory and could be used to deny all miracles.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why does the fear of the sword not prevent the transmission of a counterfeiting of the Quran?
A) Because the Arabs had no fear of the sword.
B) Because settled custom shows that even hidden matters like rulers' faults are transmitted despite fear.
C) Because the Quran itself prohibits concealment.
D) Because the counterfeiting was never actually produced.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani proves that the lack of a transmitted rival to the Quran is conclusive evidence of its inimitability, because settled custom would have preserved any challenge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever remained silent about a truth because you feared the reaction of others? What does Baqillani's argument about the inevitability of transmission say about the power of truth over fear?
?
Baqillani shows that even rulers' faults are spoken of in private. Where in your life do you privately acknowledge truths that you publicly avoid? What would it cost you to be honest?
?
If the Quran's inimitability is evidenced by the failure of any rival despite settled custom, what does that demand from you in terms of your response to the Quran? Will you let fear or custom guide your acceptance of this truth?

Learning Objective

Could divine intervention erase all memory of a counterfeiting?

In this lesson, we examine a powerful objection raised against the miraculous preservation of the Quran. The objector suggests that the counterfeiting actually occurred but was forgotten because God turned people's motives away. This challenges the very foundation of the tawatur argument. The Arabs' Inability to Counter the Quran
Baqillani refutes the claim that the Arabs neglected to counter the Quran due to lack of careful consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the Arabs' failure to produce a rival to the Quran was due to their incapacity, not a lack of effort or thought.

Core Idea
The Arabs' failure to counter the Quran proves its inimitability, not their negligence.

Imam Baqillani addresses a common objection to the Quran's miraculous nature: perhaps the Arabs simply did not bother to counter it. He shows this is impossible because the Arabs were highly intelligent, eloquent, and desperate to disprove the Prophet. Their failure to produce a rival is evidence of their inability.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the opening objection ('if someone says...') and Baqillani's immediate refutation ('it was said to them...'). Notice how he dismisses the idea as obvious nonsense.
The response uses a strong rhetorical counter.
2
Understand the analogy
Baqillani gives an analogy: if someone tells a standing person they cannot stand, it is an obvious lie. This illustrates that the Arabs knew they could not match the Quran, so they didn't even try.
The analogy appeals to basic human reason.
3
Examine the evidence of Arab intelligence
Baqillani lists qualities of the Arabs: abundant intellect, excellent natural dispositions, sound literary skills, and being described as 'a contentious people' by Allah. This shows they were capable of recognizing a challenge.
This counters the idea that they were negligent.
4
Reflect on the Quranic demands
Read the verses where the Arabs demanded extraordinary signs (springs, gardens, angels, etc.) and the Jews demanded to see Allah. This proves they were persistent in seeking proof, not lazy.
Their demands for miracles show their eagerness to disprove the Prophet.
5
Consider the rhetorical conclusion
Baqillani ends with a rhetorical question: how could all these people be ignorant unless the questioner is ignorant? This drives home the point that the only explanation is inability.
This is a powerful closing argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في المعارضة والإعجاز. فإن قال قائل: ما أنكرتم أن يكون القوم إنما تركوا معارضة القرآن لإعراضهم عن النظر في أن مقابلته بمثله موجب لتكذيب من أتى به؟ قيل لهم: فهذا مما لا نظر فيه ولا تأمل لأنه لا شبهة على أحد كمل عقله من أن قال له قائل: إنك لن تقوم ولن تقدر على القيام كاذب إذا قام وقدر على القيام والأطفال المنتقصون يعلمون هذا فضلاً عن قريش في وفارة عقولهم وجودة قرائحهم ونحائزهم وصحة آدابهم وما وصفهم الله تعالى به من أنهم قوم خصمون والتماسهم من الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم آيات غير التي أتى بها حتى قال تعالى: وما منعنا أن نرسل بالآيات إلا أن كذب بها الأولون يعني التي سألوها، ومع قولهم: لن نؤمن لك حتى تفجر لنا من الأرض ينبوعا أو تكون لك جنة من نخيل وعنب فتفجر الأنهار خلالها تفجيرا، أو تسقط السماء كما زعمت علينا كسفا أو تأتي بالله والملائكة قبيلا، وقوله: أو يكون لك بيت من زخرف أو ترقى في السماء ولن نؤمن لرقيك حتى تنزل علينا كتابا نقرؤه ومع ما ذكره عن اليهود في قوله: يسألك أهل الكتاب أن تنزل عليهم كتاباً من السماء فقد سألوا موسى أكبر من ذلك فقالوا: أرنا الله جهرة مع ما عليه أهل الإلحاد والتعطيل من الاحتجاج والعناد فكيف جهل هؤلاء أجمع ولم ينبه بعضهم بعضاً عليه لولا جهل السائل عن هذا؟. ويقال للسائل عن هذا من اليهود والنصارى: فما أنكرتم ألا يكون
Issue concerning opposition and inimitability. For if someone says: What prevents you from thinking that the people only left off opposing the Qur'an due to their turning away from considering that matching it with something like it would necessitate the falsification of the one who brought it? It was said to them: This is something about which there is no consideration or reflection, because there is no doubt for anyone of complete intellect that if someone said to him: 'You will not stand and will not be able to stand'—while he is standing and able to stand—that the speaker is a liar. Children of limited understanding know this, let alone Quraysh, with the abundance of their intellects, the excellence of their natural dispositions, their aptitudes, and the soundness of their literary skills, and what Allah, exalted, described them with: that they are a contentious people, and their seeking from the Messenger, peace be upon him, signs other than those he brought, until He said: 'And nothing prevented Us from sending signs except that the former peoples denied them'—meaning those they asked for—and with their saying: 'We will not believe you until you cause a spring to gush forth from the earth for us, or you have a garden of date palms and vines and cause rivers to gush forth in it abundantly, or you cause the sky to fall upon us in pieces as you have claimed, or you bring Allah and the angels before us,' and His saying: 'Or you have a house of ornament, or you ascend into the sky, and we will not believe in your ascent until you send down to us a book we can read'—and with what He mentioned about the Jews in His saying: 'The People of the Scripture ask you to bring down a book from heaven. They asked Moses for something greater than that, and said: Show us Allah outright.' All this, despite what the people of atheism and denial possess of argumentation and stubbornness—how could all these people have been ignorant and not alerted each other to it, except due to the ignorance of the questioner about this? And it is said to the questioner about this from the Jews and Christians: What prevents you from thinking that maybe...
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection raised against the miraculous nature of the Quran. The objector suggests that the Arabs merely refrained from producing a counter-Quran because they did not bother to consider that doing so would disprove the Prophet. The answer is that this is obviously false: it is like saying a man cannot stand when he is already standing—anyone, even children, knows this is a lie. The Arabs were known for their eloquence and intelligence (described as 'contentious' in the Quran), and they demanded extraordinary miracles from the Prophet (like springs, gardens, falling skies, angels, etc.), which shows their persistence. They also challenged Moses for even greater signs. Given their stubbornness and argumentative nature, it is impossible that they would have neglected to produce a counter-Quran out of mere oversight. The only explanation is their sheer inability. The passage ends with a rhetorical question to the objector: how could all these people be ignorant of such a simple point?

Key Terms
المعارضة
الإعجاز
القرائح
الخصومة
الآيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument insults the Arabs by implying they were incapable.
Correction: Actually, Baqillani acknowledges their intelligence and eloquence, and uses their capabilities to show that their failure was due to inability, not negligence.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani illustrate that the Arabs' failure to counter the Quran was due to incapacity, not neglect?
A) By quoting Quranic verses about their demands.
B) By comparing it to a man who is stood up and told he cannot stand.
C) By arguing that they feared retaliation.
D) By saying they were too lazy.

Key Takeaway
The Arabs' inability to produce a counter-Quran, despite their eloquence and persistence, proves its divine origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Arabs, with all their eloquence, could not produce even a single verse like the Quran. You read the Quran daily—do you truly feel its weight as the unmatchable speech of Allah? If not, what will you change today to let that reality transform your recitation and your heart?
?
Baqillani says that even children know the standing man is not lying. Yet you often treat the Quran as one book among many. In what specific area of your life are you acting as if human words could replace Allah's words? Name it now and commit to a concrete action to honor the Quran's uniqueness.
?
The Arabs demanded miracles yet failed to see the greatest miracle before them. What miracle have you been overlooking in your own life because you are too focused on asking for something else? How will you respond to the Quran as your personal sign from Allah starting today?

Refuting an Objection about the Prophet's Inability
Baqillani refutes an objection by citing Quraysh's intellect and Jewish demands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani turns the objector's premise about Quraysh's intelligence against him, using Quranic evidence to demonstrate the objector's ignorance.

Core Idea
The objector's own evidence proves his ignorance.

This passage presents an objection against the Prophet's ability to bring miracles. The objector argues that even children know the Prophet is a liar, and the intelligent Quraysh would have exposed him. Baqillani turns this argument on its head by citing the same Quraysh's contentious nature and their demands for specific signs, as well as the Jews' demands. He concludes that if these intelligent people were not convinced by the objection, the questioner must be ignorant.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Identify the objector's claim: that the Prophet could not stand and is a liar, and that even imperfect children know this.
The objector uses the intelligence of Quraysh as evidence.
2
Examine Baqillani's counterargument
Notice how Baqillani quotes Quranic verses showing that the Quraysh themselves demanded specific miracles, and Allah responded that earlier peoples had denied such signs.
The demands include springs, gardens, falling sky, and bringing Allah and angels.
3
See the Jewish demands
Baqillani also cites the Jews asking for a book and to see Allah openly, showing that even greater signs were requested but not proof of the prophet's inability.
4
Understand the rhetorical conclusion
Baqillani asks how all these intelligent people could be ignorant of the objection, implying the objector himself is the ignorant one.
This is a classic refutation: using the opponent's own premises against them.

قال له قائل : إنك لن تقوم ولن تقدر على القيام كاذب إذا قام وقدر على القيام والأطفال المنتقصون يعلمون هذا فضلاً عن قريش في وفارة عقولهم وجودة قرائحهم ونحائزهم وصحة آدابهم وما وصفهم الله تعالى به من أنهم قوم خصمون والتماسهم من الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم آيات غير التي أتى بها حتى قال تعالى : وما منعنا أن نرسل بالآيات إلا أن كذب بها الأولون يعني التي سألوها، ومع قولهم : لن نؤمن لك حتى تفجر لنا من الأرض ينبوعا أو تكون لك جنة من نخيل وعنب فتفجر الأنهار خلالها تفجيرا، أو تسقط السماء كما زعمت علينا كسفا أو تأتي بالله والملائكة قبيلا، وقوله : أو يكون لك بيت من زخرف أو ترقى في السماء ولن نؤمن لرقيك حتى تنزل علينا كتابا نقرؤه، ومع ما ذكره عن اليهود في قوله : يسألك أهل الكتاب أن تنزل عليهم كتاباً من السماء فقد سألوا موسى أكبر من ذلك فقالوا : أرنا الله جهرة مع ما عليه أهل الإلحاد والتعطيل من الاحتجاج والعناد فكيف جهل هؤلاء أجمع ولم ينبه بعضهم بعضاً عليه لولا جهل السائل عن هذا؟
Someone said to him: You will not stand and will not be able to stand, a liar when he stood and was able to stand, and imperfect children know this, let alone Quraysh in the abundance of their intellects, the excellence of their natural dispositions, their [؟] and the soundness of their manners, and what Allah Almighty described them with that they are a contentious people, and their requesting from the Messenger peace be upon him signs other than those he brought until Allah Almighty said: 'And nothing prevented Us from sending the signs except that the former peoples denied them,' meaning those which they asked, and with their saying: 'We will not believe you until you break open for us from the earth a spring, or you have a garden of date palms and vines and cause rivers to gush forth within it in gushing, or you cause the sky to fall upon us in pieces as you claim, or you bring Allah and the angels as a surety,' and His saying: 'Or you have a house of gold or you ascend into the sky, and we will not believe in your ascension until you send down to us a book we can read,' and with what He mentioned about the Jews in His saying: 'The People of the Book ask you to send down to them a book from the sky; they asked Moses for something greater than that and said: Show us Allah openly,' along with what the people of atheism and denial have of argumentation and obstinacy. So how could all of these be ignorant and not remind one another of it, except due to the ignorance of the questioner about this?
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector claims that the prophet (peace be upon him) cannot stand and is a liar, and that even deficient children know this, so how much more so the intelligent Quraysh? The response points out that Allah described the Quraysh as a contentious people who demanded specific miracles from the prophet, and Allah responded that He does not send signs except that earlier peoples denied them. Then it mentions the extensive demands from the Jews, including asking for a book from heaven and asking to see Allah openly. The conclusion is a rhetorical question: if all these intelligent people were not ignorant of the prophet's ability, then the questioner must be the ignorant one. The argument uses the opponent's own acknowledged intelligence against them.

Misconception: That the Prophet could not produce miracles because if he could, the intelligent Quraysh would have acknowledged him.
Correction: The Quraysh did acknowledge his miracles but were contentious, demanding specific signs, and Allah declined to send them because earlier peoples had denied similar signs.

Checkpoint

A) He is unable to stand and is a liar.
B) He is a magician.

Key Takeaway
The objector's argument is self-defeating because the very people he cites as intelligent demanded more signs, not less.

?

?
The Quraysh and Jews demanded specific miracles, yet they were not convinced. Is there a sign you are waiting for before you fully commit to Allah? Examine your heart: are you using intellect as a shield against faith?
?
This passage shows that even the most intelligent people can be blinded by obstinacy. In what areas of your life might you be demanding proof from Allah while ignoring the clear signs He has already sent? Repent and ask for guidance.

Why Sorcerers and Physicians Did Not Oppose Moses and Jesus
Baqillani argues that opponents' abstention is due to inability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the failure of sorcerers and physicians to oppose the miracles of Moses and Jesus proves their inability, not their choice.

Core Idea
Opponents' silence is not choice but inability.

In this passage, Baqillani directly challenges Jewish and Christian objectors who question the prophetic miracles. He argues that if the magicians and doctors could have produced similar miracles to discredit Moses and Jesus, they would have. Their abstention proves they were unable. This is a powerful theological argument that turns the opponents' silence into evidence for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let Baqillani's rhetorical style sink in before analyzing.
Notice the structure: a direct question to the opponent.
2
Identify the rhetorical challenge
Baqillani asks why the opponent does not accept that the sorcerers and doctors were unable to oppose. Understand the implied alternative: they could have but did not.
3
Understand the argument’s force
The inability of opponents supports the authenticity of miracles. If they could have imitated, they would have; their silence is evidence of divine origin.
The phrase 'ولا جواب عن ذلك أبداً' shows the argument is meant to be decisive.
4
Reflect on the opponent’s dilemma
Consider why there is no possible answer. This shows how Baqillani uses logic to defend miracles.
This argument counters skepticism about prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال للسائل عن هذا من اليهود والنصارى : فما أنكرتم ألا يكون إضراب السحرة والأطباء عن معارضة موسى وعيسى في آياتهما لعجزهم عن ذلك وإنما صرفوا عنه لذهابهم في النظر في أن معارضتهما تؤدي إلى تكذيبهما؟ ولا جواب عن ذلك أبداً.
And it is said to the questioner about this from the Jews and Christians: Why do you not deny that the abstention of the sorcerers and physicians from opposing Moses and Jesus in their miracles is due to their inability to do so, and that they refrained only because they went into considering that opposing them would lead to declaring them liars? And there is no answer to that ever.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a direct response to a Jewish or Christian questioner. Baqillani argues that if the sorcerers and physicians could have opposed Moses and Jesus by matching their miracles, they would have done so to discredit them. The fact that they did not is proof that they were unable. Furthermore, their refraining was not due to a fear of contradicting their own beliefs but because they realized that opposing the prophets would actually prove the prophets' truth. The conclusion is decisive: there is no possible counterargument.

Key Terms

السحرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the sorcerers and physicians refrained out of respect for Moses and Jesus, or because they did not want to challenge them.
Correction: Baqillani argues that their abstention was due to inability ('لعجزهم عن ذلك'), not choice or respect. They would have opposed if they could.

Checkpoint
