The Quran as Universal Proof: Rational Argument for Non-Arabs
Baqillani responds to the objection that non-Arabs are not bound by the Quran's miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani argues that the Quran's miraculous nature serves as a proof even for those who do not directly witness its challenge, through historical and rational inference.

Core Idea
Non-Arabs can deduce the Quran's miracle by investigating the Arabs' failure to imitate it.

This lesson explores a key objection: How can the Quran be a proof for non-Arabs who don't understand Arabic? Imam Baqillani responds by showing that rational investigation of history leads to the same conclusion. We'll see how the challenge to the Arabs and their failure becomes a universal proof, just like the miracles of Moses and Jesus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the passage and note the objection: non-Arabs (Indians, Turks) do not directly know the Quran is a miracle, so how can it bind them?
The objection is at the beginning: 'If they say: How is the proof of the Quran binding upon the Indians and Turks...'
2
Understand the rational inference
The answer explains that non-Arabs can investigate and learn that the Arabs were the most eloquent, had every motive to refute the Prophet, knew him intimately, yet failed to imitate the Quran. This rational knowledge suffices.
Key points: Arab eloquence, enmity, familiarity with the Prophet, and his lack of prior literacy.
3
Compare with earlier prophets
Notice the analogy with Moses and Jesus: even non-sorcerers and non-physicians accept their miracles because they know experts were challenged and failed. This shows the pattern of universal proof through historical investigation.
This strengthens the argument by showing consistency in how miracles are proven.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: كيف لزمت حجة القرآن الهند والترك وهم لا يعرفون أن ما أتى به معجز؟ قيل لهم : من حيث إنهم إذا فتشوا علموا أن العرب الذين بعث فيهم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كانوا أفصح الناس وأقدرهم على نظم الكلام العربي وأنهم النهاية في هذا الباب وأنهم أحرص الناس على تكذيبه عليه السلام وأنه نشأ وأنهم يعرفون دخیلهته وأهل مجالسته في ظعنه وإقامته وأنه ما كان يتلو من قبله من كتاب ولا يخطه بيمينه وأنه مع ذلك كله أجمع تحداهم بمثله أو بسورة من مثله مجتمعين أو مفترقين فعجزوا عن ذلك أجمع كما أن حجة موسى وعيسى عليهما السلام قائمة على من ليس بساحر ولا طبيب لعلمه بأنهما تحديا أطب الناس وأعظمهم سحراً بمثل ما أتيا به فعجزوا عن ذلك مع الحرص على تكذيبهما والإتيان بمثل ما أتيا به.
If they say: How is the proof of the Quran binding upon the Indians and Turks, while they do not know that what he brought is a miracle? It is said to them: In that if they investigate, they come to know that the Arabs among whom the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, was sent were the most eloquent of people and the most capable of composing Arabic speech, and that they were the ultimate in this field, and that they were the most eager of people to deny him, peace be upon him, and that he grew up among them, and they knew his secrets and the people of his company in his travels and residence, and that he had not recited before it any book nor written it with his right hand, and that despite all that, he challenged them collectively and individually with something like it or a chapter like it, and they were unable to do so entirely. Similarly, the proof of Moses and Jesus, peace be upon them, is established upon those who are neither sorcerers nor physicians, because they know that they challenged the most skilled people and the greatest sorcerers with something like what they brought, and they were unable, despite eagerness to deny them and to produce something like what they brought.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage answers the objection that non-Arabs (e.g., Indians, Turks) cannot be bound by the Quran's miracle because they do not directly witness its challenge. The response is that they can investigate and rationally deduce the miracle: they learn that the Arabs were the foremost experts in Arabic eloquence, had every motive to refute the Prophet (hatred, familiarity with him), and yet they failed to produce anything like the Quran. This parallels the miracles of Moses and Jesus: even non-sorcerers and non-physicians accept those miracles because they know that experts were challenged and failed. Thus, the Quran's proof is universal through historical and rational inference.

Key Terms
حجة
القرآن
غير العرب
تحدي
عجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's miracle is only a proof for Arabs or Arabic speakers.
Correction: Baqillani argues that non-Arabs can rationally infer its miraculous nature by investigating the historical challenge and failure of the Arabs, making it a universal proof.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani argue that the Quran is a proof for non-Arabs like Indians and Turks?
A) They must learn Arabic to understand it.
B) They can investigate and learn that the Arabs, despite their eloquence and enmity, were unable to imitate the Quran.
C) The Quran was translated into their languages.
D) Non-Arabs are not required to accept the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's proof is not limited to direct witnesses; it extends to all people through rational historical inference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever taken the time to investigate the historical circumstances of the Quran's revelation as Baqillani suggests—or do you rely on faith alone, without rational inquiry?
?
If you were a non-Arab living far from the Arabian Peninsula, would your conviction in the Quran be based on this chain of reasoning from failure to imitate? If not, what would you fall back on?
?
The Arabs who failed to produce a like chapter knew the Prophet intimately. You also know his biography and the Quran’s challenge. What does your inability to accept this rationally say about your own sincerity in seeking truth?

The Quran's Proof is Binding on Non-Arabs
Baqillani argues that non-Arabs are bound by the Quran's miracle through logical deduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani argues that non-Arabs are rationally bound by the Quran's miraculous nature through logical deduction.

Core Idea
The Quran's miracle is proven through reason, not just Arabic fluency.

Baqillani addresses a critical objection: how can non-Arabs, who do not understand Arabic, be obligated to accept the Quran as a miracle? He argues that through investigation, they can deduce its miraculous character by observing the failure of the most eloquent Arabs to meet its challenge. This lesson unpacks this logical argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Objection
Start by reading the objection: non-Arabs do not directly know that the Quran is a miracle. Notice the phrasing 'how did the proof become binding on Indians and Turks?'
This sets up the problem.
2
Understand the Answer
Baqillani explains that non-Arabs, upon investigation, come to know that the Arabs were the most eloquent and yet failed the Quranic challenge. This knowledge makes the proof binding.
Key point: investigation leads to certainty.
3
Study the Analogy
The passage draws an analogy with the miracles of Moses and Jesus. Their miracles were binding on non-sorcerers and non-physicians because they challenged the experts who failed.
Analogies strengthen the argument.
4
Reflect on the Logic
Consider how this argument establishes that the Quran's miracle is a proof for all people, not just Arabs. Reason bridges the gap.
The conclusion: the miracle is universal through rational inference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في لزوم حجة القرآن عند غير العرب
فإن قالوا : كيف لزمت حجة القرآن الهند والترك وهم لا يعرفون أن ما أتى به معجز؟ قيل لهم : من حيث إنهم إذا فتشوا علموا أن العرب الذين بعث فيهم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كانوا أفصح الناس وأقدرهم على نظم الكلام العربي وأنهم النهاية في هذا الباب وأنهم أحرص الناس على تكذيبه عليه السلام وأنه نشأ وأنهم يعرفون دَخِيلَته وأهل مجالسته في ظَعْنه وإقامته وأنه ما كان يتلو من قبله من كتاب ولا يخطه بيمينه وأنه مع ذلك كله أجمع تحداهم بمثله أو بسورة من مثله مجتمعين أو مفترقين فعجزوا عن ذلك أجمع كما أن حجة موسى وعيسى عليهما السلام قائمة على من ليس بساحر ولا طبيب لعلمه بأنهما تحديا أطب الناس وأعظمهم سحراً بمثل ما أتيا به فعجزوا عن ذلك مع الحرص على تكذيبهما والإتيان بمثل ما أتيا به.
Issue concerning the necessity of the proof of the Quran for non-Arabs. If they say: How did the proof of the Quran become binding on the Indians and Turks while they do not know that what he brought is a miracle? It is said to them: Because when they investigate, they know that the Arabs among whom the Prophet (peace be upon him) was sent were the most eloquent of people and the most capable of composing Arabic speech, and that they were the utmost in this field, and that they were the most eager to deny him (peace be upon him), and that he grew up among them and they knew his intimate affairs and the people of his company in his travels and his residence, and that he did not recite any book before it nor write it with his right hand, and that despite all that, he collectively challenged them with something like it or a sura like it, gathered or scattered, and they failed to do so collectively; just as the proof of Moses and Jesus (peace be upon them) is binding on whoever is not a sorcerer or physician, because he knows that they challenged the most skilled of people in medicine and the greatest of them in sorcery with something like what they brought, and they failed to do so despite their eagerness to deny them and to produce something like what they brought.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that the Quran's miraculous nature (i'jaz) is binding on non-Arabs who did not directly witness the challenge. The author first states the objection: how can the Quran be a proof for Indians and Turks who do not know that what the Prophet brought is a miracle? The answer is given through a logical deduction: these non-Arabs, upon investigation, come to know that the Arabs among whom the Prophet was sent were the most eloquent people and most capable of composing Arabic speech. They were the utmost in eloquence, and they were the most eager to deny the Prophet. They knew his background and his associates, and he was unlettered. Despite all this, he challenged them to produce something like the Quran or even a single sura, whether collectively or individually, and they failed. The author draws an analogy with the miracles of Moses and Jesus: their proof is binding on those who are not sorcerers or physicians because they know that the prophets challenged the most skilled in those arts and were unable to match them. Similarly, non-Arabs can reason that since the most eloquent Arabs failed to match the Quran, it is a miracle binding on all people.

إعجاز

معجزة

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The miracle is binding on all people through rational deduction from historical facts.

Key Takeaway
Non-Arabs are bound by the Quran's miracle because reason shows that the most eloquent Arabs failed to match it.

Refutation of Musaylima's Alleged Counter-Quran
Baqillani refutes the claim that Musaylima's speech is a valid counter-Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani dismisses Musaylima's alleged counter-Quran as invalid and what the criterion for a true miraculous challenge is.

Core Idea
A true counter-Quran must be taken seriously; Musaylima's speech was too contemptible to even be a challenge.

Baqillani addresses a common objection: if someone claims that Musaylima produced a counter to the Quran, what makes the Quran unique? He examines the actual content of Musaylima's supposed 'verses' and shows that they are not even good poetry, let alone a miracle. The key argument is historical: if it were a real challenge, the Arabs would have jumped on it, but no one did.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
The objector cites Musaylima's absurd lines to suggest that the Quran could be imitated. Recognize this as a potential challenge to the doctrine of Quranic inimitability.
Musaylima's lines are intentionally ridiculous to make the point.
2
Analyze Baqillani's Refutation
Notice how Baqillani first dismisses the speech as weak and foolish rhymed prose, then points out that it doesn't even rise to the level of decent poetry. He provides a poetic example to show it's not special.
Baqillani quotes a poet to show that even weak poetry is better.
3
Grasp the Historical Argument
The strongest proof is that if this speech were miraculous, the Arabs and apostates would have used it against the Prophet. The fact that no one did shows it was not a real challenge.
This is the crux of the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في معارضة مسيلمة للقرآن
فإن قال قائل : ما أنكرتم أن يكون مسيلمة قد عارض القرآن وقابله بقوله : «يا ضِفْدَعُ بِنْتُ ضِفْدَعَيْن، يقي فَكُمْ تنقين، لا الماءَ تُغيرين ولا نِقّي الشَّارِبَ تَمنَعِين»، وقوله : «والزَّارِعاتِ زَرْعاً، فالحاصدَاتِ حَصْداً، والطَّاحِنَاتِ طَحْناً»، وأمثال ذلك من الكلام الركيك السخيف؟ قيل له : هذا الكلام دال على جهل مُورِدِه وضعف عقله ورأيه وما يُوجِبُ السخرية منه والهز به وليس هو مع ذلك خارجاً عن وزن ركيك السجع وسخيفه، وما زاد على ذلك قليلاً خرج إلى وزن الشعر كقول بعضهم في شعره : «وقرا معلناً ليصدع قلبي والهوى يصدع الفؤاد السقيما أرأيت الذي يكذب بالدين فذاك الذي يدع اليتيما» وعلى أن هذا الكلام لو كان معجزاً لتعلقت العرب وأهل الرّدة به ولعرف أتباع النبي صلى الله عليه أنه عروض له ولَوقَعَ لهم العلم اليقين بأنه قد قوبل، وفي عدم ذلك دليل على جهل مدعى ذلك وعلى أن مسيلمة لم يدع هذا الكلام معجزاً ولا تَحَدَّى العَرَبَ بمثله فعجزوا عنه بل كان في نفسه ونفس كل سامع له أخَف وأسخف وأذل أن يتعلق به ولذلك لا نجد له نباً ولا أحداً من العرب تعلق به.
Issue concerning Musaylima's countering of the Quran. If a questioner says: What prevents you from [accepting] that Musaylima countered the Quran and matched it with his saying: 'O frog, daughter of two frogs, ...[ unclear ]... you croak, you do not change the water and you do not prevent the drinker from drinking,' and his saying: 'By those who sow sowing, and those who reap reaping, and those who grind grinding,' and similar examples of weak and foolish speech? It is said to him: This speech indicates the ignorance of its producer and the weakness of his intellect and opinion, and it necessitates mockery of him and jesting with him, and moreover it does not go beyond the weight of weak and foolish rhymed prose, and what increases a little beyond that goes into the weight of poetry, like the saying of some in his poetry: 'And he recited publicly to split my heart, and desire splits the sick heart; have you seen the one who denies the religion? That is the one who repels the orphan.' And it is also [argued] that if this speech were miraculous, the Arabs and apostates would have clung to it, and the followers of the Prophet (peace be upon him) would have known that it was a counter to him, and certain knowledge would have occurred to them that it had been matched. The absence of that is evidence of the ignorance of the claimant and that Musaylima did not claim this speech as miraculous nor challenge the Arabs with its like so that they failed; rather, in his own estimation and in the estimation of every hearer, it was too contemptible, foolish, and base to be clung to. For that reason we find no report of him nor any Arab clinging to it.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector raises the case of Musaylima, who allegedly produced a counter-Quran with absurd lines about frogs and farming, claiming this undermines the uniqueness of the Quran. Baqillani's answer first dismisses the speech as showing the ignorance and foolishness of its author; it is not even good rhymed prose, and at best it approaches the level of weak poetry, as illustrated by a verse from a poet who mocks religious denial. The key point is that if such speech were truly miraculous, it would have been taken seriously: the Arabs and apostates would have used it against the Prophet, and the Prophet's followers would have known it was a valid counter. Since no such thing happened, it proves that Musaylima himself did not present it as a miracle nor challenge the Arabs with it. The speech was inherently contemptible and no one considered it a valid challenge.

ركيك
سخيف

Misconception: Any attempt to imitate the Quran, even an absurd one like Musaylima's, disproves its inimitability.
Correction: Baqillani argues that only a serious, widely-recognized challenge would count; Musaylima's speech was too contemptible to be taken as a real counter.

B) It was not in proper Arabic
C) No one, including the Arabs and apostates, treated it as a serious challenge or clung to it
D) It was revealed after the Prophet's death

Key Takeaway
Musaylima's alleged counter-Quran fails because it is ridiculously weak in quality and, more importantly, no one—not even his followers—treated it as a serious challenge to the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani points out that Musaylima's attempted counter was so contemptible that no one even bothered to treat it as a serious challenge. Is there any area of your life—a habit, a relationship, or a distraction—that you treat as harmless but that actually diminishes the honor you give to the Quran as the unmatched Word of God? Will you commit, starting today, to removing anything that lowers the Quran's status in your heart?
?
The historical absence of a credible counter to the Quran, even from its most bitter enemies, is a powerful proof of its divine origin. Have you ever truly let that silence settle into your soul? Do you live as if you believe that no speech can match it? Tonight, ask yourself: if the Quran is indeed from Allah, what must change in how I listen to it, read it, and obey it?
?

Are you sometimes troubled by weak criticisms of Islam, or do you feel the same contempt for them that Baqillani felt for the frog rhyme? What would it mean for you to have that kind of certainty in the Quran's miracle?

Refutation of Musaylimah's Alleged Miracle
Refutes Musaylimah's alleged miracle through argument and historical observation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Musaylimah's speech cannot be considered a miracle, based on its intrinsic weakness and the absence of recognition from Arabs and the Prophet's followers.

Core Idea
True miracles are recognized by their effect; feeble speech attracts no followers.

Imam Baqillani addresses a potential objection: could Musaylimah's rhyming prose be considered a miracle like the Quran? He quotes examples of its crudeness and argues that such speech is too contemptible to be divine. Then he presents a theological argument: if it were truly miraculous, the Arabs would have recognized it and the Prophet's followers would have known of a successful challenge. This lesson unpacks his refutation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the two quoted examples of Musaylimah's speech.
2
Analyze the critique of Musaylimah's speech
Identify how Baqillani describes the speech as weak, foolish, and inviting mockery. Understand his classification of it as poor saj' (rhymed prose) and near-poetry.
The author even cites a clumsy poem to show what exceeds saj' slightly.
3
Understand the theological argument about recognition
Grasp the conditional: if this speech were a miracle, the Arabs and apostates would have clung to it, and the Prophet's followers would have known a counter-challenge occurred. Since none of that happened, it proves the speech was not a miracle.
This is a key refutation based on historical outcome.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Note the final point: Musaylimah never claimed this speech as a miracle or challenged the Arabs with it. It was too contemptible for anyone to take seriously, and no historical reports show it attracted followers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقوله : «يا ضِفْدَعُ بِنْتُ ضِفْدَعَيْن، يقي فَكُمْ تنقين، لا الماءَ تُغيرين ولا نِقّي الشَّارِبَ تَمنَعِين»، وقوله : والزَّارِعاتِ زَرْعاً، فالحاصدَاتِ حَصْداً، والطَّاحِنَاتِ طَحْناً ) ، وأمثال ذلك من الكلام الركيك السخيف؟ قيل له : هذا الكلام دال على جهل مُورِدِه وضعف عقله ورأيه وما يُوجِبُ السخرية منه والهزة منه والهزّ به وليس هو مع ذلك خارجاً عن وزن ركيك السجع وسخيفه، وما زاد على ذلك قليلاً خرج إلى وزن الشعر كقول بعضهم في شعره : وقَرا معلناً ليصدع قلبي والهوى يصدع الفؤاد السقيما أرأيت الذي يكذب بالدين فذاك الذي يدع اليتيما. وعلى أن هذا الكلام لو كان معجزاً لتعلقت العرب وأهل الرّدة به ولعرف أتباع النبي صلى الله عليه أنه عروض له ولَوقَعَ لهم العِلْمُ اليقين بأنه قد قوبل، وفي عدم ذلك دليل على جهل مدعى ذلك وعلى أن مسيلمة لم يدع هذا الكلام معجزاً ولا تَحَدَّى العَرَبَ بمثله فعجزوا عنه بل كان في نفسه ونفس كل سامع له أخَفٌ وأسخف وأذل أن يتعلق به ولذلك لا نجد له نباً ولا أحداً من العرب تعلق به.
By his saying: 'O frog, daughter of two frogs, how much you croak, you do not change the water, nor do you prevent the drinker from drinking,' and his saying: 'And the sowers sowing, then the reapers reaping, then the grinders grinding,' and similar examples of weak, foolish speech? It was said to him: This speech indicates the ignorance of its author, the weakness of his intellect and opinion, and it necessitates mockery of him and contempt for him, and it is not beyond the measure of weak and foolish saj' (rhymed prose). And what exceeds that a little goes into the meter of poetry, like the saying of some of them in his poetry: 'And he recited openly to split my heart, and passion splits the sick heart; have you seen the one who denies the religion? That is the one who repels the orphan.' And further, if this speech were miraculous, the Arabs and the apostates would have clung to it, and the followers of the Prophet (peace be upon him) would have known that he had been opposed, and they would have obtained certain knowledge that it had been countered. In the absence of that is proof of the ignorance of the claimant and that Musaylimah did not claim this speech as a miracle nor challenge the Arabs with its like so that they failed against it. Rather, in itself and in the view of every hearer, it was too light, too foolish, and too contemptible to cling to. Therefore, we find no news of him, and no Arab clung to it.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and answer to an implied objection: that Musaylimah's speech could be considered a miracle like the Quran. The author first quotes examples of Musaylimah's crude rhyming prose – addressing a frog and absurd agricultural sequences – and declares it weak and foolish. He then states the response to anyone who might argue for its miraculousness: such speech proves the ignorance and weak intellect of its author; it invites mockery and contempt. It does not even exceed the level of poor rhymed prose (saj'); if it rises slightly, it falls into clumsy verse. The author then cites a couplet that is similarly feeble. Next, he makes a theological argument: if this speech were truly a miracle, the Arabs (including those who apostatized) would have accepted it, and the Prophet's followers would have known for certain that a counter-challenge had occurred. Since no such recognition happened, it is clear that the claimant is ignorant and that Musaylimah never intended this as a miracle or challenge. On the contrary, the speech was so trivial and contemptible that no one took it seriously. The passage ends by noting the historical fact that no report of this speech attracted any followers.

?
Musaylimah's speech was too contemptible to attract followers. Think about the influences in your daily life – from media, friends, or even religious figures. Is there something you are clinging to that, like Musaylimah's speech, is lightweight and empty when tested against the truth? What would it cost you to let it go?
?
The author uses the historical observation that no one followed Musaylimah's speech as proof of its falsity. This is a sobering reminder that truth bears witness to itself. In your own life, are there areas where you have ignored clear evidence – from the Quran, from sound reasoning, or from the example of the Prophet – because following the truth would be uncomfortable? What step will you take today to align your actions with what you know to be true?

How We Know the Prophet's Challenge
Baqillani answers how the Prophet's challenge is known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the twofold basis for knowing the Prophet's challenge to produce similar speech: necessary knowledge and explicit Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The Prophet's challenge is known necessarily, not merely from reports.

This lesson addresses a fundamental question about the Quran's miraculous nature: how do we know the Prophet (PBUH) actually challenged the Arabs to produce something like it? Imam Baqillani provides a robust answer that combines intuitive certainty with textual evidence, and then cleverly turns the question back on those who object. By the end, you'll see why the challenge is undeniable.

Guided Path
1
Ponder the question
The passage begins with a hypothetical objection: 'From where is it known that the Prophet challenged the Arabs?' Consider why this question might arise, especially from non-Muslims.
2
Understand the first answer: necessary knowledge
Baqillani argues that the challenge is known necessarily (iḍṭirārī) from the Prophet's religion and statements, akin to knowing the Prophet's existence or the Quran itself. Reflect on what makes something 'necessarily known.'
This is a key concept in Islamic epistemology.
3
See the second answer: Quranic verses
The author then cites explicit verses of challenge (2:23 and 17:88) and notes the connection to 'calling witnesses' (2:23). Notice how these verses leave no excuse.
The verses quoted are the ultimate challenge and reprimand.
4
Follow the rebuttal
Baqillani turns the question on Jews, Christians, and Zoroastrians: how do they know their prophets issued similar challenges? Any answer they give applies equally to Islam.
This argument neutralizes the objection without relying on special pleading.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل من أهل الملل وغيرهم : من أين يُعْلَمُ أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم تحدى العرب أن تأتي بمثله وطالبهم بذلك؟ قيل لهم : يُعلم ذلك اضطراراً من دينه وقوله كما نعلم وجوده وظهوره وكما نعلمُ وجود القرآن نفسه اضطراراً؛ هذا على أنه في نص التلاوة نحو قوله : فأتوا بسورة من مثله، و قل لئن اجتمعت الانس والجن على أن يأتوا بمثل هذا القرآن لا يأتون بمثله، وهذا غاية التحدي والتقريع؛ وقد وصل قوله : ( فأتوا بسورة من مثله بقوله : وادعوا شهداءكم من دون الله )؛ فلا مُتَعَلَّقَ لأحد في هذا الباب. ويُقلب السؤال على من سأل عنه من اليهود والنصارى والمجوس المدعين لنبوة زَرَادَشت فيقال لهم : من أين علمتم أن موسى وعيسى وزَرَادَشْتْ تحدوا قومهم بمثل شيء مما أتوا به؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون ذلك قد ظهر من غير احتجاج منهم ولا تحدٍ إلى مثله؟ فكل شيء تعلقوا به فهو جوابنا عما سألوا عنه.
If a questioner from among the people of religions or others says: 'From where is it known that the Prophet (peace be upon him) challenged the Arabs to produce its like and demanded that of them?' It is said to them: That is known necessarily from his religion and his statement, just as we know his existence and his emergence, and just as we know the existence of the Quran itself necessarily. This, besides the fact that in the recited text there is like His saying: 'Then bring a surah like it,' and 'Say: If mankind and jinn gathered together to produce the like of this Quran, they could not produce its like,' and this is the utmost challenge and reprimand. And He connected His saying 'Then bring a surah like it' with His saying 'and call your witnesses besides God.' So there is no ground for anyone in this matter. And the question is turned back on whoever asks about it from the Jews, Christians, and Magians who claim prophethood for Zoroaster. It is said to them: From where did you know that Moses, Jesus, and Zoroaster challenged their peoples with something like what they brought? And why do you deny that this could have appeared without any argument from them or challenge to its like? For everything they cling to is our answer to what they asked about.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is an answer to the question: 'How do we know that the Prophet (PBUH) issued a challenge to the Arabs to produce a text like the Quran?' The author gives a twofold answer. First, this knowledge is 'iḍṭirārī' (necessary, self-evident) from the Prophet's religion and his statement – that is, it is so well-known and widespread that it is akin to knowing the Prophet's own existence and the existence of the Quran itself. Second, the challenge is explicitly stated in the Quranic text: verses 2:23 ('Fa'tū bi sūratin min mithlih') and 17:88 ('Qul la-in ijtama'at...'), which are the ultimate challenge and rebuke. The author notes that the first verse is connected to 'wa-d'ū shuhadā'akum min dūni llāh', leaving no excuse. After establishing the proof, the author turns the argument on its head: he asks the objector (whether Jew, Christian, or Zoroastrian) how they know that their own prophets issued similar challenges. If they claim that the challenge is known from scripture or tradition, the author says that same line of reasoning applies to Islam. Thus, the objection is neutralized.

Key Terms
اضطرار
تحدي
تلاوة
تقريع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the challenge is only known from transmitted reports (khabar), not from necessary knowledge.
Correction: Baqillani argues it is known necessarily (iḍṭirārī) from the Prophet's manifest religion and the widespread nature of the challenge.

Checkpoint
How does the author establish that the Prophet (PBUH) challenged the Arabs?
A) By citing consensus of scholars.
B) By arguing it is known necessarily from his religion and from explicit Quranic verses.
C) By pointing to the fact that no one produced a rival text.
D) By relying on the testimony of the Prophet's companions.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's challenge to produce similar speech is known necessarily and from the Quran itself, leaving no room for doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you personally experience the Quran's challenge as a pressing, undeniable reality that demands your response, or have you reduced it to a historical event that doesn't touch your life today?
?
If someone asked you tomorrow, 'How do you know the Prophet really challenged the Arabs?', would your answer be based on second-hand information, or on a deep certainty that you feel in your bones?
?
The author says the challenge is known 'necessarily'—like knowing the sun is bright. Is your faith in the Quran's challenge that immediate and certain, or have you let doubts creep in that you've never confronted?

Refuting the Claim of Producing a Comparable Text
Baqillani refutes the argument that anyone could produce a text equal to the Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the claim that anyone could produce a text like the Qur'an, and why the temporary prevention of opposition is still a valid miracle.

Core Idea
The inimitability of the Qur'an is proven by the inability of the most eloquent Arabs.

This passage presents an objection: someone might claim to have composed speech equal to the Qur'an in style and prosody. Baqillani responds by asserting that we can recognize the difference, and the historical inability of the Arabs—the pinnacle of eloquence—proves the Qur'an's uniqueness. He then explores two theological explanations for how the miracle worked, showing that both are valid and do not diminish the miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial response
Begin by reading the full passage to grasp the objection and Baqillani's immediate answer. Notice that he claims we can know a parallel is not like the Qur'an by comparing it to the original.
The objection is phrased as a question from hypothetical opponents.
2
Understand the Arabs' inability as evidence
Focus on the part where Baqillani cites the Arabs' inability to oppose the Qur'an. They were the most eloquent people, so their failure is a strong proof of the Qur'an's uniqueness.
3
Examine the two theological positions
Identify the two views: one says God prevented the Arabs only during the challenge, the other says they were able before but were prevented at the time. Note that Baqillani considers both as valid explanations.
He does not endorse one over the other; both are acceptable.
4
Analyze the analogy of temporary prevention
Read the analogy of a prophet temporarily preventing his people from moving their hands. This illustrates that even temporary prevention is a genuine miracle and refutes any claim that the miracle is weakened.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : كيف تبطلون حجة من أتى بكلام منظوم وزعم أنه مِثْلُ القرآن وعَرُوضُه؟ قيل له : لعلمنا بأنه ليس بمثل له ولا من جنس نَظْمِه؛ فإن قَدَرَ على ذلك قادر فَلْيَأتِ به لنريه أنه خلاف له ونعلم ذلك بعجز العرب عن معارضة القرآن مع العلم بأنهم أفصح الفصحاء وأبلغ البلغاء أيضاً وأشعرُ وأَخْطَبُ من على وجه الأرض ممن تكلم بلسانهم بعدهم فتعلم بذلك تعذر معارضته على مَنْ بَعْدَهم وعلى أن من الناس مَنْ يزعم أن الله سبحانه إنما أعجز العَرَبَ أيضاً عن معارضته وقت التحدي بالإتيان بمثله لكي يَخْرِقَ بذلك العادة لصاحبه ويدل على صدقه وقد يجوز أن يُقدِرَهم بعد موت النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم على مثله . ومنهم أيضاً من يقول : قد كانت العرب قادرة قبل التحدي على الإتيان بمثله وإنما أعْجَزَهم الله سبحانه عن ذلك وقت تحدي الرسول صلّى الله عليه وسلم ونَقَضَ عادتهم ليدل على صدقه ولَعَمْرِي إن ذلك لو كان كذلك لكان آية عظيمة وخرقاً للعادة كما أن نبياً لو تَحَدَّى قومه بتحريك أيديهم والخروج عن أماكنهم إلى أقرب المواضع إليها فَمُنِعُوا القدرة على ذلك وقد اعتادوا الاقتدار عليه، ثم أقْدِرُوا عليه ثانية بعد تقضي تحديه لكان خرق العادة بإيجاد القدرة على ذلك وإعدامها على خلاف المُتعالَم المألوف آية عظيمة وحجة بينة فإذا كان ذلك كذلك سقط ما سألوا عنه
If they say: 'How do you invalidate the argument of one who brings composed speech and claims it is like the Qur'an and its prosody?' It is said to him: 'Because we know that it is not like it nor of the same genre as its composition; for if someone is able to do that, let him bring it so that we may show him that it is different from it, and we know that by the inability of the Arabs to oppose the Qur'an, despite the knowledge that they were the most eloquent of the eloquent and the most eloquent of the eloquent also, and the most poetic and the most oratorical on the face of the earth among those who spoke in their language after them. So by that it is known that opposing it is impossible for those after them. And among people are those who claim that God, exalted is He, only made the Arabs unable to oppose it at the time of the challenge by bringing its like in order to break through that the custom for His companion and to indicate his truthfulness, and it is permissible that He might enable them after the death of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, to produce its like. And among them also are those who say: 'The Arabs were able before the challenge to produce its like, and God only made them unable to do that at the time of the Prophet's challenge, may God bless him and grant him peace, and broke their custom to indicate his truthfulness.' And by my life, if that were so, it would be a great sign and a breaking of custom, just as if a prophet challenged his people to move their hands and leave their places to the nearest locations, and they were prevented from having the power to do that while they were accustomed to having power over it, then they were empowered again after the conclusion of his challenge—that would be a breaking of custom by bringing into existence power over that and removing it contrary to the customary and familiar, a great sign and a clear proof. So if that is the case, what they asked about falls away.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument concerning the possibility of producing a text comparable to the Qur'an. Baqillani presents the objection: someone claims to have composed speech that matches the Qur'an in style and prosody. The answer is that we know it is not like the Qur'an because the Arabs—the most eloquent and poetic people—were unable to oppose it, and this inability is observable. Even if someone claims to have produced a parallel, we can examine it and see the difference. Baqillani then discusses two theological positions regarding the nature of the miracle. The first holds that God made the Arabs unable only during the time of the challenge, breaking their custom, and He could have enabled them after the Prophet's death. The second holds that the Arabs were naturally able before the challenge, but God prevented them at the time of the challenge. Baqillani argues that both positions are valid and that even if the second were true, it would still be a great miracle. He gives an analogy: a prophet who temporarily prevents his people from moving their hands (something they normally can do) and then restores their ability—this is still a clear miracle and proof of prophethood. Therefore, the objection that the inability to oppose is not a true miracle is refuted; it is a genuine breaking of customary norms (kharq al-ʿāda).

Key Terms
معارضة
إعجاز
خرق العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God could have enabled the Arabs to oppose the Qur'an after the challenge, the miracle is weakened.
Correction: Baqillani shows that temporary prevention is still a true miracle, as illustrated by the analogy of hand movement. The miracle lies in the suspension of normal ability, regardless of duration.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani respond to the claim that someone could produce speech equal to the Qur'an?
A) He says such speech is impossible because the Arabs were incapable of it
B) He says it is possible but not actually produced
C) He says the claim is irrelevant because the Qur'an is unique in meaning
D) He says the Qur'an is not speech but the word of God

Key Takeaway
The inimitability of the Qur'an is a proven miracle, and the theological debate about how God prevented opposition does not undermine its miraculous nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever treated the Qur'an as an ordinary book, forgetting that the most eloquent Arabs could not produce its like? How does this truth demand a change in how you approach it daily?
?
Baqillani shows that even temporary prevention is a clear miracle. Do you sometimes think that the Qur'an's miraculous nature is only theoretical? What would it take for you to feel its power in your heart right now?
?
The inability of the Arabs is a historical proof—but what about your own inability to live by the Qur'an perfectly? Does this lesson expose any excuse you have made for not submitting fully to its authority? What will you do about it today?

The Qur'an's Predictions of the Unseen
Baqillani lists examples of Qur'anic predictions and argues they prove divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an's accurate predictions of future events serve as a proof of its divine origin.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's news of the unseen is a miracle that cannot be attributed to human guesswork.

After establishing the linguistic miracle of the Qur'an, Baqillani now turns to another dimension of its inimitability: its predictions of future events. He provides several historical examples where the Qur'an made specific claims about the future that were later fulfilled exactly, demonstrating that such knowledge could only come from the Knower of the Unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the examples
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting each prediction Baqillani mentions: the conquest of Mecca, the defeat of the coalition, the triumph of Islam, the caliphate of the believers, the Jews' refusal to wish for death, the Christians' avoidance of mubāhala, and the Romans' victory.
These are all events that the Prophet could not have known by natural means.
2
Understand the argument from consistency
Notice that Baqillani emphasizes that all these predictions came true without any error. He argues that such consistent accuracy cannot be achieved by chance or guesswork.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that these predictions must come from Allah, the Knower of the Unseen. This reinforces the Qur'an's claim to be divine revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في وجوه الإعجاز
فإن قال قائل : فهل في القرآن وجه من وجوه الإعجاز غير ما ذكرتموه من بديع نظمه وعجيب رصفه وتأليفه ؟ قيل له : أجل، فيه وجهان آخران من وجوه الإعجاز.
أحدهما ما انطوى عليه من أخبار الغُيوب التي يعلم كل عاقل عَجْزَ الخلق عن معرفتها والتوصل إلى إدراكها نحو قوله : لتدخلن المسجد الحرام إن شاء الله آمنين محلقين رؤوسكم ومقصرين لا تخافون، فدخلوه كما وعدهم وأخبرهم ومن ذلك قوله تعالى : سيهزم الجمع ويولون الدبر فكان ذلك كما أخبر وقد وقوله : ليظهره على الدين كله ولو كره المشركون أظهره وأعلى دَعْوَتَه وأذل المُلوك المحاولة لأبطاله التي كانت حول صاحب الدعوة إليه وقوله تعالى : وعد الله الذين آمنوا منكم وعملوا الصالحات ليستخلفنهم في الأرض كما استخلف الذين من قبلهم . وكان من ذلك ما وعدهم الله واستخلف الأربعة الأئمة الخلفاء الراشدين .
وقوله لليهود : قل إن كانت لكم الدار الآخرة عند الله خالصة من دون الناس فتمنوا الموت إن كنتم صادقين ولن يتمنوه أبداً بما قدمت أيديهم فأخبر أنهم إن تمنوا الموت ماتوا وأنهم لن يتمنوه فلم يتمنوه على ما أخبر به علماً منهم بصدقه وأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا لا محالة .
وكذلك امتنع النصارى عن مباهلته عند دعائه لهم إليها ومطالبته بها في قوله تعالى : فقل تعالوا ندع ابناءنا وأبناءكم ونساءنا ونساءكم وأنفسنا وأنفسكم ثم نبتهل فنجعل لعنة الله على الكاذبين فامتنعوا عن المباهلة خوفاً من النكال وأليم العقاب وأن ما ينزل بهم توعدهم به ؛ وليس ذلك إلا لعلمهم بصدقه وثبوت نبوته ومن أخبار الغيوب قوله تعالى : الم غلبت الروم في أدنى الأرض وهم من بعد غلبهم سيغلبون ؛ فغلبت الرومُ فارس في بضع السنين كما أخبر نظائر هذا مما يكثر تتبعه واتفاق الصواب في هذا أجمع على سبيل التخمين والظن ممتنع متعذر فدل ذلك على أنه من أخبار علام الغيوب سبحانه
والوجه الآخر ما عليه القرآن من قصص الأولين وسير الماضين وأحاديث المتقدمين وذكر ما شَجَرَ بينهم وكان في أعصارهم مما لا يجوز حصول علمه إلا لمن كَثُر لقاؤه لأهل السِّير ودَرْسُه لها وعنايته بها ومجالسته لأهلها وكان ممن يتلو الكتب ويستخرجها مع العلم بأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يكن يتلو كتاباً ولا يَخُطُه بيمينه وأنه لم يكن ممن يُعْرَفُ بدراسة الكتب
A question concerning the aspects of inimitability. If a questioner says: Is there in the Qur'an an aspect of inimitability other than what you have mentioned of its marvelous composition (badīʿ naẓmihi), wondrous arrangement (ʿajīb raṣfihi) and structure (taʾlīfihi)? It is said to him: Yes, there are two other aspects of inimitability. One of them is what it contains of news of the unseen (akhbār al-ghuyūb) which every rational person knows is beyond the capacity of creation to know or attain. For example, His saying: 'You will enter the Sacred Mosque, if Allah wills, in safety, with your heads shaved and hair shortened, not fearing' — and they entered it just as He promised and informed them. And of that is His saying, exalted: 'The assembly will be defeated and they will turn their backs' — and it happened as He informed. And His saying: 'He will make it prevail over all religion, even if the polytheists dislike it' — He made it prevail and elevated His call and humiliated the kings who attempted to nullify it who were around the claimant of the message. And His saying, exalted: 'Allah has promised those among you who believe and do righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession on the earth just as He granted succession to those before them' — and of that was what Allah promised them, and He granted succession to the four rightly guided caliphs (al-khulafāʾ al-rāshidīn). And His saying to the Jews: 'Say: If the Final Abode with Allah is exclusively for you, excluding the people, then wish for death if you are truthful. But they will never wish for it, because of what their hands have sent forth' — He informed that if they wished for death they would die, and that they will never wish for it, so they did not wish for it, in accordance with what He informed, as they knew of his truthfulness, and that if they wished for death they would inevitably die. Likewise, the Christians refrained from invoking curses (mubāhala) when he called them to it and demanded it in His saying, exalted: 'Say: Come, let us call our sons and your sons, our women and your women, ourselves and yourselves, then invoke and lay the curse of Allah upon the liars' — so they refrained from the mubāhala for fear of punishment and painful torment, and that what he threatened them with would descend upon them; and that is only because of their knowledge of his truthfulness and the establishment of his prophethood. And among the news of the unseen is His saying, exalted: 'Alif Lam Mim. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, but they, after their defeat, will be victorious' — so the Romans defeated Persia within a few years, as He informed. The like of this is many to follow, and agreement of correctness in all of this by way of conjecture and guesswork is impossible and unattainable. This indicates that it is from the news of the Knower of the Unseen (ʿallām al-ghuyūb), exalted is He. The other aspect is what the Qur'an contains of stories of the ancients (qiṣaṣ al-awwalīn), biographies of the past, accounts of the predecessors, and mention of what occurred between them and was in their eras, knowledge of which is not attainable except for one who has frequently met the people of histories (sīra), studied them, took care with them, and sat with their people, and who was one who would read books and extract them — with the knowledge that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not read any book nor write it with his right hand, and he was not one known for studying books.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of two additional aspects of the Qur'an's inimitability (iʿjāz) beyond its linguistic composition. The author begins by acknowledging a potential question: are there other aspects of iʿjāz besides the marvelous arrangement? He answers affirmatively and enumerates two. The first aspect is predictions of the unseen (akhbār al-ghuyūb). These are events known only to God that the Prophet could not have known by natural means. Baqillani provides several examples: the promise that the companions would enter Mecca securely (fulfilled at the conquest); the prediction of defeat for the Meccan coalition at Badr (fulfilled); the prophecy that Islam would prevail over other religions (fulfilled historically); the promise of caliphate for the believers (fulfilled in the Rashidun caliphs); the challenge to the Jews to wish for death (they did not, confirming their own doubt); the avoidance of the Christians from the mubāhala (cursing) due to their fear of punishment; and the prophecy of the Romans' victory over Persia after their defeat (fulfilled within a few years). He argues that the consistent accuracy of these predictions, without any error, cannot be attributed to guesswork or coincidence, thus proving their source is the Knower of the Unseen. The second aspect is the Qur'an's detailed accounts of past nations and events—stories that require extensive study, old books, and oral tradition to know. Yet the Prophet Muhammad was unlettered (ummī), never having read or written any book, nor having studied with scholars of history. His accurate knowledge of such detailed stories, which he could not have acquired through normal means, is another proof of divine origin. This passage thus expands the concept of iʿjāz beyond the linguistic miracle to include prophetic foreknowledge and historical accuracy, both of which testify to the Qur'an's divine source.

Key Terms
إعجاز (iʿjāz)
أخبار الغيوب (akhbār al-ghuyūb)
مباهلة (mubāhala)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume the Qur'an's inimitability is only its Arabic eloquence.
Correction: This passage shows it also includes accurate predictions of the future, which cannot be replicated by humans.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, which of the following is an example of the Qur'an's prediction of the unseen (akhbār al-ghuyūb)?
A) The story of Joseph and his brothers
B) The prophecy that the Romans would defeat Persia after their own defeat
C) The description of heaven and hell
D) The laws of inheritance

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's accurate predictions of future events, which could not have been known by human means, are a clear proof of its divine origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Qur'an foretold specific events that came true exactly. You claim to believe, yet you live as if the Hereafter is uncertain. How does your daily life reflect that you truly believe the unseen news of the Qur'an? What is one habit you must change today to align your actions with that certainty?
?
The Jews and Christians avoided the challenge (wishing death or the mubahala) because they knew the truth in their hearts. Are there any clear commands or warnings in the Qur'an that you are avoiding facing, perhaps because you fear the change they demand? What is one such command, and what concrete step will you take this week to obey it?
?
If the Qur'an's predictions of the unseen prove it is from Allah, then every verse in it carries divine authority. Which prediction or promise in this passage strikes you most personally, and how does it expose a gap between your belief and your practice? What will you do today to close that gap?

The Qur'an's Accounts of Past Nations
Baqillani argues that the Qur'an's historical accounts, given the Prophet's illiteracy, constitute a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an's detailed stories of past nations, combined with the Prophet's unlettered status, prove its divine origin.

Core Idea
The Qur'an contains accurate historical accounts that an unlettered Prophet could not have known.

Baqillani presents a second aspect of the Qur'an's inimitability: its detailed narratives about ancient peoples and events. Since the Prophet Muhammad was unlettered and had no access to historical books or scholars, his accurate knowledge of these stories can only be explained by divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the argument
Notice that Baqillani emphasizes the difficulty of obtaining accurate historical knowledge without extensive study, and then states that the Prophet was unlettered and did not study books.
2
Understand the implication
The fact that the Prophet could accurately recount detailed stories of the past without any formal education in history is a miracle. It shows that the Qur'an is from Allah.
3
Reflect on the connection to i'jaz
This aspect of i'jaz is often overlooked but is a powerful proof, especially for those familiar with the oral traditions of the time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في وجوه الإعجاز
فإن قال قائل : فهل في القرآن وجه من وجوه الإعجاز غير ما ذكرتموه من بديع نظمه وعجيب رصفه وتأليفه ؟ قيل له : أجل، فيه وجهان آخران من وجوه الإعجاز.
أحدهما ما انطوى عليه من أخبار الغُيوب التي يعلم كل عاقل عَجْزَ الخلق عن معرفتها والتوصل إلى إدراكها نحو قوله : لتدخلن المسجد الحرام إن شاء الله آمنين محلقين رؤوسكم ومقصرين لا تخافون، فدخلوه كما وعدهم وأخبرهم ومن ذلك قوله تعالى : سيهزم الجمع ويولون الدبر فكان ذلك كما أخبر وقد وقوله : ليظهره على الدين كله ولو كره المشركون أظهره وأعلى دَعْوَتَه وأذل المُلوك المحاولة لأبطاله التي كانت حول صاحب الدعوة إليه وقوله تعالى : وعد الله الذين آمنوا منكم وعملوا الصالحات ليستخلفنهم في الأرض كما استخلف الذين من قبلهم . وكان من ذلك ما وعدهم الله واستخلف الأربعة الأئمة الخلفاء الراشدين .
وقوله لليهود : قل إن كانت لكم الدار الآخرة عند الله خالصة من دون الناس فتمنوا الموت إن كنتم صادقين ولن يتمنوه أبداً بما قدمت أيديهم فأخبر أنهم إن تمنوا الموت ماتوا وأنهم لن يتمنوه فلم يتمنوه على ما أخبر به علماً منهم بصدقه وأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا لا محالة .
وكذلك امتنع النصارى عن مباهلته عند دعائه لهم إليها ومطالبته بها في قوله تعالى : فقل تعالوا ندع ابناءنا وأبناءكم ونساءنا ونساءكم وأنفسنا وأنفسكم ثم نبتهل فنجعل لعنة الله على الكاذبين فامتنعوا عن المباهلة خوفاً من النكال وأليم العقاب وأن ما ينزل بهم توعدهم به ؛ وليس ذلك إلا لعلمهم بصدقه وثبوت نبوته ومن أخبار الغيوب قوله تعالى : الم غلبت الروم في أدنى الأرض وهم من بعد غلبهم سيغلبون ؛ فغلبت الرومُ فارس في بضع السنين كما أخبر نظائر هذا مما يكثر تتبعه واتفاق الصواب في هذا أجمع على سبيل التخمين والظن ممتنع متعذر فدل ذلك على أنه من أخبار علام الغيوب سبحانه
والوجه الآخر ما عليه القرآن من قصص الأولين وسير الماضين وأحاديث المتقدمين وذكر ما شَجَرَ بينهم وكان في أعصارهم مما لا يجوز حصول علمه إلا لمن كَثُر لقاؤه لأهل السِّير ودَرْسُه لها وعنايته بها ومجالسته لأهلها وكان ممن يتلو الكتب ويستخرجها مع العلم بأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يكن يتلو كتاباً ولا يَخُطُه بيمينه وأنه لم يكن ممن يُعْرَفُ بدراسة الكتب
A question concerning the aspects of inimitability. If a questioner says: Is there in the Qur'an an aspect of inimitability other than what you have mentioned of its marvelous composition (badīʿ naẓmihi), wondrous arrangement (ʿajīb raṣfihi) and structure (taʾlīfihi)? It is said to him: Yes, there are two other aspects of inimitability. One of them is what it contains of news of the unseen (akhbār al-ghuyūb) which every rational person knows is beyond the capacity of creation to know or attain. For example, His saying: 'You will enter the Sacred Mosque, if Allah wills, in safety, with your heads shaved and hair shortened, not fearing' — and they entered it just as He promised and informed them. And of that is His saying, exalted: 'The assembly will be defeated and they will turn their backs' — and it happened as He informed. And His saying: 'He will make it prevail over all religion, even if the polytheists dislike it' — He made it prevail and elevated His call and humiliated the kings who attempted to nullify it who were around the claimant of the message. And His saying, exalted: 'Allah has promised those among you who believe and do righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession on the earth just as He granted succession to those before them' — and of that was what Allah promised them, and He granted succession to the four rightly guided caliphs (al-khulafāʾ al-rāshidīn). And His saying to the Jews: 'Say: If the Final Abode with Allah is exclusively for you, excluding the people, then wish for death if you are truthful. But they will never wish for it, because of what their hands have sent forth' — He informed that if they wished for death they would die, and that they will never wish for it, so they did not wish for it, in accordance with what He informed, as they knew of his truthfulness, and that if they wished for death they would inevitably die. Likewise, the Christians refrained from invoking curses (mubāhala) when he called them to it and demanded it in His saying, exalted: 'Say: Come, let us call our sons and your sons, our women and your women, ourselves and yourselves, then invoke and lay the curse of Allah upon the liars' — so they refrained from the mubāhala for fear of punishment and painful torment, and that what he threatened them with would descend upon them; and that is only because of their knowledge of his truthfulness and the establishment of his prophethood. And among the news of the unseen is His saying, exalted: 'Alif Lam Mim. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, but they, after their defeat, will be victorious' — so the Romans defeated Persia within a few years, as He informed. The like of this is many to follow, and agreement of correctness in all of this by way of conjecture and guesswork is impossible and unattainable. This indicates that it is from the news of the Knower of the Unseen (ʿallām al-ghuyūb), exalted is He. The other aspect is what the Qur'an contains of stories of the ancients (qiṣaṣ al-awwalīn), biographies of the past, accounts of the predecessors, and mention of what occurred between them and was in their eras, knowledge of which is not attainable except for one who has frequently met the people of histories (sīra), studied them, took care with them, and sat with their people, and who was one who would read books and extract them — with the knowledge that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not read any book nor write it with his right hand, and he was not one known for studying books.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of two additional aspects of the Qur'an's inimitability (iʿjāz) beyond its linguistic composition. The author begins by acknowledging a potential question: are there other aspects of iʿjāz besides the marvelous arrangement? He answers affirmatively and enumerates two. The first aspect is predictions of the unseen (akhbār al-ghuyūb). These are events known only to God that the Prophet could not have known by natural means. Baqillani provides several examples: the promise that the companions would enter Mecca securely (fulfilled at the conquest); the prediction of defeat for the Meccan coalition at Badr (fulfilled); the prophecy that Islam would prevail over other religions (fulfilled historically); the promise of caliphate for the believers (fulfilled in the Rashidun caliphs); the challenge to the Jews to wish for death (they did not, confirming their own doubt); the avoidance of the Christians from the mubāhala (cursing) due to their fear of punishment; and the prophecy of the Romans' victory over Persia after their defeat (fulfilled within a few years). He argues that the consistent accuracy of these predictions, without any error, cannot be attributed to guesswork or coincidence, thus proving their source is the Knower of the Unseen. The second aspect is the Qur'an's detailed accounts of past nations and events—stories that require extensive study, old books, and oral tradition to know. Yet the Prophet Muhammad was unlettered (ummī), never having read or written any book, nor having studied with scholars of history. His accurate knowledge of such detailed stories, which he could not have acquired through normal means, is another proof of divine origin. This passage thus expands the concept of iʿjāz beyond the linguistic miracle to include prophetic foreknowledge and historical accuracy, both of which testify to the Qur'an's divine source.

Key Terms
قصص الأولين (qiṣaṣ al-awwalīn)
أمي (ummī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why is the Qur'an's inclusion of detailed historical accounts a miracle?
A) Because they are long and detailed
B) Because the Prophet was unlettered and could not have known them through normal means
C) Because they contain exact dates
D) Because they are written in rhyme

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate knowledge of past events, despite his illiteracy, is a clear sign that the Qur'an is from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were completely illiterate and had no access to historians or books, could you accurately describe events from a thousand years ago? What does the Prophet's ability to do so say about the source of his knowledge, and how does that affect your trust in the Qur'an?
?
The Prophet's illiteracy is often cited as a proof, but do you truly live as though the Qur'an is from Allah? What would change in your daily life if you fully internalized that the historical accounts are divine revelation?
?
Think of something you claim to know about the unseen or the past. Is it based on revelation, or on your own assumptions? How does this lesson challenge you to ground your knowledge in what Allah has revealed rather than in speculation?

Refuting the Objection: Universal Agreement on Moses' Signs
Baqillani refutes the objection that universal agreement validates only Moses' signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical refutation of the claim that universal agreement among different religions proves the authenticity of Moses' signs but not those of Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
Agreement alone is not proof—disagreement also exists.

In debates about prophethood, objectors often claim that the universal acceptance of Moses' miracles by Jews, Christians, and Muslims proves their authenticity, while Muhammad's miracles lack such consensus. Baqillani dismantles this objection by pointing out that many other religions also unanimously reject Moses' miracles. This lesson shows how Baqillani turns the argument against itself, demonstrating that agreement is not a decisive criterion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the objectors' claim that agreement of different religions on Moses' signs makes them certain, whereas Muhammad's signs lack such agreement.
The objectors list Jews, Christians, and Muslims as agreeing on Moses.
2
Identify Baqillani's initial counter
Baqillani first responds that the same reasoning applies to many of the Prophet's signs. Then he addresses the specific objection about Moses.
He points out that the objectors themselves are ignorant of the truth due to abandoning investigation.
3
Understand the symmetrical argument
Baqillani asks: if agreement to reject does not prove falsehood, then why should agreement to accept prove truth? He lists groups that deny Moses' signs (Brahmins, Magians, philosophers, materialists).
This is the core logical move: the same principle can be used against the objectors.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this refutation is effective. It shows that the objectors' criterion is not decisive because it leads to contradictory conclusions.
This lesson highlights the importance of consistent reasoning in theological arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك جَهِلَ الحقِّ فيما نقلوه قيل لهم مِثْلُ ذلك في العلم بصحة كثير من أعلام النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأنها معلومة بمثل هذا الاستدلال وأنهم إنما جَهلوا لتركهم النظر فيما يدل على صحته . فإن قالوا : إنما وجب صحة نقل أعلام موسى والانقياد له لإطباق أهل الأديان المختلفة عليه كاليهود والنصارى والمسلمين وهذه العلة مفقودة مِنْ خَبَرِكم ، قيل لهم : لِمَ وَجَبَ ذلك دون أن يجب بطلانــه وتكذيبـه لاجتماع أهل الأديان المختلفة على تكذيبه ورده كالبراهمة والمجوس والفلاسفة وضروب الدهرية؟ فإن كان إطباق المختلفين في دياناتهم على تكذيب المُخبِرِ لا يدل على كذبه فما أنكرتم أن يكون إطباق المختلفين في دياناتهم على تصديق المخبرين لا يدل على صدقهم؟
That is ignorance of the truth regarding what they transmitted. It was said to them: The same applies to knowledge of the validity of many of the signs of the Prophet (peace be upon him) – that they are known by such reasoning, and that they only ignored it because they abandoned investigating what indicates its correctness. If they say: The correctness of the transmission of Moses' signs and submission to it is necessary due to the agreement of the people of different religions upon it, like the Jews, Christians, and Muslims, and this condition is lacking in your account. It is said to them: Why is that necessary, without it being necessary to declare it false and reject it due to the agreement of the people of different religions upon its denial and rejection, like the Brahmins, Magians, philosophers, and types of materialists? If the agreement of those differing in their religions upon denying a reporter does not indicate his falsehood, then what prevents you from [admitting] that the agreement of those differing in their religions upon affirming reporters does not indicate their truthfulness?
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection and Baqillani's response. The objectors claim that the widespread agreement of Jews, Christians, and Muslims on Moses' miracles is proof of their authenticity, whereas Muhammad's miracles lack such universal agreement. Baqillani counters by pointing out that the same argument can be turned around: many religions also agree in rejecting Moses' miracles (Brahmins, Magians, philosophers, etc.). If agreement to reject does not prove falsehood, then agreement to accept does not prove truth either. Thus the objection is invalid because it assumes a principle that can be used against itself.

Key Terms

إطباق
استدلال
براهمة
مجوس
فلاسفة
دهريّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the agreement of different religions on a prophet's miracles is an absolute proof of authenticity.
Correction: Baqillani shows that because other religions also agree in rejecting those same miracles, agreement cannot be conclusive proof.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why is the agreement of different religions on Moses' miracles not a decisive proof?
A) Because Jews and Christians are biased
B) Because many other religions also reject those miracles
C) Because Muslims do not agree
D) Because Moses' miracles are not well-attested

Key Takeaway
Agreement among some religions does not constitute definitive proof because other religions disagree, so the criterion is inconsistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief about your faith simply because it was popular or widely held, without investigating its evidence? Would you be willing to re-examine it today, even if it feels uncomfortable?
?
Baqillani exposes the inconsistency of applying a standard only when it supports your view. In your own life, when have you used a double standard to judge others' actions or beliefs compared to your own? What will you do to correct this?
?
The objectors ignored evidence for Muhammad's signs because they failed to investigate. Is there an area of your religious practice where you have deliberately avoided deeper inquiry out of fear or laziness? What is one concrete step you can take this week to seek the truth there?

Second Objection: Independence of Witnesses Refuted
Baqillani refutes the objection of non-independence via a parallel argument and a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the objection that Muslims and 'Isawiyya are not independent witnesses by turning the argument and presenting a dilemma.

Core Idea
An objection that proves too much destroys itself.

Baqillani now addresses a second objection: that the agreement between Muslims and the 'Isawiyya (a Jewish sect) does not constitute independent witness because the 'Isawiyya took their knowledge from Muslims. If this objection were accepted, it would also undermine the objectors' own transmission of Mosaic miracles. Baqillani shows the consistency of his method and places the burden back on the objectors.

Guided Path
1
Read passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the objection and response.
2
Identify the objectors' claim
The objectors argue that Muslims and 'Isawiyya are not independent witnesses because the 'Isawiyya learned from Muslims, making them one group.
Notice the key term 'عيسوية'.
3
See Baqillani's counter-argument
Baqillani applies the same logic to Moses: Muslims and Christians learned from Jews, so by the same reasoning their transmission would be invalid. This shows the objection is self-defeating.
4
Appreciate the dilemma
Baqillani then forces a choice: either accept the consistency of the argument (and thus accept Jesus' miracles) or abandon their objection. Either way, their position fails.
This is a powerful rhetorical move.
5
Reflect on the method
This passage demonstrates how logical consistency is key in theological debate. Baqillani does not simply deny the objection but shows it leads to absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : فما أنكرتم من وجوب ثبوت خَبَرِ المسلمين وصِدْقِهم لإطباقهم وإطباق العيسوية منكم على تصديقهم وهم أهل دينين مُخْتَلِفين ومِلَّتين مُتباينتين؟ فإن قالوا : العيوسية إنما أخذوا نقل أعلام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم عنكم وأنتم في الأصـل فـرقـة واحدة قيل لهم : وكذلك المسلمون والنصارى إنما أخذوا نقل أعلام موسى عليه السلام عن أسلافكم وعنكم وأنتم في الأصل فرقة واحدة فلا تجب الحجة بنقلكم ثم يقال لهم : فيجب على موضوع اعتلالكم تصحيح آيات المسيح عليه السلام لإطباقنا والنصارى والعيسوية على صحتها فإن أجابوا إلى ذلك تركوا دينهم وإن أبوه تركوا اعتلالهم .
Then it is said to them: What prevents you from acknowledging the necessity of the truth of the Muslims' report and their truthfulness, due to their agreement and the agreement of the 'Isawiyya among you upon affirming them, while they are people of two different religions and two divergent creeds? If they say: The 'Isawiyya only took the transmission of Muhammad's signs (peace be upon him) from you, and you are originally one group. It is said to them: Similarly, the Muslims and Christians only took the transmission of Moses' signs (peace be upon him) from your ancestors and from you, and you are originally one group. So the proof is not established by your transmission. Then it is said to them: Based on the premise of your argument, it is necessary to affirm the miracles of Jesus (peace be upon him) due to our agreement, the Christians, and the 'Isawiyya upon their authenticity. If they accept that, they abandon their religion; if they reject it, they abandon their argument.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage contains a second objection and its rebuttal. The objectors argue that the agreement between Muslims and the 'Isawiyya (a Jewish sect that accepted Muhammad) is not valid because the 'Isawiyya learned from Muslims, so they are not independent. Baqillani turns this back on them: similarly, Muslims and Christians learned about Moses from Jews, so their agreement is not independent either. Therefore, the objection fails. Furthermore, Baqillani points out that applying the objectors' own principle would force them to accept Jesus' miracles, since Muslims, Christians, and 'Isawiyya all agree on them. This is a dilemma for the objectors.

Key Terms
عيسوية
أعلام
نقل
حجة
اعتلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An agreement among groups that share a common source is always invalid as proof.
Correction: Baqillani shows that if that were true, it would also undermine the objectors' own claims, so the objection cannot be applied selectively without absurd consequences.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's response to the claim that Muslims and 'Isawiyya are not independent witnesses?
A) He denies that they are one group
B) He argues that the same applies to Jews and Christians regarding Moses
C) He says the 'Isawiyya are actually a different religion
D) He accepts the objection and provides a different proof

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the objection by demonstrating that it proves too much, thus preserving the validity of independent witness through agreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever applied a standard to others that you would not accept for yourself? How does Baqillani's exposure of the objectors' inconsistency challenge you to examine your own double standards?
?
When you present an argument for Islam, are you prepared for it to be turned back on you? What would it take for you to respond with humility and seek truth rather than defend your position at all costs?
?
The objectors faced a dilemma: accept a truth that overturns their religion, or reject their own reasoning. Is there a truth in your life — from this lesson or elsewhere — that you have been avoiding because it would require you to change deeply? What is one step you can take today to face it?

Distinguishing Transmission from Interpretation
Baqillani refutes the claim that Christian irrational beliefs invalidate their transmission of Jesus' miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that a community's erroneous theological interpretation does not necessarily corrupt the reliability of their historical transmission of factual events.

Core Idea
Factual reports survive flawed interpretations.

When opponents argue that a group's false beliefs discredit all their reports, Baqillani offers a precise rebuttal. He separates the core historical transmission from the later theological construction. This lesson examines that distinction and shows why factual reports can remain trustworthy even when interpretations go wrong.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Notice the objection: Christians added the irrational Trinity to Jesus' miracles, so their transmission is unreliable. Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the claim.
The objection assumes that adding an interpretation invalidates the entire report.
2
Identify Baqillani's key distinction
Baqillani separates the transmitted events (miracles) from the interpretations (Trinity). He says Christians did not transmit the Trinity as a report; they deduced it themselves. This distinction is crucial.
The Trinity is not part of the original narration; it is a later theological inference.
3
Apply the principle
Reflect: if someone misinterprets a story, does that make the story false? Baqillani says no. The transmission of the miracle facts remains sound. This principle has broad applications in evaluating historical reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا قد ضَمَّت النصارى إلى نقلهم أعلام المسيح ما تحيله العقولُ من التثليث قيل لهم : إن النصارى لم تنقل التثليث فَيَفْسُدُ نقلها، وإنما تأولته واستدلت عليه عند أنفسها وضَرَبَت للحلول والاتحاد والأقانيم والجوهر الأمثال وغَلِطَت وأخطأت في اجتهادها وتأويلها وذلك لا يوجب غلطها في نقلها أنّ المسيح أبرأ الأكمه والأبرص ومشى على الماء ونحو ذلك فبطل ما قلتم .
If they say: The Christians have added to their transmission of Jesus' signs what the intellect deems impossible, namely the Trinity. It is said to them: The Christians did not transmit the Trinity such that their transmission becomes corrupt; rather, they interpreted it and deduced it among themselves, and they struck examples for incarnation, union, hypostases, and substance, and they erred and made mistakes in their ijtihad and interpretation. That does not necessitate error in their transmission that Jesus healed the blind and the leper, walked on water, and the like. Thus what you said is invalid.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage deals with an objection that Christians have added the irrational doctrine of the Trinity to the reports of Jesus' miracles, thus making their entire transmission unreliable. Baqillani distinguishes between the transmitted facts (Jesus' miracles) and the theological interpretations (Trinity) that Christians later built upon those facts. The transmission of the miracles themselves is separate from the interpretation; the Christians did not claim that the Trinity was part of the original report. Therefore, their error in interpretation does not invalidate the accuracy of the transmitted events. The objection is thus refuted.

Key Terms
تثليث
تأويل
حلول
اتحاد
أقانيم
جوهر
أكمه
أبرص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a community holds false beliefs, all their historical reports are automatically false.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that factual reports can be reliable even if interpretations based on them are erroneous. The transmission of events is separate from theological construction.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani defend the Christian transmission of Jesus' miracles against the objection that they added the Trinity?
A) He says the Trinity is not irrational
B) He argues that the Trinity was not transmitted as part of the miracle reports
C) He denies that Christians believe in the Trinity
D) He accepts that the transmission is corrupted

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that a community's erroneous theological interpretation does not necessarily corrupt the reliability of their historical transmission of factual events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a factual report from someone whose theology you reject, do you immediately dismiss it? This lesson calls you to separate the fact from the interpretation. Will you now pause and examine each report on its own merit?
?
Think of a time you confused someone's correct transmission with their flawed interpretation. How might that have led you to discard truth? Commit to distinguishing the two from now on.
?
Is there a group or individual whose beliefs you despise so much that you reject everything they say? If so, ask yourself: have I let my dislike of their interpretation blind me to facts they might accurately transmit? Will you change that starting today?
