Jews' Irrational Beliefs Undermine Their Transmission of Moses' Signs
Baqillani argues that Jewish anthropomorphic beliefs render their transmission of Moses' signs unreliable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the principle of transmission reliability to argue that Jewish anthropomorphic beliefs invalidate their reporting of Moses' miracles.

Core Idea
If adding absurdities invalidates transmission, then Jewish anthropomorphism undermines their own claims.

This lesson continues Baqillani's rebuttal of Jewish objections to Christian miracles. Having established that Jesus' miracles are transmitted through multiple reliable chains, he now turns the tables: if the Jews insist that Christian beliefs are irrational and thus their transmission must be false, then by the same logic, their own transmission of Moses' miracles is even more suspect because they have added crass anthropomorphic descriptions of God.

Guided Path
1
Understanding the establishment of Jesus' miracles
Notice how Baqillani assembles three independent transmission sources: Muslims, the 'Isawiyya, and even the Ariusiyya. This shows the reliability of Jesus' miracles.
The Ariusiyya are a Christian sect that denied Christ's divinity but still affirmed his miracles.
2
The argument against Jewish transmission
Baqillani then applies the same criterion to Jewish transmission: since they have added irrational anthropomorphic beliefs, their transmission should be rejected.
3
Examining the specific anthropomorphic claims
Baqillani lists several examples: God as a body with human features, regret over the Flood, etc. Reflect on how these are even more absurd than Christian Trinity.
4
The larger point
This argument is a powerful counter: it shows that the objection against Christianity boomerangs back on Judaism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : فيجب تصحيح أعلام المسيح صلى الله عليه وعلى نبينا وسلم بنقلنا ونقل العيسوية ونقل الموحدة النصارى من رؤوس الأروسية الذين يقولون إن عيسى ابنُ الله على جهة الاختصاص والإكرام ولا يجدون لذلك مَدْفَعاً . ثم يقال لهم : فيجب أيضاً أن يكون نقل اليهود لأعلام موسى كذباً باطلاً لأنهم قد ضموا إلى نقل ذلك ما تُحيله العقول من قولهم بالتشبيه والتجسيم وأن الله تعالى جسم ذو صورة ومتناه محدود أبيض الرأس واللحية وأنه مهموم محزون بما عليه العِبَادُ من الظلم والفساد في الأرض وأنه تعالى عن قولهم نَدِمَ على الطوفان وتغريق العالم وقال : لن أعود إلى إغراق الأرض أبداً وتخطوا في الجهل إلى حدّ لن تبلغه النصارى في التثليث والاتحاد.
And it is said to them: It is necessary to affirm the miracles of Jesus (peace be upon him and upon our Prophet) by our transmission, the transmission of the 'Isawiyya, and the transmission of the monotheistic Christians from the leaders of the Ariusiyya, who say that Jesus is the son of God by way of special distinction and honor, and they find no escape from that. Then it is said to them: It is also necessary that the transmission of the Jews of Moses' signs be false and invalid, because they have added to that transmission what the intellect deems impossible, from their statements of anthropomorphism and corporealism, and that God is a body with form, finite, limited, white-headed and white-bearded, and that He is worried and grieved by the injustice and corruption of His servants on earth, and that He (exalted above their statements) regretted the Flood and the drowning of the world and said: 'I will never again flood the earth,' and they exceeded in ignorance to a level that the Christians did not reach in the Trinity and union.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage contains two further arguments. First, Baqillani asserts that the miracles of Jesus are firmly established through multiple independent transmissions: Muslims, 'Isawiyya, and even the Ariusiyya (a Christian sect that denied Christ's divinity but still affirmed his miracles). Second, he turns the objection back on the Jews: if adding irrational beliefs invalidates transmission, then the Jewish transmission of Moses' miracles is even more suspect because they have added gross anthropomorphic descriptions of God — describing God as a body with human features, regretting the Flood, etc. These beliefs are far more absurd than the Christian Trinity, so by the objectors' own criterion, the Jewish transmission should be rejected. This is a powerful counter-argument.

Correction: Baqillani shows that Jews have added even more egregious anthropomorphisms, such as describing God as a white-bearded body who regrets the Flood, making their transmission even more suspect.

Baqillani turns the objection back on the Jews: if irrational beliefs invalidate transmission, then Jewish transmission of Moses' miracles is invalid due to their anthropomorphic doctrines.

?

In your own life, have you allowed one irrational or unexamined assumption to undermine your credibility in matters of faith? What would it cost you to repent of that and align your beliefs with sound intellect and revelation?
?
The Christians in this passage are praised for holding to the miracles of Jesus despite their flawed Christology. Are you willing to affirm what is true even when it comes from unexpected sources? Or do you dismiss truth because of the imperfections of those who carry it?

Trinity Does Not Corrupt Christian Miracle Reports
Baqillani answers the objection that Christians' addition of Trinity corrupts their transmission of Jesus' miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that a group's theological errors do not automatically invalidate their factual reports, using the example of Christian transmission of Jesus' miracles.

Core Idea
Theological error does not corrupt factual reporting.

How can we accept miracles reported by a community whose beliefs include what reason deems impossible? This is the objection Baqillani addresses. He draws a crucial distinction between transmitted facts and interpretive doctrines, showing that the two are separate. Read on to see how he defends the reliability of Christian miracle accounts despite their Trinitarian theology.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first line of the passage to grasp what the objectors claim: Christians added the Trinity (a rationally impossible doctrine) to their reports, thus corrupting all their transmissions.
2
Baqillani's first answer: distinction between transmission and interpretation
Notice how Baqillani separates the act of transmitting a report from the act of interpreting doctrine. Christians did not transmit the Trinity as a report; they derived it through personal reasoning. Therefore, their theological error does not affect their factual reports of miracles.
This is the key logical move.
3
Baqillani's second answer: multiple independent witnesses
Observe that Baqillani further argues that the miracles of Jesus are attested not only by Muslims but also by other Christian groups (like the 'Isawiyya and Arians) who differ on doctrine. This multiplicity of witnesses strengthens the case.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why this refutation is effective: the objectors cannot logically reject the miracles without also rejecting their own sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا قد ضَمَّت النصارى إلى نقلهم أعلام المسيح ما تحيله العقول من التثليث قيل لهم : إن النصارى لم تنقل التثليث فَيَفْسُدُ نقلها، وإنما تأولته واستدلت عليه عند أنفسها وضَرَبَت للحلول والاتحاد والأقانيم والجوهر الأمثال وغَلِطَت وأخطأت في اجتهادها وتأويلها وذلك لا يوجب غلطها في نقلها أنّ المسيح أبرأ الأكمه والأبرص ومشى على الماء ونحو ذلك فبطل ما قلتم . ويقال لهم : فيجب تصحيح أعلام المسيح صلى الله عليه وعلى نبينا وسلم بنقلنا ونقل العيسوية ونقل الموحدة النصارى من رؤوس الأروسية الذين يقولون إن عيسى ابنُ الله على جهة الاختصاص والإكرام ولا يجدون لذلك مَدْفَعاً .
If they say: 'The Christians have added to their transmission of the signs of the Christ what minds deem impossible, namely the Trinity,' it is said to them: The Christians did not transmit the Trinity such that their transmission would be corrupted. Rather, they interpreted it and inferred it among themselves, and they coined parables for indwelling, union, hypostases, and substance, and they erred and made mistakes in their ijtihad and interpretation. But that does not necessitate their error in their transmission that the Christ healed the blind and leprous, walked on water, and the like. So what you said is invalid. And it is said to them: It is necessary to affirm the signs of the Christ (peace be upon him and upon our Prophet) through our transmission, the transmission of the 'Isawiyya, and the transmission of the monotheist Christians from the heads of the Arians, who say that Jesus is the son of God by way of special distinction and honor, and they have no way to refute that.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection against the reliability of Christian transmission of Jesus' miracles. The objectors argue that because Christians add the Trinity (which reason deems impossible) to their transmitted reports, their entire transmission is corrupted. Baqillani replies in two parts. First, he clarifies that Christians did not transmit the Trinity as a matter of report (naql); rather, they derived it through personal interpretation (ta'wil) and reasoning. Therefore, their error in theology does not entail error in their factual reporting of observable miracles. The transmission of Jesus healing the blind and leprous, walking on water, etc., remains sound. Second, he argues that the opponents must accept the transmission of Jesus' miracles not only from Muslims but also from the 'Isawiyya (a group of Christians) and from the monotheist Christians (al-muwahhida), specifically the Arians who affirm Jesus as Son of God by honor but not as a literal begetting. Since these groups agree on the miracles, there is no escape from admitting their authenticity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any error in religious doctrine automatically invalidates all reports from that group.
Correction: Baqillani distinguishes between transmitted facts (which can be sound) and interpretive doctrines (which may be erroneous). Error in the latter does not necessarily corrupt the former.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that doctrinal errors do not automatically undermine factual reports, and multiple independent witnesses can confirm the truth of miraculous events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Baqillani uses the testimony of Christians (Arians, 'Isawiyya) to confirm miracles. Who in your life holds beliefs you consider mistaken, yet has spoken truth to you? How will you honor that truth without compromising your own faith?

When you hear a factual report from a non-Muslim or someone you disagree with, do you immediately doubt it? This lesson demands we separate the factual from the interpretive. Where in your life are you conflating the two?

Symmetry in Testimony: Jewish Anthropomorphism and Christian Trinity
Baqillani parallels Jewish anthropomorphism with Christian trinitarianism to neutralize the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a symmetrical argument to defend the reliability of transmitted miracles despite doctrinal errors in the transmitting community.

Core Idea
Doctrinal errors do not automatically nullify historical testimony.

Baqillani extends the earlier argument about Christian Trinity to the Jewish case. He shows that if we reject Christian transmission because of their erroneous beliefs, we must also reject Jewish transmission because of their anthropomorphism—leading to a contradiction. This lesson explores his clever use of symmetry to defend the principle that testimony of miracles can remain valid despite theological errors in the transmitters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the structure: an initial claim, then two back-and-forth responses.
2
Identify the opponent's position
Understand that the opponent argued that Christian belief in the Trinity corrupts their transmission of Jesus' miracles. Baqillani applies the same logic to Jews and their anthropomorphic beliefs.
3
Follow the symmetrical rebuttal
Notice how Baqillani counters each possible response from the opponent by drawing a parallel between Jews and Christians.
The argument leads to a stalemate, which is the intended effect.
4
Analyze the final conclusion
The opponent is left with no answer ('ولا جواب عن ذلك'), showing that the original objection is self-defeating if applied consistently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : فيجب أيضاً أن يكون نقل اليهود لأعلام موسى كذباً باطلاً لأنهم قد ضموا إلى نقل ذلك ما تُحيله العقول من قولهم بالتشبيه والتجسيم وأن الله تعالى جسم ذو صورة ومتناه محدود أبيض الرأس واللحية وأنه مهموم محزون بما عليه العباد من الظلم والفساد في الأرض وأنه تعالى عن قولهم ندم على الطوفان وتغريق العالم وقال : لن أعود إلى إغراق الأرض أبداً وتخطوا في الجهل إلى حد لن تبلغه النصارى في التثليث والاتحاد . وإن قالوا ليس كل اليهود يقولون ذلك، قيل لهم : ولا كل النصارى يقولون بالتثليث وإثبات النبوة على حد ما تذهب إليه الملكية واليعاقبة والنسطورية ونحن إنما نحتج بقول الموحدة منهم . فإن قالوا ليس في النصارى إلا قائل بالتثليث الذي تحيله العقول قيل لهم : ولا في اليهود إلا قائل بالتشبيه والتجسيم الذي تحيله العقول؛ ولا جواب عن ذلك .
Then it is said to them: Likewise, it would be necessary that the transmission of the Jews of the signs of Moses be false and invalid, because they have added to the transmission of that what minds deem impossible from their statements of anthropomorphism and corporealism, and that God Almighty is a body with a form, finite, limited, white of head and beard, and that He is worried and grieved by what the servants are upon of injustice and corruption on earth, and that He—exalted be He above their words—regretted the flood and the drowning of the world and said: I will never return to drowning the earth ever, and they exceeded in ignorance to a limit that the Christians did not reach in the Trinity and union. And if they say: Not all Jews say that, it is said to them: Nor do all Christians say the Trinity and affirmation of prophethood in the way the Melkites, Jacobites, and Nestorians go. We only argue with the statement of the monotheists among them. Then if they say: There is none among the Christians except a proponent of the Trinity that minds deem impossible, it is said to them: Nor among the Jews except a proponent of anthropomorphism and corporealism that minds deem impossible; and there is no answer for that.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage extends the previous argument to the Jewish case and results in a symmetrical rebuttal. First, Baqillani presents the objection: if Christian addition of Trinity were to corrupt their transmission, then by the same logic, Jewish addition of anthropomorphism (tashbih and tajsim) should corrupt their transmission of Moses' miracles. He lists extreme anthropomorphic statements attributed to some Jews, such as God having a body, being finite, with white hair, regretting the flood, etc. Then he presents the opponent's possible escape: 'Not all Jews say that.' Baqillani counters that similarly, not all Christians affirm the Trinity in the way the major sects (Melkites, Jacobites, Nestorians) do; the Muslims argue based on the monotheist Christians (like Arians) who deny the Trinity. Then the opponent may insist that all Christians affirm the rationally impossible Trinity. Baqillani retorts that then all Jews also affirm the rationally impossible anthropomorphism, leaving the opponent with no answer. The argument reaches a stalemate, showing the objection to be self-defeating.

Key Terms

النسطورية

الموحدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a religious community holds erroneous beliefs about God, their historical reports about miracles are completely unreliable.
Correction: Baqillani shows that this reasoning is inconsistent. It would force us to reject Jewish transmission of Moses' miracles as well, but that conclusion is unacceptable because the miracles of Moses are accepted by all Muslims. Therefore, doctrinal error alone does not invalidate testimony.

Checkpoint

B) He says that not all Christians believe in the Trinity.
C) He says that all Jews believe in anthropomorphism, so the opponent cannot escape.
D) He concedes the argument and moves to a different point.

Key Takeaway
Doctrinal errors in a transmitting community do not automatically nullify the historical reliability of the miracles they report, as shown by the symmetrical argument between Jews and Christians.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Baqillani forces the opponent into a stalemate. Are there issues in your faith where you rely on arguments that could be turned against you if applied consistently? How can you strengthen your reasoning to avoid such traps?

Refuting the Fabrication Claim
Baqillani refutes the claim that Muslims fabricated Muhammad's miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani counters the objection that Muslims fabricated Muhammad's miracles by appealing to consistency in transmission criteria.

Core Idea
The same method validating Moses' miracles also validates Muhammad's.

In defending prophethood, Baqillani anticipates a common objection: that Muslims simply invented Muhammad's miracles. His response is not to prove the miracles again, but to show the inconsistency in the objector's position. This passage presents a logical refutation based on shared criteria for accepting miracle reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: an objection followed by a direct response.
The objector claims Muslims lied about Muhammad's miracles.
2
Identify the structure
Recognize that this is an objection-and-answer format. The answer uses a tu quoque argument and a consistency argument.
Baqillani first turns the accusation back on the objector, then argues that the same method proves both.
3
Analyze the logical move
Understand that Baqillani is not re-proving the miracles; he is arguing that if the objector accepts Moses' miracles via transmission, then by the same or stronger criteria they must accept Muhammad's.
This is a powerful refutation because it uses the opponent's own standard.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider why this argument is effective: it does not require proving new evidence, only pointing out inconsistency.
The argument relies on the principle of consistent criteria for accepting reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال منهم قائل: قد كذب المسلمون في نقل أعلام محمد عليه السلام. قيل لهم: وقد كذبت اليهود والنصارى أيضاً في نقل أعلام، وكذبت نقلة الأمصار، وكل طريق تثبتون به أعلام موسى فيه، وبما هو أقوى منه تثبت أعلام محمد صلى الله عليه، وقد بينا ذلك فيما سلف بما يغني عن رده.
If one of them says: the Muslims have lied in transmitting the miracles of Muhammad, peace be upon him. It is said to them: the Jews and Christians have also lied in transmitting miracles, and the transmitters of the cities have lied. And every path by which you establish the miracles of Moses, by it and by what is stronger than it, the miracles of Muhammad are established, and we have clarified that previously in what suffices from repeating it.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector claims that Muslims fabricated the miracles (أعلام) of Muhammad. The answer is a tu quoque argument: if Muslims are liars, then Jews and Christians are also liars in their transmission of Moses' miracles, as are all transmitters of reports from distant cities. Moreover, the very method (طريق) by which Jews establish the miracles of Moses is the same method, or even stronger, for establishing the miracles of Muhammad. Baqillani refers to earlier discussions where this was already sufficiently demonstrated.

Key Terms
تكذيب
نقل
أعلام
طريق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection that Muslims fabricated Muhammad's miracles is a valid critique because it challenges the reliability of Islamic transmission.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the same transmission criteria apply to both Moses and Muhammad, so accepting one and rejecting the other is inconsistent.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani's answer, why can't the Jewish objector claim that Muslims fabricated Muhammad's miracles?
A) Because Muhammad's miracles were witnessed by many people.
B) Because the same criteria used for Moses' miracles also prove Muhammad's, and even more strongly.
C) Because the Quran is in Arabic and cannot be fabricated.
D) Because Jews also believe in Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani argues that the same criteria used to accept Moses' miracles also prove Muhammad's miracles, making the objection of fabrication self-defeating.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear modern accusations that the Prophet's miracles are fabrications, do you feel the same confidence in their truth as you do in historical facts like the life of Moses? If there is any disparity in your certainty, what does that reveal about the strength of your faith in the transmission of Islam? Will you commit to studying the chains of narration for at least one major miracle to remove that doubt?
?
Baqillani argues that the very method by which Jews accept Moses' miracles is also how Muslims accept Muhammad's miracles—and even more strongly. Have you ever examined the evidence for Moses' miracles versus Muhammad's with an open, critical mind? If you have not, why do you assume one is true and the other is not? Are you willing to spend this week comparing the scholarly arguments for the transmission of the splitting of the sea and the splitting of the moon, so that your faith is grounded in knowledge, not blind imitation?
?
The objection that 'Muslims fabricated' is an attack on the honesty of the entire Muslim community. How does your heart respond when you hear such an accusation? Do you react defensively or do you feel the weight of responsibility to know and convey the truth? If someone asked you today for proof that the Prophet's miracles are true, could you provide a coherent argument from transmission—or would you rely solely on emotion? What will you change starting today to be ready for that question?

Refuting the Qadariyya on Jesus Creating Birds
Baqillani refutes the Qadariyya interpretation of Jesus creating birds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani interprets the word 'khalq' in the verse about Jesus and the birds to refute the Qadariyya claim that humans can create their own actions.

Core Idea
The word 'khalq' can mean estimation and shaping, not only creation from nothing.

The Qadariyya use the verse where Jesus creates birds from clay as proof that humans can create. Baqillani responds by showing that 'khalq' in this context refers to Jesus' estimation and manual shaping, while God creates the actual formation. This distinction preserves divine sovereignty over creation. Let's examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the Qadariyya interpretation
First, consider the verse and how the Qadariyya understood it as proof of human creation. Notice the author's response.
2
Understand the dual meaning of 'khalq'
The author explains that 'khalq' can mean mental estimation (taqdir) and manual shaping (taswir). Identify these two meanings in the passage.
3
See the conclusion
Baqillani affirms Jesus' actions but clarifies that God creates the actual event. This refutes the Qadariyya proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استدلوا بقوله عز وجل: (وإذ تخلق من الطين كهيئة الطير بإذني) فالمراد بذلك: إنك تُقدر بقلبك وتصور بيدك. والخلق يكون بمعنى تقدير القلب وفكرته ويكون معناه تصوير اليد وحركاتها واعتماداتها التي يخلق الله عنده اجتماع المصدورات من الأجسام. ونحن لا ننكر أن يكون عيسى عليه السلام مفكراً بقلبه ومحركاً ليده وجوارحه حركات وفكراً يخلق الله عنده اجتماع المصدورات من الأجسام.
And if they adduce His saying, Mighty and Majestic: 'And when you create from clay as the form of a bird with My permission' (wa idh takhluqu min at-tini kahay'ati at-tayri bi-idhni), the intended meaning of that is: You estimate with your heart and shape with your hand. And 'khalq' can mean the estimation of the heart and its thought, and its meaning is the shaping of the hand and its movements and pressures by which God creates the coming together of shaped bits of bodies. And we do not deny that Jesus, peace be upon him, was thinking with his heart and moving his hand and limbs with movements and thought by which God creates the coming together of shaped bits of bodies.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage refutes a second Qadariyya proof: the verse about Jesus creating birds from clay (Quran 5:110). The Qadariyya argue that Jesus 'created' the birds, implying that humans can create. The author explains that 'takhluq' here means estimation (taqdir) and shaping (taswir), not creating ex nihilo. He clarifies that the word 'khalq' can refer to mental estimation and manual shaping. The author affirms that Jesus indeed moved his hands and thought, but it was God who actually created the coming together of the shaped pieces. Thus, the verse does not prove that humans create their own actions in a metaphysical sense; rather, Jesus merely performed actions that were the occasion for God's creation.

Key Terms
خلق
تقدير
تصوير
عيسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the word 'khalq' always means creating from nothing, and that Jesus created the birds independently.
Correction: Baqillani shows that 'khalq' can mean estimation and shaping, and that God is the true creator of the event.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the word 'takhluq' mean in the verse about Jesus and the birds?
A) Creating from nothing.
B) Estimation and shaping.
C) Bringing to life.
D) Deceiving.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Qadariyya by showing that 'khalq' in the verse about Jesus creating birds means estimation and shaping, not absolute creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something through your own planning and effort, do you genuinely believe it was God who created the outcome, or do you secretly feel it was your own doing? How does this lesson challenge that feeling?
?
Jesus, a prophet, only shaped the clay; God turned it into a bird. What 'clay' are you shaping today in your life (your work, relationships, or worship) that you need to remember is only a means, while God is the true Creator? Will you actively remind yourself of this today?
?
The Qadariyya thought they could create, but they were wrong. Are there areas in your life where you act as if you are the ultimate cause—perhaps in your career, your health, or your spirituality? What would it practically mean to hand that over to God and ask Him to create good for you?
